رحمہ اللہ کے نزدیک فرض نماز میں صرف ایک رکعت میں قرات واجب ہے، کیونکہ قرآن کریم میں اللہ تعالی ارشاد فرماتے ہیں: فَاقْرَؤُوا مَا تَيَسَّرَ مِنَ الْقُرآن . (المزمل: ۲۰) قرآن میں جو آسان لگے اسی کو نماز میں پڑھو۔ لہذا اس آیت میں فَاقْرَؤُوا امر ہے اور امر تکرار کا تقاضا نہیں کرتا ہے، تو مذکورہ اصول کی بنیاد پر حسن بصری رحمہ اللہ فرماتے ہیں کہ صرف ایک رکعت میں قراءت واجب ہے۔ ائمہ احناف اس کے جواب میں کہتے ہیں کہ ہم بھی اس اصول کو تسلیم کرتے ہیں کہ امر تکرار نہیں چاہتا تو اس کی بنیاد پر صرف ایک ہی رکعت میں قرات واجب ہے لیکن دوسری رکعت میں ہم جو وجوب قرات کے قائل ہیں وہ اس وجہ سے کہ دوسری رکعت چونکہ پہلی رکعت کے ساتھ من کل الوجوہ مشابہ ہے، تو اسی مشابہت کی بنیاد پر ہم نے کہا کہ دوسری رکعت میں بھی قراءت واجب ہے۔ پس پہلی رکعت میں قراءت عبارت النص سے ثابت ہے اور دوسری رکعت میں دلالت النص سے ثابت ہے۔ ولنا قَوْله تَعَالَى: فَاقْرَءُوا مَا تَيَسَّرَ مِنْهُ) والأمر بالفعل لا يقتضي التكرار) تقديره أن الله تعالى أمرنا بالقراءة مما تيسر من القرآن وذلك فى الصلاة بالإجماع والأمر بالفعل يقتضى امتثاله، ولا يقتضي التكرار إعادة الشيء بعينه لا إعادة مثل الشيء فاقتضى ذلك أن تكرن القراءة في ركعة واحدة كما ذهب إليه الحسن البصرى. وإنما أوجبنا في الثانية) أى إنما أوجبنا القراءة في الركعة الثانية، وهذا جواب عما يقال إنكم قلتم إن الأمر بالفعل لا يقتضى التكرار، وقد أوجبتم القراءة فى الركعة الثانية وخالفتم ما قلتم وتقرير الجواب أن وجوب القراءة في الثانية لا بعبارة النص حتى يلزم ما قلتم وإنما وجوبها في الثانية بدلالة النص وهو معنى قوله (استدلالا) بالأولى يعنى بالركعة الأولى وبين ذلك بقوله : (لأنهما يتشاكلان من كل وجه أى لأن البركعة الأولى والثانية تتشابهان من كل وجه، فلما كان كذلك وجبت في الثانية استدلالا بالأولى كالحكم في أحد النوعين ينسب في النوع الآخر، وأما تشاكل الثانية للأولى من كل وجه فمن حيث السقوط والوجوب والصفة والقدر فكل من وجبت عليه الأولى وجبت الثانية، وإذا سقطت سقطت . وأما المماثلة في الصفة ففى الجهر والأخير الإخفاء ، وأما المماثلة في القدر ففى ضم السورة مع الفاتحة. البناية: كتاب الصلاة، باب النوافل، فصل فى القراء ة ، ج ۲ ص ۵۲۵، ط: دار الكتب العلمية
According to him (Hasan al-Basri), in fard prayer, recitation is wajib in only one rak'ah, because Allah says: 'So recite what is easy of the Quran' (al-Muzzammil 20). Thus in this verse, 'faqra'u' is a command, and a command does not require repetition. So Hasan al-Basri says recitation is wajib in only one rak'ah. The Hanafi imams respond: We accept that a command does not require repetition, so on that basis recitation is wajib in only one rak'ah. But our assertion of obligation in the second rak'ah is because the second rak'ah resembles the first in every way; therefore we said recitation is wajib in the second rak'ah as well. Thus recitation in the first rak'ah is established by the explicit text (ibarat al-nass), and in the second rak'ah by implication of the text (dalalat al-nass). And we have the statement of Allah: 'So recite what is easy of it' and the principle that a command to an action does not require repetition. The meaning is that Allah commanded us to recite from what is easy of the Quran, and that is in prayer by consensus. A command to an action requires compliance, but does not require repetition as a repetition of the very same thing, not a repetition of a similar thing. So it dictates that recitation occurs in one rak'ah, as Hasan al-Basri held. And we only obligated in the second—meaning we obligated recitation in the second rak'ah. This is a response to the objection that you said the command does not require repetition, yet you obligated recitation in the second rak'ah, contradicting what you said. The answer is that the obligation of recitation in the second is not by the explicit text (ibarat al-nass) such that your objection would apply; rather its obligation in the second is by implication of the text (dalalat al-nass). This is the meaning of his saying 'by inference from the first'—meaning the first rak'ah. He explained that by saying: 'because the two resemble each other in every respect'—that is, the first and second rak'ahs resemble each other in every respect. When that is the case, it becomes obligatory in the second by inference from the first, like a ruling for one type of thing is extended to another type. The resemblance of the second to the first in every respect is in terms of falling due, obligation, description, and quantity. Whoever the first rak'ah is obligatory upon, the second is also obligatory, and if it falls, it falls. Similarly, resemblance in description is in terms of loudness and quietness, and resemblance in quantity is in terms of adding a surah to al-Fatihah. Al-Binayah: Kitab al-Salah, Bab al-Nawafil, Fasl fi al-Qira'ah, vol. 2, p. 525, Dar al-Kutub al-Ilmiyyah.
Source pages p. 120

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute concerning the obligation of Qur'anic recitation (qira'ah) in the second rak'ah of fard prayer. The opponent is Hasan al-Basri, who argues that the Qur'anic command 'faqra'u ma tayassara' (al-Muzzammil 20) is an imperative (amr) that does not require repetition, hence recitation is wajib only once, in one rak'ah. The Hanafi response concedes the usul principle that amr bi al-fi'l does not entail repetition (takraar) of identical acts. However, they distinguish between the first and second rak'ah: the first is wajib by the explicit wording of the text (ibarat al-nass), while the second is wajib by dalaalat al-nass (implication of the text), because the second rak'ah resembles the first in all respects (obligation, description, quantity, etc.). The Hanafis use qiyas based on this complete resemblance (tashakkul min kulli wajh). They further support this with a detailed passage from the commentary Al-Binayah, which explains that although the command does not require repetition of the exact same act, it can require a similar act through logical inference. The practical result: in the Hanafi madhhab, recitation is wajib in both rak'ahs of fard, unlike the view of Hasan al-Basri.

Key Terms
امر (amr): A linguistic command form (e.g., imperative verb) that indicates obligation (wujub) in Hanafi usul.
تکرار (takraar): The repetition of the exact same act (the same instance). The principle: amr does not require takraar
عبارة النص (ibarat al-nass): The explicit meaning directly derived from the wording of the text (Qur'an or Hadith). Here, the first rak'ah recitation is wajib by explicit command.
دلالة النص (dalaalat al-nass): The implied meaning of the text where the ruling for an unmentioned case is derived from the mentioned one due to logical connection (here, complete resemblance).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi response to Hasan al-Basri, why is recitation wajib in the second rak'ah of fard prayer?
A) Because the verse explicitly commands recitation in every rak'ah
B) Because the command requires repetition of the same act
C) Because the second rak'ah resembles the first in all respects, making it obligatory by dalaalat al-nass
D) Because Hasan al-Basri also held it wajib

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school uses dalaalat al-nass based on complete resemblance to extend the obligation of recitation from the first to the second rak'ah, without violating the usul principle that amr does not require repetition.

Salah — Prayer

Recitation in Nafl and Witr: Every Two Rak'ahs Are Independent
Establishing the ruling that recitation is wajib in all rak'ahs of nafl and witr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on recitation in nafl and witr, explain the legal principle that each pair of nafl is an independent prayer, and apply the qiyas reasoning to derive the ruling.

Core Idea
Every pair of nafl is an independent prayer; hence recitation is wajib in all rak'ahs.

You know that in fard prayer, recitation is required in every rak'ah. But in nafl, does the same apply? The Hanafi school answers with a decisive principle: each two rak'ahs of nafl form a separate prayer. This lesson unpacks that principle, shows its proof through qiyas, and extends it to witr. By the end, you'll see why recitation cannot be omitted from any rak'ah of nafl or witr.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core principle
The passage begins with "Inna kulla shaf' mina al-nafli salatun 'ala hidah". Understand that this is a legal maxim (qawida): every pair of nafl is an independent prayer.
This principle is the foundation for the ruling.
2
Apply the principle to recitation
Since each pair is an independent prayer, and a prayer cannot be devoid of recitation (as is the case in fard), recitation is wajib in every rak'ah of nafl.
If one rak'ah in a pair lacks recitation, that pair becomes prayer without recitation, which is invalid.
3
Examine the qiyas reasoning
The author analogizes each pair of nafl to the first pair of fard (the asl). The illa (effective cause) is that each pair is an independent act of worship.
This is qiyas shabahah: resemblance in structure.
4
Consider the practical implication: tahrimah coverage
If one intends four rak'ahs with one takbir, only the first two are wajib due to the single tahrimah. If abandoned, only two rak'ahs are owed as qada', proving each pair is separate.
The third rak'ah begins like a new prayer with thana' and ta'awwudh.
5
Distinguish witr
Witr has a different rationale: ihtiyat (precaution) because it shares features of fard and nafl. Recitation is wajib but thana' and ta'awwudh are not recited in the third rak'ah, nor is the first tashahhud completed.
This shows that witr is treated closer to fard in some respects.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

مذکورہ اصول کو ذکر کرنے کے بعد اس بات کو ثابت کر رہے ہیں کہ نفل نماز کی تمام رکعتوں میں قراءت فرض ہے، کیونکہ نفضل نماز کی ہر دو رکعت مستقل نماز ہے اور اگر دو رکعت میں قرات کرے اور دو میں قراءت نہ کرے تو گویا کہ نماز کا قراءت سے خالی ہونا لازم آئے گا، کیونکہ دو رکعت مستقل نماز ہے اور نماز کو قراءت سے خالی کرنا جائز نہیں ہے یہی تو وجہ ہے کہ اگر ایک آدمی نے چار رکعت نفل نماز کے لئے تھر یہ کبھی تو احناف کے نزدیک اب اس شخص پر اس تحریمہ کی وجہ سے صرف پہلی دو رکعت واجب ہیں ، چنانچہ اگر وہ اس نماز کو ترک کر دیتا ہے تو اس پر صرف دو رکعت کی قضاء واجب ہوگی ، اس سے بھی معلوم ہوا کہ نفل کی ہر دورکعت مستقل نماز ہے، تیسری رکعت کا قیام تحریمہ جدید کی طرح ہے، اسی وجہ سے فقہاء احناف فرماتے ہیں کہ تیسری رکعت کا آغاز ثناء سے کرے۔ الهداية كتاب الصلاة، باب النوافل، فصل فى القراء ة ، ج ۱ ص ۱۵۴، ط: رحمانیہ وَأَمَّا صِفَةُ الْقِرَاءَةِ فِيهَا فَالْقِرَاءةُ فِى السُّنَنِ فِي الرَّكَعَاتِ كُلَّهَا فَرْضٌ لِأَنَّ السُّنَّةَ تَطَوُّعٌ وَكُلُّ شَفْعِ مِنَ التَّطَوُّعِ صَلَاةٌ عَلَى حِدَةٍ، لِمَا نَذْكُرُ فِي صَلَاةِ التَّطَوُّعِ فَكَانَ كُلُّ شَفْعِ مِنْهَا بِمَنْزِلَةِ الشَّفْعِ الْأَوَّلِ مِنَ الْقِرَائِضِ. بدائع الصنائع: كتاب الصلاة، فصل فى القراءة في سنن الصلاة، ج ۱ ص ۲۸۵، ط: دار الكتب العلمية ] (قَوْلُهُ: وَالْقِرَاءَةُ وَاجِبَةٌ فِي جَمِيعِ رَكَعَاتِ النَّفْلِ وَفِي جَمِيعِ الْوِتْرِ) أَمَّا النَّفَلُ فَانَّ كُلَّ شَفْعِ مِنْهُ صَلَاةٌ عَلَى حِدَةٍ وَالْقِيَامُ إِلَى الثَّالِثَةِ كَتَحْرِيمَةٍ مُبْتَدَأَةٍ وَلِهَذَا يَسْتَفْتِحُ فِيهَا وَيَتَعَوَّذُ وَأَمَّا الْوِتْرُ فَلِلِاحْتِيَاطِ، لِأَنَّهُ مُتَرَدِّدٌ بَيْنَ الْقَرْضِ وَالنَّفَلِ لِوُجُودِ عَلَامَةِ الْأَمْرَيْنِ فَاحْتَاطُوا لَهُ بِإِيجَابِ الْقِرَاءِ ةِ لِاحْتِمَالِ أَنْ يَكُونَ نَفْلًا وَلَا يَسْتَفْتِحُ فِى الثَّالِثَةِ مِنْهُ وَلَا يَتَعَوَّذُ وَلَا يُكْمِلُ تَشَهَّدَهُ الْأَوَّلَ لِشَبَهِهِ بِالْفَرْضِ. الجوهرة النيرة كتاب الصلاة، باب النوافل، ج ۱ ص ۷۳، ط: المطبعة الخيرية ]
(105) Indeed, every pair (shaf') of voluntary prayer (nafl) is an independent prayer. Translation: Every two rak'ahs of nafl are an independent prayer. Explanation: The meaning of this principle is that in nafl prayer, every two rak'ahs are separate and independent prayers. The author of Al-Hidayah, after mentioning this principle, is proving that recitation in all rak'ahs of nafl prayer is fard (obligatory within the prayer), because every two rak'ahs of nafl prayer are an independent prayer. If one recites in two rak'ahs but not in the other two, then it would necessitate that the prayer is devoid of recitation, because each two rak'ahs are an independent prayer, and it is not permissible to leave a prayer devoid of recitation. This is the reason that if a person intends four rak'ahs of nafl prayer with one takbir, then according to the Hanafis, due to that tahrimah (opening takbir) only the first two rak'ahs are wajib (obligatory). Thus if he abandons this prayer, only the qada' (make-up) of two rak'ahs is wajib upon him. This also indicates that every two rak'ahs of nafl are an independent prayer. Standing for the third rak'ah is like a new tahrimah, and for this reason Hanafi jurists say that the third rak'ah should begin with thana' (opening supplication). Al-Hidayah: Kitab al-Salah, Bab al-Nawafil, Fasl fi al-Qira'ah, vol. 1, p. 154, Rahmaniyyah. 'As for the description of recitation in them, recitation in the sunan (optional prayers) in all the rak'ahs is fard (obligatory), because the sunnah is supererogatory, and every pair of supererogatory prayer is an independent prayer, as we will mention in the prayer of supererogation. Thus each pair of them is like the first pair of the obligatory prayers.' Bada'i' al-Sana'i': Kitab al-Salah, Fasl fi al-Qira'ah fi Sunan al-Salah, vol. 1, p. 285, Dar al-Kutub al-Ilmiyyah. 'His saying: Recitation is wajib in all rak'ahs of nafl and in all of witr. As for nafl, every pair of it is an independent prayer, and standing for the third is like a new tahrimah, so he opens with thana' and ta'awwudh. As for witr, it is for precaution, because it is ambiguous between fard and nafl, having signs of both. So they took precaution by making recitation obligatory due to the possibility that it is nafl, yet he does not open with thana' in the third of it, nor ta'awwudh, nor does he complete the first tashahhud, due to its resemblance to fard.' Al-Jawhara al-Nayyirah: Kitab al-Salah, Bab al-Nawafil, vol. 1, p. 73, al-Matba'ah al-Khayriyyah.
Source pages p. 121

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the obligation of Qur'anic recitation in nafl (supererogatory) and witr prayers. It begins by stating a foundational legal principle (qawida): in nafl prayer, every two rak'ahs (shaf') constitute an independent prayer (salah wahidah). This is not merely a theoretical statement; it has practical consequences. The author of Usool al-Hidayah explains that because each pair is independent, leaving recitation in any pair would render that pair devoid of recitation, which is invalid. Therefore, recitation is fard (obligatory within the prayer) in every rak'ah of nafl. Furthermore, the principle is illustrated by the case of a person who intends four rak'ahs of nafl with a single takbir: only the first two rak'ahs are wajib (due to the tahrimah), and if abandoned, only two rak'ahs are owed as qada'. This shows that each pair is a separate unit. The third rak'ah is initiated like a new prayer, with thana' and ta'awwudh. The passage then quotes Al-Hidayah and Bada'i' al-Sana'i' to confirm that recitation in sunan (nafl/sunnah prayers) is fard in all rak'ahs because each pair is independent. Finally, Al-Jawhara al-Nayyirah adds the rule for witr: recitation is wajib in all its rak'ahs due to ihtiyat (precaution), since witr shares characteristics of both fard and nafl. However, unlike nafl, the third rak'ah of witr does not begin with thana' and ta'awwudh, nor is the first tashahhud completed, because of its resemblance to fard. The Hanafi ruling: recitation is wajib in all rak'ahs of nafl and witr, but the specific rituals (thana', ta'awwudh, tashahhud) differ between the two.

Key Terms
شفع (shaf'): A pair of rak'ahs in nafl prayer considered a single unit.
نفل (nafl): Voluntary, supererogatory prayer beyond the obligatory and sunnah mu'akkadah.
وتر (witr): An odd-numbered prayer (usually three rak'ahs) performed after Isha', considered wajib in the Hanafi school.
تحریمہ (tahrimah): The opening takbir (Allahu Akbar) that begins the prayer and renders it sacred.
احتیاط (ihtiyat): Precautionary legal reasoning used when a case shares features of two categories; the stricter ruling is applied to ensure validity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Why is recitation wajib in every rak'ah of nafl prayer according to the Hanafi madhhab?
A) Because the Prophet (ﷺ) always recited in every rak'ah of nafl
B) Because every two rak'ahs of nafl constitute an independent prayer, and a prayer cannot be devoid of recitation
C) Because the Quran explicitly commands recitation in each rak'ah of nafl
D) Because it is a concession for ease

Key Takeaway
Every two rak'ahs of nafl form an independent prayer; therefore, recitation is wajib in all rak'ahs of nafl and witr.

The Maxim of Shuru': Beginning Obligates What is Started and Necessary
Stating the principle that starting a worship obligates both the act and its prerequisites

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi maxim 'al-shuru' mulzim ma shara'a fihi' to determine how many rak'ahs become obligatory upon beginning a nafl prayer, and explain the intra-Hanafi disagreement between the two (Abu Hanifa & Muhammad) and Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
Beginning obligates what you started and what it depends on—but only the started pair is initially wajib.

This lesson introduces a foundational Hanafi legal maxim that governs the obligations that arise when one commences a worship, specifically the prayer. The maxim states that the act of beginning (shuru') makes obligatory both the thing one has started (ma shara'a fihi) and anything without which that thing would not be valid (ma la sihhata lahu illa bihi). We will see how this maxim is applied to a four-rak'ah nafl prayer, and explore a disagreement within the Hanafi school about how many rak'ahs become obligatory upon the initial takbir.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Maxim
Break down the maxim: 'al-shuru' mulzim ma shara'a fihi wa ma la sihhata lahu illa bihi'. Identify the two components: (1) the act begun itself, and (2) anything that is a prerequisite for its validity.
The cause (sabab) of obligation is the actual commencement (takbir), not merely the intention.
2
Apply to Nafl Prayer
Consider a person who intends four rak'ahs of nafl and makes takbir. The first rak'ah is 'ma shara'a fihi'—it is what was started. The second rak'ah becomes obligatory because the first rak'ah depends on it for validity (a prayer requires at least two rak'ahs). Thus, the first pair (two rak'ahs) becomes wajib.
The second pair (third and fourth rak'ahs) is neither started nor necessary for the first pair's validity.
3
Identify the Intra-Madhhab Dispute
Imam Abu Yusuf holds that all four rak'ahs become obligatory from the start because the intention was for four. The two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) argue that only the first pair is obligated initially, as the cause is the actual beginning which only covers the first pair.
The key is whether the cause (shuru') attaches to the entire intended act or only to the act as actually commenced.
4
Analyze the Thamarah al-Khilaf
If the prayer is invalidated after two rak'ahs (before standing for the third), according to the two, only two rak'ahs need to be made up. According to Abu Yusuf, all four rak'ahs require qada. This practical difference stems from the different views on what the beginning obligates.
This illustrates how a seemingly abstract principle has concrete consequences in worship.
5
Determine the Mufta Bihi
Al-Hidayah states that the position of the two is the apparent view (wajh al-zahir), and it is the relied-upon position for fatwa. Students should adopt this view unless acting as a mufti with due consideration of the school's hierarchy.
The authority weight is zahir al-riwayah.

(١٠٦ ) إِنَّ الشُّرُوعَ مُلْزِمٌ مَا شَرَعَ فِيْهِ وَمَا لَا صِحَّةَ لَهُ إِلَّا بِهِ.
ترجمہ : شروع کرنا اس چیز کو لازم کرتا ہے جس کو شروع کیا ہو اور اس کو جس کے بغیر شروع کی ہوئی چیز صحیح نہ ہو۔
تشریح: مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ شروع کرنا اس چیز کے وجوب کا سبب بنتا ہے جس کو شروع کیا گیا ہو، اور اس چیز کے وجوب کا سبب بنتا ہے جس پر شروع کی ہوئی چیز موقوف ہو، مثلاً نفل نماز شروع کرتے ہی رکعت اولی واجب ہو گئی کیونکہ رکعت اولی ( ما شرع فیہ ) ہے، اور رکعت اولی کی صحت موقوف ہے رکعت ثانیہ پر لہذا شروع کرنے سے رکعت ثانیہ بھی واجب ہوگئی۔ صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول کو ذکر کرنے کے بعد اس بات کو ثابت کرتے ہیں کہ اگر ایک آدمی نے چار رکعت نفل نماز کی نیت کر لی اور تحریمہ باندھ لی تو اس تحریمہ اولی سے صرف اس شخص پر دو رکعت واجب ہوں گی ، اب اگر اس شخص نے تیسری رکعت کے لئے کھڑا ہونے سے پہلے شفع اول فاسد کر دیا تو اب اس شخص پر طرفین کے نزدیک صرف دور کعت کی قضا واجب ہوگی نہ کہ چار رکعت کی، جبکہ امام ابو یوسف رحمہ اللہ کے نزدیک چار رکعت کی قضاء واجب ہے۔ طرفین کی دلیل یہ اصول ہے کہ شروع کرنا اس چیز کے وجوب کا سبب ہوتا ہے جس کو شروع کیا ہو اور اس چیز کے و جوب کا سبب ہوتا ہے جس پر مشروع کی ہوئی کی صحت موقوف ہو ، تو اسی اصول کی بنیاد پر طرفین فرماتے ہیں کہ پہلی رکعت تو اس لئے واجب ہوگی کہ وہ ما شرع فیہ تھی اور دوسری رکعت اس لئے واجب ہوگی کہ رکعت اولی کی صحت رکعت ثانیہ پر موقوف ہے، رہی بات شفع ثانی ( یعنی آخری دو رکعتیں) تو وہ نہ ما شرع فیہ ہے اور نہ اس پر ما شرع فیہ کی صحت موقوف ہے، لہذ اشفع اول کو شروع کرنے سے شفع ثانی واجب نہیں ہو گا۔
الهداية كتاب الصلاة، باب النوافل، فصل فى القراء ة ، ج ۱ ص ۱۵۵، ط: رحمانیه وَجْهُ الظَّاهِرِ أَنَّ الشُّرُوعَ مُلْزِمٌ مَا شَرَعَ فِيهِ وَمَا لَا صِحَّةَ لَهُ إِلَّا بِهِ وَلَا تَعَلَّقَ لِأَحَدِ الشَّفْعَيْنِ بِالْآخِرِ وَهَذَا لِأَنَّ السَّبَبَ هُوَ الشُّرُوعُ وَلَمْ يُوجَدُ الشُّرُوعُ فِي الشَّفْعِ الثَّانِي مَا لَمْ يَقُمُ إِلَى الثَّالِثَةِ فَلَمْ تَقْتَرِنُ النِّيَّةُ بِالسَّبَبِ وَإِنَّمَا هِيَ مُجَرَّدُ النِّيَّةِ وَهِيَ لَمْ تُؤَثْرُ فِي الْإِيجَابِ. تبيين الحقائق كتاب الصلاة، باب الوتر والنوافل، ج ١ ص ۱۷۴، ط: دار الكتاب الإسلامي
(106) Indeed, beginning obligates what one has started and what is not valid except by it. Translation: Beginning makes obligatory that which one has begun and that without which the begun thing is not valid. Explanation: The meaning of the above principle is that beginning causes the obligation of the thing that was begun, and causes the obligation of that upon which the begun thing depends. For example, upon beginning nafl prayer, the first rak'ah becomes obligatory because it is 'what was begun', and the validity of the first rak'ah depends on the second rak'ah, so by beginning, the second rak'ah also becomes obligatory. The author of Al-Hidayah, after mentioning this principle, proves that if a person intends four rak'ahs of nafl prayer and makes the takbirat al-ihram, then due to that first takbir only two rak'ahs become obligatory for him. Now, if he invalidates the first pair before standing for the third rak'ah, then according to the two (imams) only two rak'ahs need to be made up, not four, whereas according to Imam Abu Yusuf four rak'ahs must be made up. The proof of the two is this principle: that beginning causes the obligation of what one began and of what the validity of the begun depends on. On this basis, the two say that the first rak'ah becomes obligatory because it is 'what was begun', and the second rak'ah becomes obligatory because the validity of the first depends on the second. As for the second pair (the last two rak'ahs), it is neither 'what was begun' nor does the validity of what was begun depend on it, so beginning the first pair does not make the second pair obligatory. [Al-Hidayah, Kitab al-Salah, Bab al-Nawafil, Fasl fi al-Qira'ah, vol. 1 p. 155, Rahmaniyyah: 'The apparent view is that beginning obligates what one began and what is not valid except by it, and there is no connection of one pair to the other. This is because the cause is the beginning, and the beginning of the second pair does not occur until one stands for the third. So the intention is not conjoined with the cause; it is mere intention, which has no effect in obligation.' Tabyin al-Haqa'iq, Kitab al-Salah, Bab al-Witr wa al-Nawafil, vol. 1 p. 174, Dar al-Kitab al-Islami.]
Source pages p. 122

Commentary
This passage presents a key Hanafi legal maxim: 'Beginning obligates what one has started and what is necessary for its validity.' The commentator explains that when one begins a prayer (e.g., by takbir), the first rak'ah becomes obligatory (wajib) as it is what was started. Then, because the validity of the first rak'ah depends on the second (since a prayer must have at least two rak'ahs), the second rak'ah also becomes obligatory. The commentator applies this to a specific scenario: if a person intends a four-rak'ah nafl prayer, only the first two rak'ahs become obligatory upon starting. If the first pair is invalidated before standing for the third, only two rak'ahs need to be made up according to Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad (the two). Imam Abu Yusuf, however, holds that all four rak'ahs become obligatory. The text gives the reasoning: the cause of obligation is the actual beginning (the takbir), and that only applies to the first pair. The second pair is not begun until one actually stands for the third rak'ah. This principle is supported by a quote from Al-Hidayah affirming the apparent view (wajh al-zahir). The passage thus demonstrates how a general legal maxim is applied to derive specific fiqh rulings, including an intra-madhhab ikhtilaf.

Key Terms
شروع (shuru'): The act of commencing a worship, specifically the takbirat al-ihram in prayer, which creates legal obligations.
ما شرع فيه (ma shara'a fihi): That which is actually begun, e.g., the first rak'ah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If someone intends four rak'ahs of nafl, makes takbir, then invalidates the prayer after two rak'ahs, how many rak'ahs must he make up according to the relied-upon Hanafi view?
A) Four rak'ahs
B) Two rak'ahs
C) None, because nafl does not require qada
D) One rak'ah

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi maxim 'al-shuru' mulzim ma shara'a fihi' teaches that beginning a worship obligates only what is actually started and what is indispensable for its validity—not merely what is intended.

The Binding Nature of Shuru' in Supererogatory Prayer
A principle and its application to a dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi principle of shuru' being binding, apply it to determine which rak'ahs become wajib upon beginning a supererogatory prayer, and distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa/Muhammad versus Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
Beginning an act worship obligates the act and its prerequisites, but only what is actually started.

In Hanafi fiqh, starting a supererogatory prayer is not a casual act—it creates immediate legal obligations. The principle 'shuru' is binding' determines which parts of the prayer become wajib and what happens if you invalidate it. This lesson unpacks the maxim and a classic dispute between the founding imams about how many rak'ahs are owed when you start a four-rak'ah nafl.

Guided Path
1
Understand the maxim
Read the Arabic maxim and its translation. Grasp that shuru' (beginning) makes obligatory both the act started (ma shara'a fihi) and anything necessary for its validity (ma la sihhata lahu illa bihi).
The maxim is broader than prayer; it applies to all acts of worship.
2
Apply the maxim to a 2-rak'ah nafl
Consider a person who starts a 2-rak'ah nafl. The first rak'ah is 'ma shara'a fihi' and becomes wajib. The second rak'ah is necessary for the validity of the first (since a single rak'ah cannot be a complete prayer), so it also becomes wajib.
This is the straightforward case.
3
Extend to a 4-rak'ah nafl
Now consider a person who intends four rak'ahs and begins with takbir. The first two rak'ahs are the first set (shaf' awwal). The third and fourth rak'ahs are a separate set (shaf' thani). According to the maxim, only the first set is started and its prerequisite (the second rak'ah) is obligatory.
The crucial question: does the second set also become obligatory immediately?
4
Identify the dispute
The majority (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) hold that only the first two rak'ahs become wajib upon starting; the second set become wajib only when one stands for the third rak'ah. Abu Yusuf argues that all four become wajib from the start because the intention encompassed all four.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
5
Analyze the thamarah (practical consequence)
If the first two rak'ahs are invalidated before standing for the third, according to the majority only two rak'ahs must be made up; according to Abu Yusuf, four. This shows the real-world impact of the dispute.
Understand why the distinction matters for qada'.

(106) Verily, the act of beginning is binding upon what one has begun and upon that without which it has no validity. Translation: Beginning an action makes obligatory that which was begun and that upon which the correctness of what was begun depends. Explanation: The meaning of the mentioned principle is that beginning an act causes the obligation of what was begun, and also causes the obligation of that upon which the begun act depends. For example, upon beginning a supererogatory prayer, the first rak'ah becomes obligatory because it is 'what was begun', and the validity of the first rak'ah depends on the second rak'ah, so by beginning, the second rak'ah also becomes obligatory. After mentioning this principle, the author of Al-Hidayah proves that if a person intended a four-rak'ah supererogatory prayer and proclaimed the takbir al-tahrimah, then by that first takbir only two rak'ahs become obligatory upon him. Now, if he invalidates the first set (shaf' awwal) before standing for the third rak'ah, then according to the two sides (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) only two rak'ahs are due as make-up, not four, whereas according to Imam Abu Yusuf, four rak'ahs are due. The proof of the two sides is this principle: that beginning causes the obligation of what was begun and of that upon which the correctness of what was begun depends. On this basis, the two sides say that the first rak'ah is obligatory because it is 'what was begun', and the second rak'ah is obligatory because the validity of the first rak'ah depends on the second. As for the second set (i.e., the last two rak'ahs), it is neither 'what was begun' nor does the validity of 'what was begun' depend on it. Therefore, beginning the first set does not make the second set obligatory. Al-Hidayah, Book of Prayer, Chapter on Supererogatory Prayers, Section on Recitation, vol. 1 p. 155, Rahmaniyyah edition: The apparent view is that beginning is binding upon what one has begun and upon that without which it has no validity, and there is no connection of one set with the other. This is because the cause is the act of beginning, and the act of beginning has not occurred in the second set as long as he has not stood for the third. Thus the intention is not associated with the cause, and it is merely intention, and it has no effect in creating obligation. Tabyin al-Haqa'iq, Book of Prayer, Chapter on Witr and Supererogatory Prayers, vol. 1 p. 174, Dar al-Kitab al-Islami edition.
Source pages p. 122

Commentary
This passage presents a key Hanafi legal maxim: 'Beginning (shuru') is binding upon what one has begun and upon that without which it has no validity.' The author first states the maxim in Arabic, then provides an Urdu translation and commentary. The maxim means that when you start an act, you become obligated to complete that act and also to fulfill whatever is necessary for its validity. The example given is of a person who intends to pray four rak'ahs of nafl prayer and begins with the opening takbir. Immediately, the first rak'ah becomes wajib (obligatory) because it is what was started (ma shara'a fihi). The second rak'ah also becomes wajib because the validity of the first rak'ah depends on it (a single prayer unit cannot be valid alone). The author then applies this principle to a scenario: if the person invalidates the first two rak'ahs before standing for the third, how many rak'ahs must he make up? According to the majority (Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad, referred to as 'the two sides'), only two rak'ahs are due. Their reasoning is that the act of beginning only covered the first set (shaf' awwal); the second set (shaf' thani) was not yet started and was not a prerequisite for the first set. Imam Abu Yusuf, however, holds that all four rak'ahs become obligatory from the start because the intention of four was present. The text cites Al-Hidayah to reinforce that the apparent position is that beginning only obligates what is started and its prerequisites, and the two sets are independent; the second set only becomes obligatory when one stands for the third rak'ah. This is an important principle in Hanafi fiqh for understanding how obligations arise in supererogatory acts.

Key Terms
شروع (shurūʿ): The act of beginning an act of worship; in this context, it refers to starting the prayer with the opening takbir (tahrimah)
ما شرع فيه (mā sharaʿa fīhi): That which has been started; in the example, the first rak'ah of a supererogatory prayer
شفع (shafʿ): A pair or set; in prayer, it refers to two rak'ahs together, either the first two (shaf' awwal) or the last two (shaf' thani) in a four-rak'ah nafl
تحریمہ (taḥrīmah): The opening takbir (saying Allahu Akbar) that begins the prayer and makes worldly actions forbidden (haram) during the prayer

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority view (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), if a person begins a four-rak'ah supererogatory prayer and then invalidates the first two rak'ahs before standing for the third, how many rak'ahs must they make up?
A) Four rak'ahs
B) Two rak'ahs
C) One rak'ah
D) None, because nafl prayers are not obligatory

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi principle of shuru' being binding means that starting a supererogatory prayer immediately obligates the first two rak'ahs and their prerequisites, but not the entire intended number.

Omission of Recitation in Supererogatory Prayer: Intra-Hanafi Dispute on the Tahrimah
Intra-Hanafi dispute on recitation omission in nafl

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi positions on the effect of omitting recitation in the first set of a supererogatory prayer and apply the correct ruling based on each imam's view.

Core Idea
Omitting recitation in nafl prayer divides the Hanafi imams: does it void the prayer or just corrupt it?

Recitation (qira'ah) in the first two rak'ahs is wajib in every prayer according to the Hanafi school. But what happens if you omit it in a supererogatory prayer? The three founding imams disagreed sharply: does the entire prayer collapse, or can it be saved? This lesson unpacks their reasoning and the practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the disputed issue
Recognize that the act is a four-rak'ah supererogatory prayer (nafl) and the dispute is about the effect of omitting recitation in the first set (shaf' awwal) on the validity of the tahrimah (opening takbir).
The tahrimah is the act that initiates the prayer; if it is invalid, the prayer never began.
2
State Imam Muhammad's position
Imam Muhammad holds that omitting recitation in either both or even one rak'ah of the first set invalidates the tahrimah completely. The prayer is void and cannot be continued.
This is the strictest view: recitation is so integral that its absence in any rak'ah of the first set destroys the prayer's foundation.
3
State Imam Abu Yusuf's position
Imam Abu Yusuf holds that omitting recitation in both rak'ahs of the first set does not invalidate the tahrimah. Instead, it only corrupts the performance (fasad al-ada'), meaning the prayer is still valid but defective.
This view allows the prayer to continue; the second set can be built upon the first despite the defect.
4
State Imam Abu Hanifa's position
Imam Abu Hanifa distinguishes: if recitation is omitted in both rak'ahs, the tahrimah is invalid; if omitted in only one, the tahrimah remains valid and the prayer can proceed.
This is the middle ground: the tahrimah depends on recitation in at least one rak'ah of the first set.
5
Connect to the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
The dispute affects how many rak'ahs become obligatory if a person starts a four-rak'ah nafl and omits recitation entirely. According to the two sides (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), only two rak'ahs are due; according to Abu Yusuf, four are due.
This shows how the theoretical dispute has a direct impact on qada' (make-up) obligations.

(١٠) إِنَّ عِنْدَ مُحَمَّدٍ تَرُكُ الْقِرَاءَةِ فِي الْأُولَيَيْنِ أَوْ فِي إِحْدَاهُمَا يُوجِبُ بُطَلانَ التَّحْرِيمَةِ وَعِندَ أَبِى يُوسُفَ تَرُكُ الْقِرَاءَةِ فِي الشَّفْعِ الْأَوَّلِ لَا يُوجِبُ بُطَلانَ التَّحْرِيمَةِ وَإِنَّمَا يُوجِبُ فَسَادَ الْأَدَاءِ وَعِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيْفَةَ تَرُكُ الْقِرَاءَةِ فِي الْأُولَيَيْن يُوجِبُ بُطَلانَ التَّحْرِيمَةِ وَفِي إِحْدَاهُمَا لَا يُوجِبُ . ترجمہ: امام محمد کے نزدیک پہلی دو رکعتوں میں یا دونوں میں سے ایک رکعت میں قراءت کو ترک کرنا یہ تحریمہ کے بطلان کو ثابت کرتا ہے، اور امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک شفع اول میں قراءت کوترک کرنا یہ تحریمہ کے بطلان کو ثابت نہیں کرتا، یہ فساد اداء ہی کو ثابت کرتا ہے ، امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک پہلی دونوں رکعتوں میں قرات کو ترک کرنا تحریمہ کو باطل کر دیتا ہے اور دونوں میں سے ایک کوترک کرنا تحریمہ کے بطلان کو ثابت نہیں کرتا۔ تشریح : مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ امام محمد رحمہ اللہ کے نزدیک اگر کسی آدمی نے شفع اول کی دونوں رکعتوں میں یا دونوں میں سے ایک رکعت میں قراءت نہ کی تو اس شخص کی تحریمہ باطل ہو جائے گی لہذ اشفع ثانی کی بنا کر ناشفع اول پر درست نہیں ہے۔ اور امام ابو یوسف رحمہ اللہ کے نزدیک اگر ایک آدمی شفع اول کی دونوں رکعتوں میں قراءت نہ کرے پھر بھی تحریمہ باقی رہے گی البتہ اداء فاسد ہو جائے گی ، لہذا اسی شفع اول پر شفع ثانی کی بناء کرنا درست ہے۔ اور امام ابوحنیفہ رحمہ اللہ کے نزدیک اگر شفیع اول کی دونوں رکعتوں میں قراءت ترک کردی تو تحریمہ باطل ہو جائے گی، البتہ اگر شفع اول کی ایک رکعت میں قرات ترک کی تو اس سے تحریمہ باطل نہیں ہوگی لہذا اس پر شفع ثانی کی بنا درست ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول کو ذکر کرنے کے بعد اس بات کو ثابت کر رہے ہیں کہ اگر کسی آدمی نے چار رکعت نفل نماز شروع کی اور پھر کسی رکعت میں بھی قراءت نہیں کی تو اب طرفین کے نزدیک اس پر صرف دور کعت کی قضا واجب ہے اور امام ابو یوسف رحمہ اللہ کے نزدیک چار رکعت الهداية كتاب الصلاة، باب النوافل، فصل فى القراء ة ، ج ۱ ص ۱۵۵، ط: رحمانيه
(10) Indeed, according to Muhammad, omitting recitation in the first two or in one of them causes the invalidation of the tahrimah. According to Abu Yusuf, omitting recitation in the first set does not cause the invalidation of the tahrimah; rather, it only causes corruption of the performance. According to Abu Hanifa, omitting recitation in the first two causes the invalidation of the tahrimah, but in one of them it does not cause it. Translation: According to Imam Muhammad, omitting recitation in the first two rak'ahs or in one of them establishes the invalidation of the tahrimah. According to Imam Abu Yusuf, omitting recitation in the first set does not establish the invalidation of the tahrimah; it only establishes corruption of the performance. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, omitting recitation in the first two rak'ahs invalidates the tahrimah, but omitting it in one of them does not establish the invalidation of the tahrimah. Explanation: The meaning of the mentioned principle is that according to Imam Muhammad, if a person does not recite in both rak'ahs of the first set or in one of them, his tahrimah becomes invalid, so building the second set upon the first set is not valid. According to Imam Abu Yusuf, if a person does not recite in both rak'ahs of the first set, the tahrimah remains, but the performance becomes corrupt; therefore, building the second set upon that first set is valid. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, if recitation is omitted in both rak'ahs of the first set, the tahrimah becomes invalid; however, if recitation is omitted in one rak'ah of the first set, the tahrimah does not become invalid, so building the second set upon it is valid. After mentioning this principle, the author of Al-Hidayah proves that if a person begins a four-rak'ah supererogatory prayer and then does not recite in any rak'ah, then according to the two sides only two rak'ahs are due as make-up, and according to Imam Abu Yusuf, four rak'ahs. Al-Hidayah, Book of Prayer, Chapter on Supererogatory Prayers, Section on Recitation, vol. 1 p. 155, Rahmaniyyah edition.
Source pages p. 123

Commentary
This passage presents the second principle from Usool al-Hidayah, detailing the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the effect of omitting recitation (qira'ah) in the first set (shaf' awwal) of a supererogatory prayer. The principle is stated in Arabic, followed by an Urdu translation and explanation. Three positions are given: Imam Muhammad holds that omitting recitation in either both or even one of the first two rak'ahs invalidates the tahrimah (opening takbir). This means the entire prayer is invalid and cannot be built upon. Imam Abu Yusuf holds that omitting recitation in both rak'ahs of the first set does not invalidate the tahrimah; rather, the performance becomes fasad (corrupt) but the prayer can still be connected, so building the second set on the first is valid. Imam Abu Hanifa takes a middle position: if recitation is omitted in both rak'ahs, the tahrimah is invalid; but if omitted in only one, the tahrimah remains valid, and the second set can be built upon the first. The passage then connects this to the earlier discussion on how many rak'ahs become obligatory when starting a four-rak'ah nafl: if recitation is completely omitted, the two sides (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) hold that only two rak'ahs are due (because the tahrimah was invalidated before the second set could be started), while Abu Yusuf holds that four are due (because the tahrimah remained valid). This shows how the ruling on recitation affects the number of rak'ahs due as make-up.

Key Terms
قراءت (qirāʾah): The recitation of a portion of the Qur'an in prayer; in this context, it refers to the obligation to recite in the first two rak'ahs of a supererogatory prayer
بطلان تحریمہ (buṭlān al-taḥrīmah): The invalidation of the opening takbir, meaning the entire prayer is rendered void from the start
فساد اداء (fasād al-adāʾ): Corruption of the performance; the prayer is still valid in its essence but defective in its execution, requiring sajdah al-sahw or making the nafl makruh

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling of Imam Abu Yusuf regarding the omission of recitation in both rak'ahs of the first set of a supererogatory prayer?
A) The tahrimah is invalid and the prayer must be restarted
B) The tahrimah remains valid, but the performance becomes corrupt
C) The prayer is valid and no compensation is needed
D) The entire prayer becomes void and requires repetition

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has three distinct positions on the effect of omitting recitation in the first set of a supererogatory prayer, with Imam Muhammad being the strictest and Imam Abu Yusuf the most lenient.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
10 min
Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Leaving Recitation in the First Two Rak'ahs
Explains the three Hanafi positions on omission of qira'ah in early rak'ahs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi positions on the effect of omitting qira'ah in the first two rak'ahs of a nafil prayer and apply them to determine the required qada.

Core Idea
Omitting recitation in the first two rak'ahs affects the tahrimah differently according to each Hanafi imam.

This passage from al-Hidayah records an important intra-Hanafi dispute on whether leaving recitation in the first two rak'ahs invalidates the opening of the prayer. The three leading imams of the school differ on the precise effect, leading to different practical outcomes in repeating the prayer. Understanding this ikhtilaf sharpens your ability to trace rulings back to their foundational principles.

Guided Path
1
State the three positions
Identify each imam's ruling on omitting recitation in both first rak'ahs and in just one of them.
Imam Muhammad: both or one → tahrimah invalid. Imam Abu Yusuf: both → fasad, not butlan. Imam Abu Hanifa: both → butlan, one → no butlan.
2
Understand the technical terms
Distinguish between 'butlan al-tahrimah' (invalidity of the opening) and 'fasad al-ada'' (corruption of performance).
Fasad al-ada' means the prayer is performed but invalid; butlan means the act never validly started.
3
Apply to a four-rak'ah nafil
Consider a person who starts 4 rak'ahs and omits recitation completely in all rak'ahs. Determine how many rak'ahs must be repeated according to each imam.
Abu Hanifa & Muhammad: 2 rak'ahs repeated. Abu Yusuf: 4 rak'ahs repeated.
4
Recognize the dalil
Note Abu Yusuf's analogy: the prayer of an unlettered person (ummi) is valid without recitation, so leaving recitation does not invalidate the tahrimah.
This shows how qiyas is used within the madhhab.
5
Trace the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: the number of rak'ahs to repeat differs. This affects how a mufti advises a person who made this mistake.
The khilaf is not merely theoretical; it changes the ruling for the individual.

باطل نہیں ہوئی لہذا اشفع ثانی کو شروع کرنا صحیح ہے، لیکن ترک قراءت کی وجہ سے چاروں رکعتیں فاسد ہو گئیں اس لئے چاروں کی قضاء واجب ہے۔ (وَكَذَا الْخِلافُ لَوْ جَرَّدَ الْأَرْبَعَ عَنْ الْقِرَاءَةِ) أَى يَقْضِى رَكْعَتَيْنِ عِنْدَهُمَا لِأَنَّ أَفْعَالَ الصَّلَاةِ لَمَّا فَسَدَتْ بِتَرْكِ الْقِرَاءةِ بَطَلَتْ التَّحْرِيمَةُ لِأَنَّهَا إِنَّمَا انْعَقَدَتْ لِأُجُلِهَا فَلَمْ يَصِحٌ شُرُوعُهُ فِي الشَّفْعِ الثَّانِي فَيَلْزَمُ قَضَاءُ الشَّفْعِ الأَوَّلِ فَقَط وَعِندَ أَبِى يُوسُفَ تَرْكُ الْقِرَاءَةِ لَا يُوجِبُ بُطَلَانَ التَّحْرِيمَةِ لِجَوَازِ صَلَاةِ الْأُمِّيِّ بِلَا قِرَاءَ وَ فَيَصِحُ شُرُوعُهُ فِي الْأَرْبَعِ فَيَلْزَمُ قَضَاءُ الْأَرْبَعِ لِإِفْسَادِهَا بِتَرْكِ الْقِرَاءَةِ أَوْ قَرَأَ فِي إِحْدَى الْأَخْرَيَيْنِ فَحَسْبُ أَى يَلْزَمُهُ قَضَاءُ رَكْعَتَيْنِ عِنْدَهُمَا وَقَضَاءُ أَرْبَعِ عِنْدَهُ عَلَى قِيَاسِ مَا سَبَقَ.
Indeed, according to Muhammad, leaving recitation in the first two or in one of them necessitates the invalidity of the tahrimah. According to Abu Yusuf, leaving recitation in the first pair does not necessitate the invalidity of the tahrimah, it only necessitates the corruption of performance. According to Abu Hanifa, leaving recitation in the first two necessitates the invalidity of the tahrimah, and in one of them it does not necessitate. Translation: According to Imam Muhammad, if a person did not recite in both rak'ahs of the first pair or in one of them, his tahrimah becomes invalid. So building the second pair upon the first is not correct. According to Imam Abu Yusuf, if a person did not recite in both rak'ahs of the first pair, the tahrimah remains but the performance becomes corrupt, so building the second pair upon the first is correct. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, if recitation is left in both rak'ahs, the tahrimah becomes invalid; but if left in one, it does not become invalid, so building the second pair is correct. Explanation: After mentioning the principle, the author of al-Hidayah proves that if a person started a four-rak'ah nafil and did not recite at all, then according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), only two rak'ahs must be repeated, while according to Abu Yusuf, four. This is because according to the two, the tahrimah became invalid due to leaving recitation, so the second pair was not validly started, as if he had intended two rak'ahs and corrupted them. According to Abu Yusuf, the tahrimah remained, so starting the second pair is valid, but all four were corrupted by leaving recitation, so all four must be repeated. (And similarly the dispute if he performs four without any recitation) i.e., he repeats two according to the two, because when the acts of prayer are corrupted by leaving recitation, the tahrimah is invalidated since it was only contracted for their sake, so his beginning the second pair is not valid, so only the repetition of the first pair is required. According to Abu Yusuf, leaving recitation does not necessitate invalidity of the tahrimah because of the permissibility of the prayer of an unlettered person without recitation, so his beginning the four is valid, so the repetition of all four is required due to their corruption by leaving recitation. Or if he recited in only one of the last two, then he repeats two according to the two and four according to him, by analogy to what preceded.
Source pages p. 123

Commentary
This lesson presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the effect of omitting recitation (qira'ah) in the first two rak'ahs (shaf' awwal) of a non-obligatory (nafil) prayer. The passage first states the positions of the three leading imams of the school: Imam Muhammad holds that omitting recitation in either both or even one of the first two rak'ahs invalidates the tahrimah (the act of beginning prayer). Imam Abu Yusuf holds that omitting recitation in both of the first two does not invalidate the tahrimah, but rather corrupts the performance (fasad al-ada'). Imam Abu Hanifa distinguishes between the two: omitting recitation in both first rak'ahs invalidates the tahrimah, but omitting it in only one does not. The commentary then applies these positions to a scenario where a person starts a four-rak'ah nafil prayer and omits recitation entirely. According to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), since the tahrimah is invalidated, the second pair was not validly begun; he is considered to have intended only two rak'ahs, so he must repeat two rak'ahs. According to Abu Yusuf, since the tahrimah remains, the second pair is validly begun, but all four rak'ahs are corrupted, so all four must be repeated. The passage concludes with an Arabic quote from Majma' al-Anhur and Al-Hidayah summarizing the same dispute, including a variation where recitation is omitted in the first two but done in one of the last two.

Key Terms
تحریمة (tahrimah): The act of initiating prayer with takbir and intention; the state that renders worldly actions forbidden during prayer.
شفع (shaf'): A pair of rak'ahs; in nafil, the first two rak'ahs are called shaf' awwal.
فساد الأداء (fasad al-ada'): Corruption of performance; the prayer is performed but not valid and must be repeated.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, leaving recitation in how many of the first two rak'ahs invalidates the tahrimah?
A) Both of the first two rak'ahs
B) Only the first rak'ah
C) Only the second rak'ah
D) Neither, it only corrupts the performance

Key Takeaway
The three Hanafi imams differ on whether omitting recitation in the first two rak'ahs invalidates the tahrimah or merely corrupts the performance, leading to different numbers of rak'ahs to repeat.

Salah — Prayer

The Principle 'Prayer is the Best Thing Set Before One'
States the maxim and applies it to sitting in nafil prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi maxim 'Prayer is the best thing set before one' to justify permissibility of sitting in nafil prayer despite ability to stand.

Core Idea
Prayer is the best thing placed before you—so nafil can be prayed sitting even if able to stand, to avoid hardship.

In this lesson, we examine a key principle from Al-Hidayah: 'Prayer is the best thing set before one.' This principle underscores the ease and accessibility of prayer in the Hanafi school. The author uses it to justify that one may pray nafil sitting even when able to stand, removing hardship and encouraging voluntary worship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the maxim and its literal meaning
Note the Arabic phrase 'إِنَّ الصَّلَاةَ خَيْرُ مَوْضُوعِ' and its translation: 'Verily, prayer is the best thing placed before one.' Recognize that it positions prayer as an easily accessible good deed.
The maxim is cited in Al-Hidayah as a foundational principle.
2
Understand the legal purpose: ease and encouragement
The maxim implies that prayer is made easy to attain; conditions should not be so burdensome that they lead to abandoning the prayer. This is especially relevant for nafil (voluntary) prayers.
Nafil acts are generally more forgiving than fard.
3
See the application to sitting in nafil
The author argues that a person may pray nafil sitting even if able to stand, because requiring standing could cause hardship and discourage the prayer. The maxim provides the basis for this leniency.
This ruling applies to all nafil prayers, not just specific ones.
4
Recognize the thamarah (practical consequence)
The practical result is that sitting is permissible, though standing remains better. This balances encouragement with the ideal of standing when possible.
Other schools may differ; some require standing if able.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إِنَّ الصَّلَاةَ خَيْرُ مَوْضُوعِ . ترجمہ: نماز بہترین موضوع ہے۔ تشریح: مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ نماز خیر موضوع ہے یعنی بندے کے لئے یہ نیکی اس طرح مہیا کر دی گئی ہے کہ جمیع اوقات میں حاصل کر سکتا ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کرنے کے بعد اس بات کو ثابت کر رہے ہیں کہ آدمی نفل کھڑے ہونے پر قدرت کے باوجود بیٹھ کر پڑھ سکتا ہے کیونکہ نماز خیر موضوع ہے، اور بسا اوقات انسان پر کھڑا ہونا شاق گزرتا ہے تو اب اس کے لئے قیام کو ترک کرنا جائز ہے، کیونکہ اگر نفل نماز میں قیام کی شرط لگائی جائے تو یہ نفل نماز کو چھوڑنے کا باعث اور سبب ہوسکتا ہے۔
Verily, prayer is the best thing placed (before one). Translation: Prayer is the best subject. Explanation: The meaning of the mentioned principle is that prayer is the best thing placed, i.e., for the servant, this good deed is made available in such a way that he can attain it at all times. The author of Al-Hidayah, after mentioning this principle, is proving that a person may pray nafil sitting despite ability to stand, because prayer is the best thing placed, and sometimes standing is burdensome for a person, so it is permissible for him to abandon standing, because if standing were made a condition in nafil prayer, it would cause and lead to abandoning nafil prayer.
Source pages p. 124

Commentary
This lesson presents a key principle from Al-Hidayah: 'Prayer is the best thing placed (before a person),' meaning it is an easily accessible good deed. The commentator explains that the author uses this principle to justify the permissibility of sitting in nafil prayers even when one is able to stand. The rationale is to remove hardship and encourage performing nafil prayers. If standing were required, some might abandon the prayer altogether. Thus, in the Hanafi school, sitting in nafil is allowed, though standing is better. This is an application of the maxim that ease is considered in nafil acts.

Key Terms
خير موضوع (khayru mawdu'in): The best thing set before one; a description of prayer indicating its easy accessibility.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Not allowed; standing is obligatory in all prayers
B) Allowed, but standing is better
C) Allowed only if one is sick or elderly
D) Not allowed because it reduces reward

Key Takeaway
The maxim 'Prayer is the best thing placed before one' allows sitting in nafil prayer to avoid hardship and encourage worship.

Principle 108: Nafil Prayer is the Best Appointed Thing (Al-Salat Khayr Mawdu')
Commentary on a usul principle with dalil and intra-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi principle that prayer is the best appointed thing, explain why sitting in nafil is permissible even with ability to stand, and identify the intra-Hanafi dispute on qada when recitation is left in nafil prayer.

Core Idea
Prayer is the best appointed thing – thus nafil prayer is facilitated so it is never abandoned.

This lesson unpacks the first principle from Usool-e-Hidayah: 'Indeed prayer is the best appointed thing.' We will see how this principle justifies the permissibility of sitting in nafil prayer even when one is able to stand, and we will explore an intra-Hanafi dispute about making up missed rak'at when recitation is omitted. The principle acts as a legal maxim (qa'idah) that informs several rulings in the chapter of prayer.

Guided Path
1
Understand the principle
The principle 'al-salat khayr mawdu'' means prayer is the best thing appointed for the servant, available at all times. It implies that prayer should be made easy to perform.
2
Apply the principle to sitting in nafil
Because prayer is the best, it should not be made difficult. Standing can be burdensome; if it were a condition, people might abandon nafil. So sitting is allowed even with ability to stand, as the text states: 'If standing were made a condition in nafil prayer, it could become a cause for abandoning nafil prayer.'
This applies only to nafil, not to fard or witr.
3
Identify the hadith evidence
The hadith 'Whoever prays standing, that is better; whoever prays sitting, he has half the reward' proves the permission for nafil. The hadith to 'Imran ibn Husayn (Pray standing; if not, then sitting) shows standing is obligatory for fard but not for nafil.
The exception 'except with an excuse' in another narration clarifies that sitting without excuse reduces reward but is still valid for nafil.
4
Examine the dispute on qada
If one leaves recitation in the first two rak'at of a four-rak'at nafil, Abu Hanifa and Muhammad say only the first two rak'at are invalid and must be made up; Abu Yusuf says all four must be made up. The reasoning turns on whether the takbir al-tahrimah becomes invalid when the acts it was contracted for are corrupted.
The text explains: according to the majority, the takbir is invalid, so starting the second pair is not valid. Abu Yusuf analogizes to the illiterate person's valid prayer without recitation.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The text favors the view of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad (two rak'at qada) as the relied-upon position. The tarjih is based on the principle that the takbir is contracted for the specific acts.
This dispute does not affect the general ruling on sitting in nafil, which is unanimous among the Hanafis.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اصول ہدایہ جلد اول کی قضا کرے گا۔ طرفین کے نزدیک شفع اول میں ترک قراءت کی وجہ سے تحریمہ باطل ہوگئی ، تو اب شفع ثانی کا شروع کرنا درست نہیں ہوا ، پس گویا اس نے دو رکعت کے لئے تحریمہ باندھی تھی اور اسی کو فاسد کیا تو اس پر دو رکعت کی قضاء واجب ہے، چونکہ امام ابو یوسف رحمہ اللہ کے نزدیک تحریمہ باطل نہیں ہوئی لہذا اشفع ثانی کو شروع کرنا صحیح ہے، لیکن ترک قراءت کی وجہ سے چاروں رکعتیں فاسد ہو گئیں اس لئے چاروں کی قضاء واجب ہے۔

(۱۰۸) إِنَّ الصَّلَاةَ خَيْرُ مَوْضُوعِ .

ترجمہ: نماز بہترین موضوع ہے۔

تشریح: مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ نماز خیر موضوع ہے یعنی بندے کے لئے یہ نیکی اس طرح مہیا کر دی گئی ہے کہ جمیع اوقات میں حاصل کر سکتا ہے۔

صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کرنے کے بعد اس بات کو ثابت کر رہے ہیں کہ آدمی نفل کھڑے ہونے پر قدرت کے باوجود بیٹھ کر پڑھ سکتا ہے کیونکہ نماز خیر موضوع ہے، اور بسا اوقات انسان پر کھڑا ہونا شاق گزرتا ہے تو اب اس کے لئے قیام کو ترک کرنا جائز ہے، کیونکہ اگر نفل نماز میں قیام کی شرط لگائی جائے تو یہ نفل نماز کو چھوڑنے کا باعث اور سبب ہوسکتا ہے۔ حاصل یہ ہے کہ نفل نماز غیر واجب ہے اور جو چیز اس انداز پر ہو اس میں ایسی شرط نہیں لگائی جاتی جو اس کے (وَكَذَا الْخِلافُ لَوْ جَرَّدَ الْأَرْبَعَ عَنْ الْقِرَاءَةِ) أَى يَقْضِى رَكْعَتَيْنِ عِنْدَهُمَا لِأَنَّ أَفْعَالَ الصَّلَاةِ لَمَّا فَسَدَتْ بِتَرْكِ الْقِرَاءةِ بَطَلَتْ التَّحْرِيمَةُ لِأَنَّهَا إِنَّمَا انْعَقَدَتْ لِأُجُلِهَا فَلَمْ يَصِحٌ شُرُوعُهُ فِي الشَّفْعِ الثَّانِي فَيَلْزَمُ قَضَاءُ الشَّفْعِ الأَوَّلِ فَقَط وَعِندَ أَبِى يُوسُفَ تَرْكُ الْقِرَاءَةِ لَا يُوجِبُ بُطَلَانَ التَّحْرِيمَةِ لِجَوَازِ صَلَاةِ الْأُمِّيِّ بِلَا قِرَاء وَ فَيَصِحُ شُرُوعُهُ فِي الْأَرْبَعِ فَيَلْزَمُ قَضَاءُ الْأَرْبَعِ لِإِفْسَادِهَا بِتَرْكِ الْقِرَاءَةِ أَوْ قَرَأَ فِي إِحْدَى الْأَخْرَيَيْنِ فَحَسْبُ أَى يَلْزَمُهُ قَضَاءُ رَكْعَتَيْنِ عِنْدَهُمَا وَقَضَاءُ أَرْبَعِ عِنْدَهُ عَلَى قِيَاسِ مَا سَبَقَ.
[مجمع الأنهر : كتاب الصلاة، باب الوتر والنوافل، ج ۱ ص ۱۲۸، ط: دار إحياء التراث] الهداية كتاب الصلاة، باب النوافل، فصل فى القراء ة ، ج ۱ ص ۱۵۶، ط: رحمانیه

اصول ہدایہ جلد اول

چھوڑنے کا سبب ہو، کیونکہ جو ترک خیر کا سبب ہو گا وہ خیر نہیں ہو سکتا اور قیام کی شرط لگانا نفل کے چھوڑنے کا سبب ہو سکتا ہے، کیونکہ بسا اوقات مصلی پر قیام شاق ہوتا ہے، پس اگر قیام کو نفل نماز میں شرط قرار دینے کی صورت میں نفل ہی کا ترک کرنا لازم آئے گا حالانکہ نفل خیر موضوع ہے ،اس لئے نفل نماز کے لئے قیام کی شرط نہیں لگائی جائے گی ۔

وَإِنَّمَا جَازَتْ النَّافِلَةُ قَاعِدًا مَعَ الْقُدْرَةِ عَلَى الْقِيَامِ لِأَنَّ الصَّلَاةَ خَيْرُ مَوْضُوعِ وَرُبَّمَا يَشُقُّ عَلَيْهِ الْقِيَامُ فَجَازَ لَهُ تَرُكُهُ كَى لَا يَنْقَطِعَ عَنْ هَذَا الْخَيْرِ الْمَوْضُوعِ وَقُيِّدَ بِالنَّافِلَةِ احْتِرَازًا عَنْ الْقَرْضِ وَالْوِتْرِ.
الجوهرة النيرة : كتاب الصلاة، باب النوافل، ج ا ص ۷۴، ط: المطبعة الخيرية ] وَيَتَنَفَّلُ قَاعِدًا مَعَ الْقُدْرَةِ عَلَى الْقِيَامِ ابْتِدَاءً وَبِنَاءً أَمَّا الابْتِدَاء فَلِقَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ الصَّلَاةُ وَالسَّلَامُ مَنْ صَلَّى قَائِمًا فَهُوَ أَفْضَلُ وَمَنْ صَلَّى قَاعِدًا فَلَهُ نِصْفُ أَجْرِ الْقَائِمِ وَالْمُرَادُ بِهِ النَّفَلُ فِي غَيْرِ حَالَةِ الْعُذْرِ بِدَلِيلِ قَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ الصَّلَاةُ وَالسَّلَامُ صَلَاةُ الْقَاعِدِ عَلَى النِّصْفِ مِنْ صَلَاةِ الْقَائِمِ إِلَّا مِنْ عُذْرٍ وَالْفَرْضُ لَا يَجُوزُ أَنْ يُصَلَّى قَاعِدًا مِنْ غَيْرِ عُذْرٍ بِدَلِيلِ قَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ الصَّلَاةُ وَالسَّلَامُ لِعِمْرَانَ بنِ حُصَيْنٍ صَلِّ قَائِمًا فَإِنْ لَمْ تَسْتَطِعُ فَقَاعِدًا الْحَدِيثَ ، فَتَعَيَّنَ النَّفَلُ مُرَادًا مَعَ الْقُدْرَةِ عَلَى الْقِيَامِ وَلانَّ الصَّلَاةَ خَيْرُ مَوْضُوعِ فَرُبَّمَا يَشُقُّ عَلَيْهِ الْقِيَامُ فَجَازَ تَرْكُهُ كَيْ لَا يَتْرُكَهُ أَصْلًا.
تبيين الحقائق: كتاب الصلاة، باب الوتر والنوافل، ج ا ص ٦ ا ، ا ، ط: دار الكتاب الإسلامي] الهداية كتاب الصلاة، باب النوافل، فصل فى القراء ة ، ج ۱ ص ۱۵۶، ط: رحمانیه
The principle of Usool-e-Hidayah will judge: According to both (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), in the first pair, due to leaving recitation, the takbir al-tahrimah becomes invalid, so starting the second pair is not correct. So it is as if he bound the takbir for two rak'at and invalidated that, so making up two rak'at is obligatory. Since according to Imam Abu Yusuf (may Allah have mercy on him) the takbir al-tahrimah did not become invalid, starting the second pair is valid, but due to leaving recitation, all four rak'at become invalid, so making up all four is obligatory.

(108) Indeed prayer is the best appointed thing.

Translation: Prayer is the best thing.

Explanation: The meaning of the aforementioned principle is that prayer is the best thing, meaning that this goodness is made available for the servant such that he can obtain it at all times.

The author of Hidayah, after mentioning the aforementioned principle, is proving that a person can pray nafil sitting even if able to stand, because prayer is the best appointed thing, and sometimes standing is arduous for a person, so for him abandoning standing is permissible, because if standing were made a condition in nafil prayer, it could become a cause and reason for abandoning nafil prayer. The conclusion is that nafil prayer is non-obligatory, and something that is of this nature is not conditioned with a condition that would become a cause for its (abandonment). (And likewise the difference if he separated the four from recitation) meaning he makes up two rak'at according to them (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) because when the actions of prayer become corrupted by leaving recitation, the takbir al-tahrimah becomes invalid because it was only contracted for their sake, so his beginning of the second pair is not correct, so only the making up of the first pair is necessary. And according to Abu Yusuf, leaving recitation does not necessitate the invalidity of the takbir al-tahrimah because of the permissibility of the prayer of the illiterate person without recitation, so his beginning of the four is valid, so making up all four is necessary due to its corruption by leaving recitation. And if he recited in only the two others (i.e., the last two), then according to them (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) he must make up two rak'at, and according to him (Abu Yusuf) he must make up four, in analogy to what preceded.

[References]

Then why nafil prayer is permitted sitting with ability to stand is that prayer is the best appointed thing, and perhaps standing is arduous for him, so it is permissible for him to abandon it so that he does not become cut off from this appointed good. And it is restricted to nafil as a precaution regarding fard and witr.
Al-Jawhara al-Nayyira: ... He prays nafil sitting with ability to stand initially and by way of building. As for initially, due to his statement (peace and blessings be upon him): Whoever prays standing, that is better, and whoever prays sitting, he has half the reward of the one who stands. And what is meant by it is nafil in a non-excused state, as evidence by his statement (peace and blessings be upon him): The prayer of the sitting is half of the prayer of the standing, except with an excuse. And fard is not permissible to be prayed sitting without an excuse, as evidence by his statement (peace and blessings be upon him) to 'Imran ibn Husayn: Pray standing, and if you cannot, then sitting... So nafil is determined to be intended with ability to stand, and because prayer is the best appointed thing, so perhaps standing is arduous for him, so it is permissible to abandon it so that he does not leave it altogether.
Tabyin al-Haqa'iq: ...
Source pages p. 124

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the first principle (108) from Usool-e-Hidayah. The passage opens with an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning making up missed rak'at in nafil prayer when one abandons recitation (qira'ah) in the first two rak'at of a four-rak'at nafil. According to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), if one leaves recitation in the first two rak'at, the takbir al-tahrimah becomes invalid because it was contracted for those specific actions. Hence, starting the second pair is not valid, and only the first two rak'at need to be made up. Imam Abu Yusuf disagrees: he holds that leaving recitation does not invalidate the takbir because the prayer of an illiterate person without recitation is valid. Therefore, the entire four-rak'at prayer becomes corrupted, and all four must be made up. The text then states the principle: 'Indeed prayer is the best appointed thing.' The author explains that this means prayer is a great good made readily available to the servant. Building on this principle, the author of Hidayah proves that one may perform nafil prayer sitting even when able to stand. Because standing is sometimes burdensome, and if it were a condition, it might discourage people from praying nafil altogether. Since nafil is not obligatory, it should not be burdened with conditions that could lead to its abandonment. The Arabic quotes from Majma' al-Anhur, Al-Jawhara al-Nayyira, and Tabyin al-Haqa'iq further support this: the Prophet (peace be upon him) said that a sitting prayer has half the reward of a standing one except for an excuse, and for fard, standing is required unless unable. Thus, the permission for nafil to be prayed sitting is to prevent the person from leaving the prayer entirely due to hardship.

Key Terms
خير موضوع (khayr mawdu'): Here it means that prayer is the best thing that has been appointed or created for the servant to obtain good deeds easily.
نفل (nafil): Supererogatory prayer, non-obligatory acts of worship that earn reward.
قیام (qiyam): Standing in prayer. Here it is discussed as a condition for fard but not for nafil in the Hanafi school.
تحریمہ (tahrimah): The initial takbir (takbir al-tahrimah) that enters one into the state of prayer. Its validity condition is discussed in the dispute.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is it permissible to pray nafil sitting even if one can stand?
A) Because sitting is equal to standing in reward.
B) Because standing is not a condition for nafil; the principle 'prayer is the best appointed thing' facilitates it to prevent abandonment.
C) Because the Prophet (peace be upon him) always prayed nafil sitting.
D) Because nafil prayer is invalid if prayed standing.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi principle that prayer is the best appointed thing facilitates nafil worship by removing conditions that might lead to its abandonment, such as requiring standing, and governs related rulings like qada for omitted recitation.

Nafil Prayers Are Not Time-Specific
Commentary on a principle from Hidayah about nafil prayers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi principle that nafil prayers are permissible at any time and apply it to the scenario of a traveler praying on a mount.

Core Idea
Nafil prayers can be performed at any time, even when travel or conditions prevent full fard prayer.

In this lesson, we examine a fundamental principle of Hanafi fiqh: nafil (supererogatory) prayers are not tied to specific times. Unlike the five daily fard prayers, which have fixed windows, nawafil may be offered at virtually any moment. The author of al-Hidayah uses this rule to explain why a traveler may pray nafil on his mount, regardless of direction, without the usual conditions of facing qibla or performing full postures.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
Read the principle: 'Indeed nafil prayers are not restricted to time.' This is the ruling—nawafil are flexible in time.
This is a general rule with some exceptions (the three prohibited times).
2
Understand the Scope
The principle means nafil can be performed at any time of day or night, unlike fard prayers which have specific prescribed times.
The three prohibited times (sunrise, zenith, sunset) still prohibit any prayer, including nafil.
3
Apply to the Example
The author of Hidayah cites a traveler outside the city who prays nafil on his mount. This is permissible even if the mount faces any direction, showing that nafil does not require facing qibla when traveling? Actually, the example is about permissibility when one cannot dismount.
The full passage is cut off, but the point is that nafil can be performed even with reduced conditions.
4
Distinguish from Fard
Contrast this with fard prayers: they must be performed in their specific times, facing qibla, and with full postures unless an excuse exists.
Nafil prayers enjoy leniency in time, place, and manner.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۱۰۹) إِنَّ النَّوَافِلَ غَيْرُ مُخْتَصَّةٍ بِوَقْتِ .

ترجمہ : نوافل کسی وقت کے ساتھ مخصوص نہیں ہیں۔

تشریح : مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ نوافل کسی وقت کے ساتھ مختص نہیں ہیں بلکہ ہمہ اوقات میں ادا کئے جاسکتے ہیں۔ صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کرنے کے بعد اس بات کو ثابت کر رہے ہیں کہ اگر مسافر آدمی شہر سے باہر نفل نماز سواری پر پڑھتا ہے تو یہ جائز ہے، چاہے عذر ہو یا نہ ہواورسواری جس جہت کی
(109) Indeed nafil prayers are not restricted to time. Translation: Nafil prayers are not specific to any time. Explanation: The meaning of the mentioned principle is that nafil prayers are not confined to a particular time, rather they can be performed at all times. The author of Hidayah, after mentioning the principle, is proving that if a traveling person outside the city performs nafil prayer on his mount, it is permissible, whether there is an excuse or not, and the mount [to whichever direction]
Source pages p. 125

Commentary
This passage introduces the second principle: nafil prayers are not restricted to specific times. The author comments that nafil can be performed at any time. The example from Hidayah is that a traveler outside the city may pray nafil on his mount, regardless of the direction, and this is valid. This is to illustrate the permissibility of nafil at times when one would not be able to perform the full prayer with all conditions. The passage is incomplete, but the key point is the flexibility of nafil in terms of time and conditions.

Key Terms
نوافل (nawafil): Plural of nafil, supererogatory prayers. Here meaning optional prayers not bound to specific times.
مختص (mukhtass): To be specific or confined to a particular thing. Here it means nafil is not restricted to any specific time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Nafil prayers are only valid if prayed at night.

C) Nafil prayers must be prayed on a mount.
D) Nafil prayers are only for travelers.

Key Takeaway
Nafil prayers are flexible and can be performed at any time, except for the three prohibited times of sunrise, zenith, and sunset.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Nawafil Are Not Restricted to a Specific Time
Establishes permissibility of nafl prayer on mount outside city without qiblah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on performing nafl prayer on a mount without facing qiblah and explain the evidence and reasoning behind it.

Core Idea
Nawafil are not time-bound; they can be performed anytime, even on a mount without qiblah.

This lesson examines a key principle from Usool al-Hidayah: nawafil (supererogatory prayers) are not restricted to specific times. The author applies this to allow a traveler to pray nafl on his mount outside the city without dismounting or facing the qiblah, whether he has an excuse or not. By studying the hadith and the rationale that prayer is a good act not to be hindered, we understand the Hanafi emphasis on facilitating worship.

Guided Path
1
State the principle
Identify the core statement: 'Indeed nawafil are not restricted to a time.' This is the foundational rule.
The Arabic: إِنَّ النَّوَافِلَ غَيْرُ مُخْتَصَّةٍ بِوَقْتِ
2
Identify the application
The Hidayah applies this rule to a traveler praying nafl on a mount outside the city. The ruling: it is permissible to pray without facing qiblah, even without an excuse.
The mount's direction does not matter.
3
Find the dalil (evidence)
The proof includes the hadith: 'Whoever prays standing is best; whoever prays sitting has half the reward.' This shows flexibility in nafl. Also, the general principle that prayer is a good act.
Hadith from 'Imran ibn Husayn, quoted in Al-Jawharah.
4
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith indicates that sitting is permissible in nafl even when able to stand, demonstrating that nafl is not bound by strict conditions like fard. The reasoning (ta'lil) is that imposing hardship might cause abandonment of the good deed.
The text says: 'so that he does not cut off from this good act.'
5
Note the cross-madhhab ikhtilaf
The Shafi'i school generally requires facing qiblah for all prayers, including nafl. The Hanafi school allows departure (istihsan) based on the hadith and the principle of not hindering good.
This is a legitimate difference (mukhtalaf fih).

(Reason for leaving: that which causes leaving good cannot be good, and stipulating standing could cause leaving nafl because sometimes standing is burdensome; so if standing is made a condition for nafl prayer, it would necessitate leaving nafl, whereas nafl is a good act. Therefore standing is not made a condition for nafl prayer. (109) Indeed nawafil are not restricted to a time. Translation: Nawafil are not specific to any time. Explanation: The meaning of this principle is that nawafil are not restricted to a time; rather they can be performed at all times. And nafl is permitted while sitting even when able to stand because prayer is a good act; sometimes standing is burdensome, so he is allowed to leave it so that he does not cut off from this good act. It is restricted to nafl to exclude fard and witr. Al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah: Book of Salah, Chapter of Nawafil, vol.1 p.74: He prays nafl sitting even when able to stand, initially and continuously. As for initially, because the Prophet (SAW) said: 'Whoever prays standing is best; whoever prays sitting has half the reward of the standing.' This refers to nafl without excuse; the proof is his saying: 'The prayer of the sitting is half of the prayer of the standing, except due to an excuse.' And fard is not permitted to be prayed sitting without excuse, as the Prophet (SAW) said to 'Imran ibn Husayn: 'Pray standing; if you cannot, then sitting.' So nafl is intended when able to stand. And because prayer is a good act, sometimes standing is burdensome, so leaving it is permitted so that he does not leave it entirely. Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from Usool al-Hidayah. It states the principle that supererogatory prayers (nawafil) are not time-bound. The author explains that this principle permits a traveler to pray nafl on his mount outside the city without dismounting or facing the qiblah, excused or not. The proof includes the hadith about sitting in prayer and the reasoning that prayer is a good act; imposing conditions that lead to abandoning it would defeat the purpose. The passage then quotes from Al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah and Tabyin al-Haqa'iq to support the permissibility of sitting in nafl and the ruling that fard is not permitted without excuse. The emphasis is on maintaining the performance of good deeds by removing unnecessary hardships.

Key Terms
نوافل (nawafil): Supererogatory prayers; non-obligatory prayers performed for extra reward.
مختصة بوقت (mukhtaṣṣah biwaqt): Restricted to a specific time; i.e., cannot be performed before or after the prescribed time.
