The Fard Does Not Repeat: Joining a Congregation After Starting Alone
Explaining the principle and its application to a missed congregational prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle 'al-fard la yatakarrar fi waqt wahid' to determine the correct course of action when a person performing a fard prayer individually is joined by a congregation for the same prayer.

Core Idea
A fard prayer once begun must be completed; it cannot be repeated in the same time, so joining the congregation after completing most of it makes the second prayer nafl.

In this lesson, we examine a practical scenario: you are praying Zuhr alone, have completed three rak'ahs, and then a congregation for Zuhr starts. What should you do? The answer lies in the Hanafi legal principle that a fard obligation does not repeat in a single time. We will parse the reasoning, apply the principle, and see how it determines whether your subsequent prayer is fard or nafl.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Principle
State the principle: 'Al-fard la yatakarrar fi waqt wahid' (The fard does not repeat in one time). Understand that this means you cannot perform the same obligatory prayer twice within the same time window.
This principle is a corollary of the fact that once an obligation is fulfilled, it is not due again.
2
Recognize the Scenario
Consider the specific case: a person has individually performed three rak'ahs of a four-rak'ah fard prayer (e.g., Zuhr) when a congregation for the same prayer is established.
The person has already done the majority (akthar) of the prayer.
3
Apply the 'Majority Stands for the Whole' Rule
The Hanafi principle 'al-akthar yanuzulu manzilatal kull' (the majority takes the place of the whole) is invoked. Because three out of four rak'ahs (the majority) have been completed, the original fard is considered nearly fulfilled. It would be improper to abandon it; instead, the person must complete the remaining one rak'ah to finalize the fard.
This rule is used to avoid leaving an obligation incomplete.
4
Determine the Ruling
Since the original fard has been completed (by doing the fourth rak'ah), the subsequent prayer with the congregation cannot be another fard (because fard does not repeat). Hence, the prayer with the imam is nafl (supererogatory). The person joins the congregation after finishing his individual prayer, and his intention for the prayer with the imam should be nafl.
If he had not yet performed the sajdah of the third rak'ah (i.e., only two rak'ahs done), he would stop after two, make taslim, and join the congregation with the intention of fard. In that case, the first two rak'ahs become nafl.
5
Contrast with the Exception
Notice the exception: if the person has done less than the majority (e.g., only two rak'ahs without the third sajdah), he can terminate his individual prayer and join the congregation for fard, because the original fard is not yet substantially commenced. The earlier rak'ahs then count as nafl.
This is consistent with the principle: since the fard was not yet established (majority not reached), it can be replaced.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب إدراك الفريضة
( ١١٠ ) إِنَّ الْفَرْضَ لَا يَتَكَرَّرُ فِي وَقْتِ وَاحِدٍ.
ترجمہ: فرض ایک وقت میں مکرر نہیں ہوتا۔
تشریح: مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ ایک ہی وقت میں فرض مکرر نہیں ہوتا یعنی ایک وقت میں ایک ہی فرض کو دو مر تبہ ادا کرنا درست نہیں ہے۔
صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول کو ذکر کرنے کے بعد اس بات کو ثابت کرنا چاہتے ہیں کہ اگر ایک آدمی انفرادی طور پر مثلا ظہر کی تین رکعت پڑھ چکا تھا پھر جماعت کھڑی ہوگئی تو اب یہ شخص اپنی چار رکعت کو پورا کرے اور پھر لوگوں کے ساتھ جماعت میں شامل ہو جائے ، اس لئے کہ یہ شخص ظہر کی اکثر نماز پڑھ چکا ہے اور اکثر کل کے قائم مقام ہوتا ہے ،صرف ایک رکعت باقی ہے اسے مکمل کر کے جماعت میں شامل ہو ، اب امام کے ساتھ اس کی یہ نماز نفل ہوگی نہ کہ فرض ، کیونکہ فرض تو یہ ایک مرتبہ پڑھ چکا ہے اور مذکورہ قاعدے کی بنیاد پر فرض میں تکرار جائز نہیں ہے، لہذا اس کی یہ جماعت کے ساتھ نماز نفل ہی ہوگی نہ کہ فرض ۔ برخلاف اس کے تیسری رکعت کا سجدہ نہ کیا ہو تو دو رکعت پر سلام پھیر دے اور جماعت کے ساتھ فرض نماز میں شامل ہو جائے ، اب پہلی دو رکعتیں نفل ہو جائیں گی ، اور جماعت کے ساتھ نماز فرض ہو گی۔
(وَرَاكِبًا خَارِجَ الْمِصْرِ مُومِيَّا إِلَى أَى جِهَةِ تَوَجَّهَتْ دَابَّتُهُ) أَيْ وَيَتَنَفَّلُ رَاكِبًا لِحَدِيثِ جَابِرٍ أَنَّهُ قَالَ رَأَيْتُ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ يُصَلَّى وَهُوَ عَلَى رَاحِلَتِهِ النَّوَافِلَ فِي كُلِّ جِهَةٍ لَكِنْ يَخْفِضُ السُّجُودَ مِنْ الرُّكُوعِ وَيُومِنُ إِيمَاء وَلَانَّ النَّوَافِلَ غَيْرَ مُخْتَصَّةٍ بِوَقْتٍ فَلَوْ أَلْزَمْنَاهُ النُّزُولَ وَاسْتِقْبَالَ الْقِبْلَةِ تَنْقَطِعُ عَنْهُ النَّافِلَةُ أَوْ يَنْقَطِعُ هُوَ عَنْ الْقَافِلَةِ، وَأَمَّا الْفَرَائِضُ فَمُخْتَصَّةٌ بِوَقْتِ فَلا تَجُوزُ عَلَى الدَّابَّةِ إِلَّا لِلضَّرُورَةِ.
[تبيين الحقائق كتاب الصلاة، باب الوتر والنوافل، ج ۱ ص ۱۷۷، ط: دار الكتاب الإسلامي]
الهداية كتاب الصلاة، باب إدراك القريضة، ج ۱ ص ۱۵۸، ط: رحمانيه
Chapter: Perceiving the Obligatory Prayer (110) Indeed, the fard does not repeat in one time. Translation: The fard is not repeated in one time. Explanation: The meaning of the aforementioned principle is that the fard is not repeated in one time, meaning it is not correct to perform the same fard twice in one time. The author of al-Hidayah, after mentioning the aforementioned principle, wants to prove that if a person individually, for example, has prayed three rak'ahs of Zuhr, then a congregation is established, then this person should complete his four rak'ahs and then join the congregation with the people, because this person has prayed the majority of the Zuhr prayer, and the majority stands in place of the whole. Only one rak'ah remains. He completes it and joins the congregation. Now his prayer with the imam will be nafl, not fard, because he has already prayed the fard once, and based on the mentioned rule, repetition in fard is not permissible. Therefore, his prayer with the congregation will only be nafl, not fard. Contrary to this, if he has not done the sajdah of the third rak'ah, then he should say taslim after two rak'ahs and join the congregation for the fard prayer. Now the first two rak'ahs will become nafl, and the prayer with the congregation will be fard. (And a rider outside the city, pointing to whichever direction his mount turns) i.e., he prays nafl while riding, based on the hadith of Jabir who said: I saw the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) praying on his mount, the nawafil, in every direction, but he makes the prostration lower than the bowing, and he gestures by nodding. And because nawafil are not specific to a time, so if we oblige him to dismount and face the qibla, the nafl would be cut off from him, or he would be cut off from the caravan. As for the obligatory prayers, they are specific to a time, so they are not permissible on an animal except in necessity. [Tabyin al-Haqa'iq, Book of Prayer, Chapter of Witr and Nawafil, vol. 1 p. 177, Dar al-Kitab al-Islami] al-Hidayah, Book of Prayer, Chapter of Perceiving the Obligatory Prayer, vol. 1 p. 158, Rahmaniyyah
Source pages p. 126

Commentary
This is a ruling with a supporting citation from al-Hidayah. The passage opens with the principle 'The fard does not repeat in one time' and then explains its application to a common scenario: a person who has individually prayed three rak'ahs of Zuhr when a congregation for the same prayer begins. According to the Hanafi school, since he has performed the majority of the fard (three out of four rak'ahs), he must complete his prayer (the fourth rak'ah) to finish his original fard. He then joins the congregation, but his prayer with the imam is considered nafl, not fard, because fard cannot be repeated in the same time. If he had not yet performed the sajdah of the third rak'ah, he should instead stop after two rak'ahs (by doing taslim), and then join the congregation for a new fard prayer; in that case, the first two rak'ahs become nafl. The passage then includes an Arabic quotation from Tabyin al-Haqa'iq (about a traveler praying nafl on his mount without facing the qibla) which supports the general principle that nafl prayers are flexible in time and place, while fard prayers are specific. Both citations are from Hanafi sources, reinforcing the ruling.

Key Terms
فرض (fard): The obligatory act that must be performed; in this context, the obligatory prayer (Zuhr).
نفل (nafl): Supererogatory voluntary prayer; in this passage, the second prayer performed with the imam after already completing the fard.
تکرار (takrar): Repetition; here it means performing the same fard prayer twice in the same time.
اکثر (akthar): Majority; in Hanafi legal theory, the majority of an act often stands in place of the whole (al-akthar yanuzulu manzilatal kull).
قاعدہ (qa'idah): Principle or rule; here it refers to the rule 'fard does not repeat'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A person is praying Zuhr individually and has completed three rak'ahs. A congregation for Zuhr then starts. According to the Hanafi principle 'إن الفرض لا يتكرر في وقت واحد', what should he do?
A) Break his prayer after three rak'ahs and join the congregation as a follower.
B) Complete the fourth rak'ah of his prayer, then join the congregation as a nafl follower.
C) Join the congregation immediately without completing his prayer, and his three rak'ahs will be nafl.
D) Complete his prayer alone and not join the congregation.

Key Takeaway
The principle 'fard does not repeat' ensures that once a fard prayer is substantially performed (majority completed), it must be completed; subsequent participation in congregation is considered nafl, not fard.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Qada is Specific to the Wajib – Making Up Sunnah Prayers
Stating the principle that qada is for wajib only, with an exception for Fajr sunnah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi principle that qada applies only to wajib prayers and identify the exception for the Fajr sunnah.

Core Idea
Missed sunnah prayers are not made up — only the wajib obligates qada.

In the Hanafi school, the act of making up a missed prayer (qada) is tied exclusively to obligations (fard and wajib). Supererogatory prayers (sunnah and nafl) are not subject to qada. However, there is a notable exception for the sunnah of Fajr when it is missed together with the fard. This lesson unpacks this principle, its evidence, and its practical application.

Guided Path
1
State the principle
Identify the core statement: 'Inna al-qada ikhtassa bil-wajib' (qada is specific to wajib). Understand that this means qada is only for obligatory prayers, not voluntary ones.
2
Analyze the definition of qada
Qada is defined as 'delivering the like of what was obligated by command' (mithl ma wajaba bil-amr). Since sunnah prayers are not commanded with the same level of obligation, they cannot be 'made up' in this sense.
This is a linguistic-legal argument grounding the principle.
3
Apply to the Fajr sunnah
Consider the scenario: a person misses only the two rak'ahs of Fajr sunnah (performs the fard on time). According to the Shaykhayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani), he should not make them up at any time, because they are sunnah.
Some narrations suggest Abu Hanifa differed, but the relied-upon position is with the Shaykhayn.
4
Identify the exception
If the entire Fajr prayer (fard and sunnah) is missed, the sunnah is made up as a follow-up (taba'an) to the fard. This is based on the hadith of the night of camping at the caravan.
The exception proves the rule: qada for sunnah is only allowed when attached to a wajib.
5
Compare with other schools
Other schools, like the Shafi'i, require qada for all missed prayers, including sunnah. The Hanafi position is more restrictive, based on the principle that only obligations create a duty to make up.
The thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference) is clear: a Hanafi does not make up a missed sunnah in most cases, while a Shafi'i does.

(111) Indeed, qada is specific to the wajib. Translation: Qada is specific to the wajib. Explanation: The meaning of the aforementioned principle is that qada (making up) is specific only to fard and wajib, not to nawafil, i.e., there is no qada for nawafil. The author of al-Hidayah, after mentioning the aforementioned principle, is proving that if a person misses the two rak'ahs of sunnah of Fajr, then according to the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf or the Shaykhayn?), he should not make them up before sunrise nor after sunrise, because it is sunnah, and based on the mentioned principle, qada is specific to obligatory prayer (salat wajibah), not to sunan and nawafil. Therefore, he should not make up these sunnan. Qada is specific to wajib because qada is the name for delivering the equivalent of what was obligated by command. Since these (sunnan) are not wajib, how can delivering the equivalent of wajib be realized? (His saying: And if he prayed three, he completes and follows as a volunteer) Because the majority has the ruling of the whole, so it cannot tolerate nullification. And he only follows as a volunteer because the fard does not repeat in one time. And it is stated in al-Hawi al-Qudsi that what is performed with the imam is nafl, by which he attains the virtue of congregation, and Asr does not apply to him because after it he does not follow, as known from the chapter of disliked times. For this reason, he restricted it to Zuhr and restricted it to three, because if he was in the third and did not restrict it with sajdah, then he cuts it off because he is in a position of rejection. (Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: Book of Prayer, Chapter of Perceiving the Obligatory Prayer, vol. 2 p. 78, Dar al-Kitab al-Islami) al-Hidayah, Book of Prayer, Chapter of Perceiving the Obligatory Prayer, vol. 1 p. 120, Rahmaniyyah. (His saying: And it is not made up except as a follow-up) i.e., the sunnah of Fajr is not made up except if it is missed together with the fard, then it is made up as a follow-up to the fard, whether he makes it up with the congregation or alone, because the original rule regarding sunnah is that it is not made up due to the specificity of qada to wajib, and the hadith came regarding its qada as a follow-up to the fard on the morning of the night of camping at the caravan, so what remains beyond that is upon the original rule. (Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: Book of Prayer, Chapter of Perceiving the Obligatory Prayer, vol. 2 p. 80, Dar al-Kitab al-Islami)
Source pages p. 127

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi principle that qada (making up a missed prayer) is only required for obligatory prayers (fard and wajib), not for sunnah or nafl prayers. The author explains the principle in Urdu and then provides an example: if a person misses the two-rak'ah sunnah of Fajr, according to the two shaykhs (likely Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, or the two primary figures of the school), he should not make it up at any time—neither before sunrise (if he wakes up just before sunrise) nor after sunrise—because it is sunnah, and qada is only for wajib. The reasoning is that qada means performing the equivalent of what was obligated by the divine command; since sunnah prayers are not commanded with the same level of obligation, they cannot have a qada. The Arabic quotes from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq and al-Hidayah further elaborate: firstly, a reiteration of the principle from a different context (the case of one who has prayed three rak'ahs and joins as a volunteer), and secondly, an exception: the sunnah of Fajr can be made up only if it was missed together with the fard (i.e., if the whole Fajr prayer was missed), in which case it is made up as a follow-up to the fard, based on the hadith of the night of camping at the caravan. This exception is limited to that specific scenario.

Key Terms
قضاء (qada): Making up a missed prayer or act after its prescribed time has passed.
واجب (wajib): An obligatory act that is established by a probable (zanni) evidence; in this context, it includes both fard and wajib.
سنت (sunnah): A recommended practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him); here specifically the two rak'ahs before Fajr fard.
نفل (nafl): Voluntary, supererogatory prayer.
شیخین (shaykhayn): The two shaykhs: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, the primary students of Abu Hanifa.
تبعاً (taba'an): As a follow-up; here it means the sunnah is made up together with the fard when both are missed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following prayers must be made up if missed?
A) The two rak'ahs of Fajr sunnah (when fard is performed on time)
B) The Fajr fard prayer
C) The Duha prayer (a voluntary prayer)
D) Both A and B

Key Takeaway
Qada (making up missed prayers) in the Hanafi school is only required for wajib (obligatory) prayers; sunnah prayers are not made up, except for the Fajr sunnah which can be made up as a follow-up to the fard if both are missed.

The Obligation of Order Between Missed and Current Farḍ Prayers
Stating the obligation of order between qaḍā' prayers and the current farḍ

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of tartīb for ṣāḥib al-tartīb and apply it to a concrete scenario.

Core Idea
A person who remembers his missed prayers must make them up before the current farḍ—order is wājib.

This passage from al-Hidayah introduces a fundamental rule for anyone who has missed prayers and remembers them: the order between missed prayers and the current farḍ prayer is necessary (mustaḥaqq). In the Hanafi school, this necessity is considered wājib for the person who is capable of maintaining order (ṣāḥib al-tartīb). Understanding this principle is crucial for correctly fulfilling one's obligations when making up missed prayers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act: Tartīb (Order)
Recognize that the ruling concerns the sequence in which missed prayers (fawā'it) and the current farḍ prayer should be performed.
2
Identify the Condition: Ṣāḥib al-Tartīb
The ruling applies only to a person who remembers his missed prayers (i.e., he knows which prayers he missed and how many). The number of missed prayers must not exceed five (according to the later Hanafi view).
If the number exceeds five, the obligation of order is dropped.
3
State the Ruling: Wājib
The term 'mustaḥaqq' in Hanafi terminology indicates wujūb. Therefore, it is wājib for ṣāḥib al-tartīb to observe order.
Violating this wājib, without a valid excuse, is sinful but does not invalidate the current prayer.
4
Apply to a Concrete Example
If a person misses Zuhr prayer and now it is 'Asr time, he must first make up the missed Zuhr (qaḍā') and then perform the current 'Asr farḍ.
If he prays 'Asr first, he commits a sin but his 'Asr prayer is still valid (sahīh). He must still make up Zuhr later.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب قضاء الفوائت
(۱۱۲) إِنَّ التَّرْتِيْبَ بَيْنَ الْفَوَائِتِ وَفَرْضِ الْوَقْتِ مُسْتَحَقٌّ .
ترجمہ: فوت شدہ نمازوں اور وقتی فرض نماز کے درمیان ترتیب ضروری ہے۔
تشریح: مذکورہ اصول کا تعلق صاحب ترتیب کے ساتھ ہے، یعنی صاحب ترتیب کے لئے ضروری ہے کہ وہ اپنی فوت شدہ نماز اور وقتی فرض کے درمیان ترتیب کا لحاظ رکھے یعنی پہلے فوت شدہ نمازوں کی قضا کرے بعد میں فرض وقت کو ادا کرے۔
صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کرنے کے بعد اس بات کو ثابت کر رہے ہیں اگر صاحب ترتیب سے مثلا ظہر کی نماز فوت ہو گئی اور اب عصر کی نماز کا وقت ہے تو مذکورہ اصول کی بنیاد پر پہلے ظہر کی قضا کرے بعد میں فرض وقت یعنی عصر کو ادا کرے۔
Chapter: Making up Missed Prayers (Bāb Qaḍā' al-Fawā'it). (112) Indeed, order (al-tartīb) between missed prayers (al-fawā'it) and the farḍ of the time is necessary (mustaḥaqq). Translation: Order between missed prayers and the current farḍ prayer is necessary. Explanation: The mentioned principle relates to a person who is capable of order (ṣāḥib al-tartīb), i.e., it is necessary for him to observe order between his missed prayer and the current farḍ, meaning he should first make up the missed prayers and then perform the current farḍ. The author of al-Hidayah, after mentioning this principle, proves that if a person of order misses, for example, the Ẓuhr prayer and now it is the time of 'Asr, then based on the mentioned principle, he should first make up Ẓuhr and then perform the current farḍ, i.e., 'Asr.
Source pages p. 128

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement introducing the principle of order (tartīb) between missed prayers and the current farḍ. It begins a new chapter on making up missed prayers. The Arabic principle states: 'Indeed, order between missed prayers and the farḍ of the time is necessary (mustaḥaqq).' The term 'mustaḥaqq' here indicates a requirement, and in the Hanafi school it is considered wājib for the person who is capable of keeping track of his missed prayers (ṣāḥib al-tartīb). The Urdu commentary explains that such a person must observe order: he must pray the missed ones first, then the current farḍ. An example is given: if someone misses Ẓuhr and it is now 'Asr time, he should pray the missed Ẓuhr before praying 'Asr.

Key Terms
التَّرْتِيْبُ (al-tartīb): The obligation to perform missed prayers in sequence before the current farḍ, and to perform the missed prayers in their own chronological order.
الْفَوَائِتُ (al-fawā'it): Missed prayers (plural of fā'itah) that were not performed in their prescribed time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) It is wājib for a person of order (ṣāḥib al-tartīb).
C) It is not required at all.
D) It is fard, and omitting it invalidates the prayer.

Key Takeaway
Order (tartīb) between missed farḍ prayers and the current farḍ is wājib for a person who remembers his missed prayers (ṣāḥib al-tartīb); violating it does not invalidate the current prayer but incurs sin.

When Order Drops: Narrow Time, Forgetfulness, and Many Missed Prayers
Ruling with proof: exceptions to wājib order

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three circumstances that drop the obligation of order (tartīb) between missed prayers and the current farḍ prayer, and apply them to practical scenarios.

Core Idea
Order is wājib but drops when time is too short, you forget, or you have more than six missed prayers.

In the previous lesson, we learned that order between missed prayers and the current farḍ is wājib for the ṣāḥib al-tartīb. However, the Sharīʿa provides relief in three situations to prevent hardship or loss of the current prayer. This passage from Al-Hidayah lists those exceptions, citing the authority of the Hanafi school. Let us examine each exception and its rationale.

Guided Path
1
Identify the basic ruling
The passage begins by stating the default: order is wājib. Confirm that this is the established Hanafi position from previous lessons.
2
List the three exceptions
Read the three causes that drop the order: narrow time (ḍīq al-waqt), forgetfulness (nisyān), and many missed prayers (kathrat al-fawā'it). Note that the number for 'many' is given as six in the text.
Some Hanafi sources say five; the text here says six.
3
Analyze 'narrow time'
Understand that if performing a missed prayer would cause the current farḍ to be missed (e.g., only enough time remains for one prayer), then order is not required. The priority is to save the current prayer.
This is a mercy to prevent missing the current farḍ.
4
Analyze 'forgetfulness'
If the person forgets the missed prayer, they may proceed with the current prayer without making it up first. Once they remember, they must make it up later but the current prayer is valid.
Forgetfulness here means genuinely not remembering at the time.
5
Analyze 'many missed prayers'
When the number of missed prayers exceeds six (or five in some narrations), the obligation of order drops due to hardship. The person may pray the current prayers without making up all missed ones in sequence.
The exact number is a matter of intra-Hanafi detail.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۱۱۳) إِنَّ التَّرْتِيبَ يَسْقُطُ بِضِيقِ الْوَقْتِ وَكَذَا بِالنِّسْيَانِ وَكَثُرَةِ الْفَوَائِتِ.
ترجمہ: وقت کی تنگی نسیان اور فوت شدہ نمازوں کی کثرت کی وجہ سے ترتیب ساقط ہو جاتی ہے۔
تشریح: صاحب ترتیب شخص کی ترتیب تین اسباب سے ساقط ہو جاتی ہے:
۱. جب وقت تنگ ہو یعنی فائتہ نماز میں مشغول ہونے سے وقتی نماز کے فوت ہونے کا اندیشہ ہو۔
۲. فوت شدہ نماز کو بھول جائے۔
۳. فوت شدہ نمازوں کی تعداد چھ (۶) سے زیادہ ہو جائے۔

أَنَّ مُرَاعَا ةَ التَّرْتِيبِ بَيْنَ الْفَوَائِتِ وَبَيْنَ فَرْضِ الْوَقْتِ وَاجِبٌ إِلَّا فِي حَالَةِ النِّسْيَانِ أَوْ ضِيقٍ الْوَقْتِ أَوْ كَثُرَةِ الْفَوَائِتِ.
المبسوط للسرخسى كتاب الصلاة، باب نوادر الصلاة، ج ۲ ص ۸۷]
الهداية: كتاب الصلاة، باب قضاء الفوائت، ج ۱ ص ۱۶۱، ط: رحمانیہ
(113) Indeed, order is dropped due to narrowness of time, and similarly due to forgetfulness and the abundance of missed prayers. Translation: Order is dropped due to narrowness of time, forgetfulness, and the abundance of missed prayers. Explanation: The order of a person of order is dropped due to three causes: 1. When time is narrow, i.e., there is fear of missing the current prayer if occupied with the missed prayer. 2. He forgets the missed prayer. 3. The number of missed prayers exceeds six (6). The author of al-Hidayah, after mentioning this principle, explains that if a person of order misses, for example, Ẓuhr and now it is the last time of 'Asr, if he occupies himself with making up the missed prayer, then... [incomplete]. al-Hidayah: Kitāb al-Ṣalāh, Bāb Qaḍā' al-Fawā'it, vol. 1, p. 161. Indeed, observing order between missed prayers and the farḍ of the time is wājib except in the case of forgetfulness, narrowness of time, or abundance of missed prayers. al-Mabsūṭ for al-Sarakhsī, Kitāb al-Ṣalāh, Bāb Nawādir al-Ṣalāh, vol. 2, p. 87.
Source pages p. 128

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof that complements the previous one. It states the exceptions to the obligation of order. Three causes drop the order: (1) narrowness of time — if performing the missed prayer would cause the current farḍ to be missed (e.g., only enough time remains for the current prayer), then order is not required; (2) forgetfulness — if one forgets the missed prayer, he may proceed with the current one; (3) many missed prayers — when the number exceeds six (some say five or six), order is no longer required due to difficulty. The passage then quotes al-Mabsūṭ which confirms that order is wājib except in these three situations. The Urdu commentary gives an example: if someone missed Ẓuhr and it is now the end of 'Asr time, he may not make up Ẓuhr if doing so would cause him to miss 'Asr.

Key Terms
ضِيقِ الْوَقْتِ (ḍīq al-waqt): The situation where the remaining time for the current farḍ prayer is only enough for that prayer itself, leaving no time to make up missed prayers without losing the current farḍ.
كَثُرَةِ الْفَوَائِتِ (kathrat al-fawā'it): The accumulation of missed prayers that exceeds a certain number (here stated as six), making order impractical.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In which of the following situations is the order (tartīb) between missed prayers and the current farḍ NOT required?
A) When the missed prayer is a supererogatory prayer.
B) When the person has missed exactly one prayer and remembers it.
C) When making up the missed prayer would cause the current farḍ to be missed due to narrow time.
D) When the person has missed prayers but they are all from the same day.

Key Takeaway
Order between missed and current prayers is wājib, but the Sharīʿa lifts this obligation in cases of narrow time, forgetfulness, or when missed prayers exceed six.

The Obligation of Sequence Between Missed and Current Prayers
Statement of the obligation of sequence between missed and current prayers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on tartib between fawa'it and fard al-waqt and identify the condition of being 'sahib al-tartib'.

Core Idea
You must pray missed prayers before the current fard — sequence is wajib.

When you remember missed prayers, the Hanafi school requires you to make them up in order before praying the current obligatory prayer. This lesson explains that obligation and its key condition of being 'sahib al-tartib'. We will also note the difference with the Shafi'i school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling level
The act is performing sequence (tartib) between missed prayers (fawa'it) and the current fard. The ruling is 'mustahaqq' (required), which in Hanafi terminology equals 'wajib'. Note that it is not fard because the evidence is not qat'i.
Wajib means obligatory but proven by zanni evidence.
2
Understand the condition of 'sahib al-tartib'
The obligation of sequence only applies to a person who is 'sahib al-tartib' — one who remembers the missed prayers and their order. If someone has many missed prayers or does not remember the order, the sequence requirement drops.
This condition is derived from the broader ruling and will be expanded in later lessons.
3
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that sequence is sunnah, not wajib. The practical implication: in the Shafi'i school, one may pray the current fard first without sin, whereas in the Hanafi school, leaving the sequence is a sin (though the prayer is still valid).
The dispute is based on different interpretations of the evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إِنَّ التَّرْتِيْبَ بَيْنَ الْفَوَائِتِ وَفَرْضِ الْوَقْتِ مُسْتَحَقٌّ . ترجمہ: فوت شدہ نمازوں اور وقتی فرض نماز کے درمیان ترتیب ضروری ہے۔
Indeed, sequence between missed prayers and the obligatory prayer of the time is required.
Source pages p. 128

Commentary
This is a ruling statement from the Hanafi school regarding the obligation of sequence (tartib) between missed prayers (fawa'it) and the current obligatory prayer (fard al-waqt). The principle applies to a person who is 'sahib al-tartib' (one who remembers the missed prayers and their order). For such a person, it is wajib to pray the missed prayers first, then the current prayer. This is the standard position in the madhhab, as found in Hidayah and other sources.

Key Terms
فوائت (fawa'it): Plural of fa'ita: prayers that were missed and must be made up (qada').
ترتيب (tartib): Performing acts in a specific order; here, praying missed prayers before the current obligatory prayer.
مستحق (mustahaqq): Required, obligatory; in this context equivalent to 'wajib'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on sequence (tartib) between missed prayers (fawa'it) and the current obligatory prayer for a person who remembers the missed prayers?
A) It is fard and cannot be dropped.
B) It is wajib according to the Hanafi school.
C) It is sunnah.
D) It is makruh.

Key Takeaway
Sequence between missed and current prayers is wajib for a person who remembers the order of missed prayers.

Sequence Drops Due to Narrow Time, Forgetting, or Many Missed Prayers
States three exceptions to the sequence requirement.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three causes that waive the sequence obligation and distinguish each cause's condition.

Core Idea
Sequence between prayers is waived when time is short, you forget, or you have many missed prayers.

We have learned that sequence between missed and current prayers is wajib when the missed prayer is more than three days old, provided you remember. But what if time is about to run out? Or you cannot remember the order? Or you have many missed prayers? The Hanafi school provides relief in such cases, as the text explains.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three causes
Read the Arabic statement and its translation. List the three causes explicitly mentioned: narrowness of time, forgetfulness, and abundance of missed prayers.
These are the only causes that drop sequence. No others.
2
Understand narrow time
Narrow time (diq al-waqt) means the remaining time for the current prayer is so short that if you start with the missed prayer, you will miss the current prayer.
The measure is the fear of missing the current prayer.
3
Understand forgetfulness
Forgetfulness (nisyan) includes forgetting which prayers are missed or forgetting their order. If you are uncertain, sequence drops.
This applies even if you remember that you have missed prayers but not the details.
4
Understand many missed prayers
If the number of missed prayers exceeds six (kathrat al-fawa'it), sequence drops because it becomes burdensome to maintain the order.
The Hanafi school sets the limit at six based on the practice of the Companions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إِنَّ التَّرْتِيبَ يَسْقُطُ بِضِيقِ الْوَقْتِ وَكَذَا بِالنِّسْيَانِ وَكَثُرَةِ الْفَوَائِتِ. ترجمہ: وقت کی تنگی نسیان اور فوت شدہ نمازوں کی کثرت کی وجہ سے ترتیب ساقط ہو جاتی ہے۔
Indeed, sequence drops due to narrowness of time, and similarly due to forgetfulness and abundance of missed prayers.
Source pages p. 128

Commentary
This is a companion ruling to the previous one, stating three conditions under which the obligation of sequence is lifted. First, narrow time (diq al-waqt): if one fears that the current prayer will be missed if they start with the missed prayer, they pray the current one first. Second, forgetfulness (nisyan): if one forgets which prayer is missed, sequence is not required. Third, many missed prayers (kathrat al-fawa'it): when missed prayers exceed six (according to the Hanafi position), sequence drops because it becomes too burdensome to remember the order. These exceptions are based on mercy and practicality.

Key Terms
ضيق الوقت (diq al-waqt): When the remaining time for the current prayer is so short that praying the missed prayer would cause the current prayer to be missed.
نسيان (nisyan): Forgetting which missed prayers are due or their order.
كثرة الفوائت (kathrat al-fawa'it): Missed prayers numbering more than six (the Hanafi threshold).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, the sequence between missed and current prayers is waived in all of the following EXCEPT:
A) Narrow time
B) Forgetfulness
C) Abundance of missed prayers (more than six)
D) Intentionally delaying the missed prayer

Key Takeaway
The obligation of sequence is suspended in three specific cases to prevent hardship: narrow time, forgetfulness, and abundance of missed prayers.

Effect of Invalid Fardiyyah on Tahrimah: Muhammad vs. Shaykhayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on fardiyyah and tahrimah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two positions in the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the effect of invalid fardiyyah on the tahrimah and identify the mufta bihi.

Core Idea
When fardiyyah is invalid, the prayer's tahrimah may remain—two Hanafi views on whether it perishes.

Consider a person who owes a missed prayer (e.g., Zuhr) and prays the current prayer (e.g., 'Asr) without first making up the missed one. If the current prayer becomes invalid due to missing sequence, does the entire prayer collapse, or does only its attribute of being obligatory (fardiyyah) dissolve? This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute on exactly this point, distinguishing between the essence of the prayer (tahrimah) and its obligatory character.

Guided Path
1
Understand the scenario
You need to grasp the context: a person who owes a missed prayer prays a current fard prayer without observing the required sequence. The current prayer becomes fasid (invalid) because sequence is a required condition. The dispute is about the consequences of this invalidity.
2
Define key terms: fardiyyah and tahrimah
Fardiyyah refers to the attribute of being an obligatory (fard) prayer. Tahrimah is the initial takbir that sanctifies the prayer and marks its beginning; it also refers to the prayer as a valid act once initiated. Understand that the scholars distinguish between the prayer's essence and its obligatory label.
Tahrimah is a rukn in Hanafi fiqh.
3
State Imam Muhammad's position
Imam Muhammad holds that when fardiyyah is invalidated, the tahrimah becomes void fundamentally (batalat al-tahrimah aslan). In other words, the entire prayer collapses; it is as if no prayer was commenced.
4
State the two shaykhs' position
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (the two shaykhs) hold that the tahrimah does not become void. The prayer remains a valid act in its essence; only the attribute of being fard is invalidated. The prayer may be considered nafl or deficient, but not entirely void.
This is the mufta bihi (relied-upon) position.
5
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf and the mufta bihi
The practical consequence: according to Imam Muhammad, the person must repeat the prayer entirely. According to the two shaykhs, the prayer is not repeated (it is valid for fulfilling the act, though deficient) but the missed prayer must still be made up. Later Hanafi works prefer the view of the two shaykhs.
The additional text in the passage confirms the rule on sequence and its exceptions (narrow time, forgetfulness, many missed prayers).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إِنَّ الْفَرْضِيَّةَ إِذَا بَطَلَتْ بَطَلَتِ التَّحْرِيمَةُ أَصْلًا عِندَ مُحَمَّدٍ وَعِندَ الشَّيْخَينِ لَا يَبْطُلُ . ترجمہ: امام محمد کے نزدیک جب فرضیت باطل ہو جائے تو اصل تحریمہ بھی باطل ہو جائے گی ، اور شیخین کے نزدیک اصل تحریمہ باطل نہیں ہوگی۔ قَوْلُهُ: وَقَدَّمَهَا عَلَى صَلَاةِ الْوَقْتِ إِلَّا أَنْ يَخَافَ فَوْتَ صَلَاةِ الْوَقْتِ عَلَى الْفَائِتَةِ ثُمَّ يَقْضِيهَا. التَّرْتِيبُ بَيْنَ الْفَرَائِتِ وَفَرْضِ الْوَقْتِ عِنْدَنَا شَرُطٌ مُسْتَحَقٌّ وَيُسْقِطُهُ ثَلَاثَةُ أَشْيَاءَ ضِيقُ الْوَقْتِ وَالنِّسْيَانُ وَدُخُولُ الْفَوَائِتِ فِي حَيِّزِ التَّكْرَارِ.
Indeed, when fardiyyah (obligatory nature) is invalidated, the tahrimah (initial takbir) becomes void fundamentally according to Muhammad, but according to the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) it does not become void. Translation: According to Imam Muhammad, when fardiyyah becomes invalid, the original tahrimah also becomes invalid; according to the two shaykhs, the original tahrimah does not become invalid. His statement: 'And he (the one who misses sequence) may offer it before the prayer of the time unless he fears missing the prayer of the time due to the missed prayer; then he prays it and later makes it up.' Sequence between missed prayers and the obligatory prayer of the time is, according to us, a required condition, and three things drop it: narrowness of time, forgetfulness, and the missed prayers entering into the realm of repetition.
Source pages p. 129

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the effect of invalidating the fardiyyah (obligatory nature) of a prayer on its tahrimah (the initial takbir that makes the prayer sacred). The scenario: a person who owes a missed prayer (e.g., Zuhr) prays 'Asr without sequence, but within its time. If he prays 'Asr in the last part of its time, it is valid because sequence drops due to narrow time. But if he prays 'Asr earlier, his 'Asr becomes invalid (fasid) because sequence was required and he omitted it. The question: does this invalidity affect the entire prayer (the 'asl') or just the attribute (being fard)? Imam Muhammad holds that the entire prayer is void (batil) because the fardiyyah is integral; if the fardiyyah is invalidated, the tahrimah is void ab initio. The two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) hold that only the attribute of being fard is invalidated; the prayer itself as a nafl or something else remains valid (the tahrimah does not become void). The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that of the two shaykhs. The additional quotes confirm the rule on sequence and its exceptions.

Key Terms
فرضية (fardiyyah): The attribute of being obligatory (fard) that applies to a prayer.
تحريمة (tahrimah): The initial takbir (Allahu Akbar) that sanctifies the prayer and marks its beginning; also used to refer to the prayer itself once started.
شيخين (al-shaykhayn): The two masters: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (or sometimes Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, but here it is the former).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), if a person prays 'Asr without first making up a missed Zuhr (and 'Asr is invalid due to missing sequence), what happens to the tahrimah?
A) The tahrimah becomes void, so the prayer is totally invalid.
B) The tahrimah remains; only the fardiyyah is invalidated.
C) The prayer is still valid as fard.
D) The prayer is valid as sunnah.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, when a prayer becomes invalid due to missing sequence, the relied-upon view holds that the prayer is not entirely void; only its attribute of being fard is invalidated.

Three Exceptions to the Order of Prayers
Ruling on the three exceptions to the obligation of order in prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three exceptions that drop the requirement of order (tartib) between missed and current prayers in the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Tartib is wajib but dropped when time is tight, you forget, or missed prayers are many.

In the Hanafi school, when you owe missed prayers, you must pray them in order before the current prayer. However, this binding condition is not absolute. The classical texts identify three specific situations where this requirement is lifted, ensuring that the obligation of the current prayer is not compromised. This lesson unpacks those three exceptions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the default ruling
Recognize that tartib (order) is a necessary condition (sharṭ mustaḥaqq) in the Hanafi school, meaning it is wajib to observe.
2
Understand the nature of the condition
Note that it is not a pillar (rukn) but a binding condition – omission requires compensation but does not invalidate the current prayer if later rectified.
3
Learn the first exception: narrowness of time
If the current prayer's time is so short that praying the missed prayer first would cause missing the current prayer, then tartib is dropped.
The current prayer takes precedence.
4
Learn the second exception: forgetfulness
If one forgets the missed prayers at the time of the current prayer, tartib is dropped – but one must still make them up later.
Forgetfulness here means not remembering until after completing the current prayer.
5
Learn the third exception: numerous missed prayers
When the number of missed prayers exceeds five (or, according to some narrations, exceeds the number of daily prayers), they are considered 'entering into repetition' and tartib is dropped.
The exact threshold is five or more missed prayers.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
التَّرْتِيبُ بَيْنَ الْفَرَائِتِ وَفَرْضِ الْوَقْتِ عِنْدَنَا شَرُطٌ مُسْتَحَقٌّ وَيُسْقِطُهُ ثَلَاثَةُ أَشْيَاءَ ضِيقُ الْوَقْتِ وَالنِّسْيَانُ وَدُخُولُ الْفَوَائِتِ فِي حَيِّزِ التَّكْرَارِ.
The order between missed prayers and the obligatory current prayer is a necessary condition according to us, and three things drop it: narrowness of time, forgetfulness, and the missed prayers entering into the category of repetition.
Source pages p. 129

Commentary
Ruling statement from the Hanafi school on the obligation of ordering (tartib) between missed prayers (fawā'it) and the current obligatory prayer (farḍ al-waqt). It states that this order is a necessary condition (sharṭ mustaḥaqq), meaning it is obligatory to observe. However, this condition is dropped in three specific situations: (1) if time is so narrow that praying the missed prayer first would cause missing the current prayer; (2) if one forgets the missed prayers; (3) if the missed prayers have become numerous (more than five, or according to some, more than the number of daily prayers). In these cases, one prays the current prayer first and then makes up the missed ones.

Key Terms
التَّرْتِيب (al-tartīb): The obligation to pray missed prayers in order before the current prayer.
الْفَرَائِتُ (al-farā'it): Missed obligatory prayers that are yet to be made up.
شَرُطٌ مُسْتَحَقٌّ (sharṭ mustaḥaqq): A condition that is owed, i.e., obligatory to fulfill.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Narrowness of time, forgetfulness, and travel
B) Narrowness of time, forgetfulness, and many missed prayers entering into repetition
C) Narrowness of time, illness, and many missed prayers
D) Forgetfulness, many missed prayers, and being a traveller

Key Takeaway
The obligation of tartib between missed and current prayers is dropped in three specific cases: narrow time, forgetfulness, and numerous missed prayers.

Effect of Invalidation of Obligation on the Prayer's Original Status
Intra-Hanafi dispute on whether invalidation of farḍiyyah invalidates the tahrima itself

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on the invalidation of farḍiyyah and evaluate the disagreement between the Two Shaykhs and Imam Muhammad.

Core Idea
The tahrima is contracted for the prayer itself, not just the obligation; losing the farḍiyyah does not invalidate the prayer.

In Hanafi fiqh, when a prayer is performed without observing the required order (tartib) of missed prayers, its obligatory nature (farḍiyyah) becomes invalid. But does this invalidation affect only the attribute of being fard, or does it nullify the entire prayer? This lesson unpacks an important intra-Hanafi disagreement between the Two Shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) and Imam Muhammad on this very question, and explores the practical consequences that follow.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position (Two Shaykhs)
Identify what Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold: the prayer remains valid as a nafl, and only the attribute of farḍiyyah is invalidated.
They base this on the idea that the tahrima was contracted for the original prayer with the attribute, not for the attribute alone.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
State Imam Muhammad's position: the entire prayer is invalid (bāṭil) because the tahrima was contracted specifically for the fard prayer.
Muhammad argues that since the farḍiyyah is gone, the tahrima has no basis.
3
Follow each proof
Understand the dalil for each: Muhammad uses a direct link between tahrima and fard; the Two Shaykhs use qiyas with the kaffarah fasting case.
The Two Shaykhs' analogy shows that an act can lose its attribute but remain valid as a voluntary act.
4
Analyze the Two Shaykhs' response
Understand their rebuttal: the contract is for the substance with the attribute, not the attribute alone. Invalidation of the attribute does not necessitate invalidation of the substance.
This is a key usul principle: no necessary concomitance between attribute and substance.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Identify practical consequences: according to the Two Shaykhs, the prayer counts as nafl (so no need to repeat as fard, but missed Zuhr must still be made up); laughter does not break wudu. According to Muhammad, the prayer is void, must be repeated, and laughter breaks wudu.
The mufta bihi is the view of the Two Shaykhs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إِنَّ الْفَرْضِيَّةَ إِذَا بَطَلَتْ بَطَلَتِ التَّحْرِيمَةُ أَصْلًا عِندَ مُحَمَّدٍ وَعِندَ الشَّيْخَينِ لَا يَبْطُلُ . وَبِبُطَلان الْفَرْضِيَّةِ لَا يَبْطُلُ أَصْلُ الصَّلَاةِ عِنْدَ الشَّيْخَيْنِ خِلَافًا لِمُحَمَّدٍ) لِأَنَّ التَّحْرِيمَةَ عُقِدَتْ لِلْفَرْضِ فَإِذَا بَطَلَتْ الْفَرْضِيَّةُ بَطَلَتْ أَصْلًا وَلَهُمَا أَنَّهَا عُقِدَتْ لِأَصْلِ الصَّلَاةِ بِوَصْفِ الْفَرْضِيَّةِ فَلَمْ يَكُنُ مِنْ ضَرُورَةِ بُطْلَانِ الْوَصْفِ بُطَلَانُ الْأَصْلِ. لَا يَبْطُلُ أَصْلُ الصَّلَاةِ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَأَبِى يُوسُفَ وَعِندَ مُحَمَّدٍ يَبْطُلُ) حَتَّى لَوْ قَهْقَهَ بَعْدَ التَّذَكُرِ لَا تَنْتَقِضُ طَهَارَتُهُ (قَوْلُهُ فَلَمْ يَكُنْ مِنْ ضَرُورَةِ بُطَلَانِ الْوَصْفِ بُطَلَانُ الْأَصْلِ) يَعْنِي لَيْسَ الْمَوْجُودُ مِمَّا يُبْطِلُ أَصْلَ الصَّلَاةِ كَالْحَدَثِ بَلْ وَصْفَ الْفَرْضِيَّةِ. وَلَا تَلَازُمُ بَيْنَ بُطْلَانِ الْوَصْفِ وَبُطْلَانِ الْأَصْلِ كَالْمُكَفِّرِ بِالصَّوْمِ إِذَا أَيْسَرَ فِي خِلَالِ الْيَوْمِ لَا يَبْطُلُ صَوْمُهُ فَيَصِيرُ مُفْطِرًا بَلْ يَبْطُلُ وَصُفُ وُقُوعِهِ كَفَّارَةً.
Indeed, when the obligatory nature is invalidated, the tahrima is invalidated fundamentally according to Muhammad, and according to the Two Shaykhs it is not invalidated. And with the invalidation of the obligatory nature, the original prayer is not invalidated according to the Two Shaykhs, contrary to Muhammad, because the tahrima was contracted for the obligatory prayer, so when the obligatory nature is invalidated, it is fundamentally invalidated. And for them (the Two Shaykhs) it was contracted for the original prayer with the attribute of obligation, so it is not necessary that the invalidation of the attribute entails the invalidation of the original. The original prayer is not invalidated according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, and according to Muhammad it is invalidated, such that if he laughs after remembering, his purification is not nullified. His statement: 'so it is not necessary that the invalidation of the attribute entails the invalidation of the original' means that what exists is not something that invalidates the original prayer, like a hadath, but rather the attribute of obligation. And there is no necessary concomitance between the invalidation of the attribute and the invalidation of the original, like the one making expiation by fasting: if he becomes wealthy during the day, his fast is not invalidated, so he becomes a non-faster? rather the attribute of its occurrence as expiation is invalidated.
Source pages p. 129

Commentary
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute on the effect of invalidation of the obligatory nature (farḍiyyah) of a prayer. The dispute arises in a scenario where a person who has missed a prayer (e.g., Zuhr) prays the current prayer (e.g., Asr) without observing order, and the order is required (time is not narrow). In such a case, the Asr prayer is considered invalid (fāsid) because the obligation to pray Asr as a fard is not valid due to the missed Zuhr. The question is: does this invalidation only affect the attribute of being a fard, or does it invalidate the entire prayer (the prayer as an act of worship)? Imam Muhammad holds that the tahrima (the opening takbir that makes the prayer sacred) is contracted for the fard prayer. Since the fardiyyah is invalid, the entire tahrima is invalid, and the prayer is completely void. The Two Shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) hold that the tahrima is contracted for the original prayer (aṣl al-ṣalāh) with the attribute of farḍiyyah. Therefore, when the attribute is invalidated, the original prayer remains valid, but it becomes a nafl (supererogatory) prayer instead of a fard. They use an analogy with kaffarah: if a person begins fasting for expiation while poor, then becomes wealthy during the day, the fast is not invalidated; rather, its attribute as expiation is lost, but the fast itself counts as a supererogatory act. Similarly, the prayer remains valid as nafl. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that of the Two Shaykhs.

Key Terms
الْفَرْضِيَّة (al-farḍiyyah): The legal attribute of being an obligatory (fard) act of worship.
التَّحْرِيمَة (al-taḥrīmah): The state of consecration entered by the opening takbir (takbīr taḥrīmah), which renders certain actions prohibited during prayer.
الشَّيْخَينِ (al-Shaykhayn): Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (the two elders of the Hanafi school).
الْوَصْف (al-waṣf): An attribute or quality that is not essential to the substance (aṣl).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Two Shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), if a person prays 'Asr before making up a missed Zuhr without a valid excuse (and time is not narrow), what is the status of the 'Asr prayer?
A) It is completely invalid (bāṭil)
B) It is valid as a fard prayer
C) It is valid as a nafl (supererogatory) prayer
D) It is makrūh but still valid as fard

Key Takeaway
The invalidation of farḍiyyah does not destroy the prayer itself; it transforms the prayer into a valid nafl according to the relied-upon Hanafi position.

Effect of Invalidating Fardiyyah on Original Prayer
Intra-Hanafi dispute on whether invalidating fardiyyah invalidates asl al-salah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on whether invalidation of fardiyyah invalidates asl al-salah, explain the reasoning of the Sheikhayn and Imam Muhammad, and apply the analogy of kaffarah to this ruling.

Core Idea
Invalidating the attribute (wasf) of obligation does not invalidate the essence (asl) of prayer.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a person who begins a fard prayer, but the obligation is lifted during the prayer (e.g., reaching home after travel). Does the prayer become invalid, or does it continue as a supererogatory (nafl) prayer? The Hanafi school is divided: the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) hold that the prayer remains valid as nafl, while Imam Muhammad holds that it becomes completely invalid. This distinction rests on a key legal principle: the separability of an attribute from its essence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core issue
Determine the exact question: if the fardiyyah attribute is invalidated during prayer, does the prayer become batil or remain valid as nafl?
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf with practical consequences.
2
State the position of the Sheikhayn
According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, asl al-salah is not invalidated; it becomes nafl. Takbirat al-ihram was contracted for the essence with an attribute.
This is the mufta bihi (operative) position.
3
State the position of Imam Muhammad
According to Imam Muhammad, both attribute and essence are invalidated because the takbir was contracted specifically for the fard prayer.
This is a valid internal ikhtilaf but weaker in the madhhab.
4
Analyze the dalil for each position
Sheikhayn: invalidation of attribute does not necessitate invalidation of essence. Muhammad: the contract was for the fard, so when fardiyyah falls, the contract collapses.
The key is whether the contract is for the essence with a condition or for the specific attribute.
5
Evaluate the tarjih and analogy
The Sheikhayn support their view with an analogy to kaffarah fasting: when a poor person begins fasting for expiation and becomes wealthy, the fast remains valid as a voluntary act. Similarly, the prayer remains valid as nafl.
Analogy (qiyas) is used to strengthen the argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اصول ہدایہ جلد اول ہو جائے گا، البتہ اصل نماز اس کے حق میں نفل اور تطوع ہوگی، امام محمد رحمہ اللہ کے نزدیک وصف اور اصل صلاۃ دونوں باطل ہوں گی۔ علامہ ابن ہمام رحمہ اللہ نے اس مسئلہ کو مثال کے ذریعے واضح کیا ہے، اگر کسی شخص نے تنگدستی اور غربت کی وجہ سے کفارہ یمین کے اندر تین روزے رکھنا شروع کئے، ایک دو روزے کے بعد وہ مالدار ہو گیا تو اب اس کے لئے غلام آزاد کرنا یا اطعام یا کسوۃ سے کفارہ دینا ضروری ہوگا، ان تینوں پر عدم قدرت کی صورت میں روزہ رکھنے کا حکم ہے، پس جب اس نے تنگدستی کی وجہ سے روزے کے ساتھ کفارہ ادا کرنا شروع کیا لیکن اس دوران مالدار ہو گیا تو اس روزے کا وصف وقوع کفارہ باطل ہو جائے گا، لیکن اصل روزہ باطل نہیں ہوگا، اور یہ روزہ فضل شمار ہوگا، اسی طرح صورت مسئولہ میں مصلی کا وصف فرض ہونا باطل ہوگا اور اصل نماز باطل نہیں ہوگی بلکہ وہ نفل شمار ہوگی۔
وَبِبُطْلَانِ الْفَرْضِيَّةِ لَا يَبْطُلُ أَصْلُ الصَّلَاةِ عِنْدَ الشَّيْخَيْنِ خِلَافًا لِمُحَمَّدٍ، لِأَنَّ التَّحْرِيمَةَ عُقِدَتْ لِلْفَرْضِ فَإِذَا بَطَلَتْ الْفَرْضِيَّةُ بَطَلَتْ أَصْلًا، وَلَهُمَا أَنَّهَا عُقِدَتْ لِأَصْلِ الصَّلَاةِ بِوَصْفِ الْفَرْضِيَّةِ فَلَمْ يَكُنْ مِنْ ضَرُورَةِ بُطْلَانِ الْوَصْفِ بُطْلَانُ الْأَصْلِ۔
مجمع الأنهر: كتاب الصلاة، باب قضاء الفوائت ج ۱ ص ۱۴۵، ط: المطبعة الخيرية (لَا يَبْطُلُ أَصْلُ الصَّلَاةِ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَأَبِي يُوسُفَ وَعِنْدَ مُحَمَّدٍ يَبْطُلُ) حَتَّى لَوْ قَهْقَهَ بَعْدَ التَّذَكُرِ لَا تَنْتَقِضُ طَهَارَتُهُ (قَوْلُهُ فَلَمْ يَكُنْ مِنْ ضَرُورَةِ بُطْلَانِ الْوَصْفِ بُطْلَانُ الْأَصْلِ) يَعْنِي لَيْسَ الْمَوْجُودُ مِمَّا يُبْطِلُ أَصْلَ الصَّلَاةِ كَالْحَدَثِ بَلْ وَصْفَ الْفَرْضِيَّةِ، وَلَا تَلَازُمَ بَيْنَ بُطْلَانِ الْوَصْفِ وَبُطْلَانِ الْأَصْلِ كَالْمُكَفِّرِ بِالصَّوْمِ إِذَا أَيْسَرَ فِي خِلَالِ الْيَوْمِ لَا يَبْطُلُ صَوْمُهُ فَيَصِيرُ مُفْطِرًا بَلْ يَبْطُلُ وَصْفُ وُقُوعِهِ كَفَّارَةً۔
فتح القدير: كتاب الصلاة، باب قضاء الفوائت ج ا ص ۴۹۲، ط: دار الفكر
The original prayer will become supererogatory (nafl) for him. According to Imam Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on him), both the attribute and the original prayer are invalid. Allamah Ibn Humam (may Allah have mercy on him) clarified this issue with an example: If a person began fasting three days for the expiation of an oath due to poverty, and after one or two days he became wealthy, then it becomes necessary for him to free a slave, or feed, or clothe as expiation. Fasting is only prescribed when one is unable to do these three. So when he began expiation with fasting due to poverty, but during that period he became wealthy, the attribute of its occurring as expiation is invalidated, but the fast itself is not invalidated; it is considered a voluntary fast. Similarly, in the issue at hand, the attribute of being obligatory (fard) for the prayer is invalidated, but the original prayer is not invalidated; rather, it is counted as nafl. 'And with the invalidation of fardiyyah, the original prayer is not invalidated according to the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), contrary to Muhammad. Because the takbirat al-ihram was contracted for the fard, so when fardiyyah is invalidated, it (the prayer) is invalidated entirely. And for them (the two shaykhs), it (the takbir) was contracted for the original prayer with the attribute of fardiyyah, so it is not a necessary consequence of the invalidation of the attribute that the essence is invalidated.' Majma' al-Anhur: 'The original prayer is not invalidated according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, and according to Muhammad it is invalidated. Even if he laughs out loud after remembering, his ablution is not nullified.' His statement: 'so it is not a necessary consequence of the invalidation of the attribute that the essence is invalidated' means the existing thing is not something that nullifies the original prayer like hadath, but rather the attribute of fardiyyah. And there is no necessary correlation between the invalidation of the attribute and the invalidation of the essence, like the one expiating with fasting who becomes wealthy during the day: his fast is not invalidated, so he becomes a non-faster, but rather the attribute of its occurrence as expiation is invalidated. Fath al-Qadir.
Source pages p. 130

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the effect of invalidating the attribute of being obligatory (fardiyyah) on the original prayer (asl al-salah). The context is a situation where a person begins a prayer intending it as fard, but during the prayer, the obligation is lifted (e.g., he reaches his hometown after traveling, or his excuse for tayammum ends). The question: does the prayer remain valid as an obligation, or does it become invalid, or does it become nafl? The text states: With the invalidation of fardiyyah, the original prayer is not invalidated according to the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), contrary to Imam Muhammad. The reasoning given for Muhammad is that takbirat al-ihram (tahrimah) was contracted specifically for the fard prayer; therefore, when the fardiyyah is invalidated, the entire contract is nullified, so the prayer becomes invalid. For the two shaykhs, the takbir was contracted for the original prayer (asl al-salah) with the attribute of fardiyyah; since the attribute is separable, its nullification does not entail nullification of the essence. The example of expiation is used: if someone begins fasting for expiation while poor but becomes wealthy during the day, the attribute of expiation is invalidated, but the fast itself remains valid as a voluntary fast. Similarly, the prayer remains valid as a supererogatory (nafl) act. The later sources (Majma' al-Anhur, Fath al-Qadir) confirm this as the mufta bihi position (Sheikhayn's view).

Key Terms
الفرضية (al-fardiyyah): The attribute or legal quality of being obligatory (fard) attached to an act of worship.
أصل الصلاة (asl al-salah): The essential act of prayer itself, distinguished from its specific legal attribute (e.g., fard, nafl).
الوصف (al-wasf): The attribute or property of an act that is not inseparable from its essence, such as being fard or being expiation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), if the attribute of being fard is invalidated during prayer, what happens to the prayer?
A) It becomes invalid (batil) and must be repeated.
B) It remains valid as a supererogatory (nafl) prayer.
C) It becomes suspended until the obligation returns.
D) It is considered a sin unless repeated.

Key Takeaway
The invalidation of the attribute of obligation (fardiyyah) does not invalidate the essence of the prayer; it transforms it into a voluntary (nafl) prayer.

Sujud al-Sahw is Not Repeated: A Rational Proof for Post-Salam Preference
Establishing that sujud al-sahw is not repeated, leading to preference after salam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi principle that sujud al-sahw is not repeated and explain how it leads to performing sujud al-sahw after salam, while distinguishing this from the views of Imam Malik and Imam al-Shafi'i.

Core Idea
Sujud al-sahw cannot be repeated, so it must be delayed to after salam to avoid invalidity.

This lesson examines a key principle in Hanafi fiqh: sujud al-sahw (prostration for forgetfulness) is not subject to repetition. The author of al-Hidayah uses this principle as a rational proof (dalīl ma‘qūl) to establish that sujud al-sahw should always be performed after the salam, regardless of whether the forgetfulness involved an increase or decrease in the prayer. We will explore the reasoning behind this position and compare it with the views of Imam Malik and Imam al-Shafi'i.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
The Hanafi school holds that sujud al-sahw is performed after the salam in all cases of forgetfulness, whether increase or decrease.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam Malik distinguishes between increase (after salam) and decrease (before salam); Imam al-Shafi'i prefers before salam.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Malik: for decrease, before salam to compensate; for increase, after salam because prayer is complete. Shafi'i: before salam is based on hadith and analogy.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response relies on the principle that sujud al-sahw is not repeated. If done before salam, a subsequent doubt may necessitate another sujud, leading to repetition, which is prohibited. Therefore, delaying to after salam is the only safe option.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Hanafis always perform one sujud after salam; Malikis may do before or after depending on the cause; Shafi'is generally do before salam.

Source Text

باب سجود السهو (۱۱۵) إِنَّ سُجُودَ السَّهُو مِمَّا لَا يَتَكَرَّرُ . ترجمہ: سجدہ سہو ان چیزوں میں سے ہے جو مکرر نہیں ہوتے ۔ تشریح : مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ بعض اشیاء ایسی ہیں جن میں تکرار نہیں ہوتا اور سجدہ سہو بھی ان اشیاء میں سے ہے یعنی سجدہ سہو میں بھی تکرار نہیں ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کرنے کے بعد اس بات کو ثابت کر رہے ہیں کہ احناف کے نزدیک چاہے نماز میں زیادتی ہو جائے یا کمی ، ایک ہی سجدہ سلام کے بعد واجب ہوتا ہے نہ کہ سلام سے پہلے، دراصل یہ امام مالک رحمہ اللہ کے قول سے احتراز ہے، امام مالک رحمہ اللہ کے نزدیک نماز میں کمی کی صورت میں سلام سے پہلے سجدہ کرے اور زیادتی کی صورت میں سلام کے بعد سجدہ کرے، امام شافعی رحمہ اللہ کے نزدیک سجدہ سہو سلام سے پہلے کرنا اولی ہے، جبکہ احناف کے نزدیک دونوں صورتوں میں سلام کے بعد سجدہ سہو کرے گا، کیونکہ اگر سلام سے پہلے سجدہ کرے تو اس صورت میں تکرار آئے گا، جبکہ مذکورہ اصول کی رو سے سجدہ سہو میں تکرار نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے کہ سلام سے پہلے سجدہ سہو کرنے میں تکرار کا امکان ہے بایں طور کہ سلام سے پہلے سجدہ کر لیا پھر جب سلام پھیرنے کا وقت آیا تو اس کو شک ہو گیا کہ تین رکعتیں ہوئیں یا چار ہوئیں، اسی سوچ میں پڑا رہا یہاں تک کہ سلام میں تاخیر ہوگئی پھر یاد آیا کہ چار رکعتیں ہوگئی ہیں، تو اب تاخیر سلام کی وجہ سے اس پر دوبارہ سجدہ سہو واجب ہوا، اب یہ شخص دوبارہ سجدہ سہو کرے گا یا نہیں، دو ہی صورتیں ہیں، اگر اس نے دوبارہ سجدہ سہو نہیں کیا تو نماز میں ایسا نقص باقی رہ گیا جس کی تلافی نہیں کی گئی ہے اور اگر دوبارہ سجدہ ہو گیا تو سجدہ سہو مکرر ہو جائے گا، حالانکہ یہ بالاجماع غیر مشروع ہے، اس لئے مناسب یہ ہے کہ سجدہ سہو سلام کے بعد کیا جائے تا کہ تمام سہووں کی تلافی ممکن ہو۔
الهداية: كتاب الصلاة، باب سجود السهو ج ا ص ۱۶۴، ط: رحمانيه (وَلأَنَّ سُجُودَ السَّهُوِ مِمَّا لَا يَتَكَرَّرُ) دَلِيلٌ مَعْقُولٌ عَلَى أَوْلَوِيَّةِ التَّأْخِيرِ، وَبَيَانُهُ أَنَّ سُجُودَ السَّهُوِ كَانَ يَنْبَغِي أَلَّا يَتَأَخَّرَ عَنْ زَمَانٍ وُجُودِ الْعِلَّةِ وَهِيَ السَّهُمُ إِلَّا أَنَّهُ تَأَخَّرَ لِضَرُورَةِ أَلَّا يَتَكَرَّرَ لِأَنَّهُ
Chapter of Sujud al-Sahw. (115) Indeed, the prostration of forgetfulness is among things that are not repeated. Translation: Sujud al-Sahw is among things that are not repeated. Explanation: The meaning of the mentioned principle is that there are some things which are not subject to repetition, and sujud al-sahw is among those things, i.e., sujud al-sahw is not repeated. The author of al-Hidayah, after mentioning this principle, is proving that according to the Hanafis, whether there is an increase or decrease in the prayer, a single sujud is obligatory after the salam, not before the salam. In fact, this is avoiding the statement of Imam Malik, according to whom in case of decrease one prostrates before salam and in case of increase after salam. According to Imam al-Shafi'i, it is preferable to do sujud before salam. According to the Hanafis, in both cases one prostrates after salam because if one prostrates before salam, repetition would occur, while according to the mentioned principle, sujud al-sahw is not repeated. This is because performing sujud al-sahw before salam has the possibility of repetition: for example, if one prostrates before salam, then when the time to say salam comes, he doubts whether he has prayed three or four rak'ahs, and remains in this thought until salam is delayed, then remembers that he has prayed four rak'ahs. Now due to the delay in salam, another sujud al-sahw becomes obligatory. This person will either do a second sujud or not. If he does not do it, a defect remains in the prayer that has not been compensated. If he does a second sujud, then sujud al-sahw is repeated, while this is unanimously unlegislated. Therefore, it is appropriate that sujud al-sahw be performed after salam so that compensation for all instances of forgetfulness is possible. Al-Hidayah: 'And because sujud al-sahw is among things that are not repeated' is a rational proof for the preference of delay. Its explanation: sujud al-sahw should not have been delayed from the time of the existence of the cause, which is forgetfulness, except that it is delayed out of necessity so that it is not repeated, because...
Source pages p. 131

Commentary
This passage introduces a key principle in Hanafi fiqh: sujud al-sahw (prostration for forgetfulness) is not subject to repetition. The author of al-Hidayah uses this principle to argue that sujud al-sahw should be performed after the salam, not before it, regardless of whether the forgetfulness involved an increase or decrease in the prayer. The reasoning is that if it were done before salam, there is a risk of needing to repeat it due to subsequent doubts, leading to multiple prostration events. Since repetition is not legislated (and would be invalid), the only way to avoid this is to postpone the prostration until after the salam. This position is contrasted with Imam Malik (who differentiates between increase and decrease) and Imam al-Shafi'i (who prefers before salam). The Hanafi view follows the principle that sujud al-sahw is a single compensating act that cannot be repeated. The text also includes an illustrative scenario: if a person does sujud before salam and then delays salam due to doubt, another sujud becomes wajib, leading to either an unrepaired defect or an invalid repetition. Hence, the Hanafi ruling is supported by rational necessity (dalil ma'qul).

Key Terms
سجود السهو (sujud al-sahw): Prostration performed to compensate for forgetfulness in prayer (salah).
لا يتكرر (la yatakarrar): Not subject to repetition; sujud al-sahw cannot be performed more than once in a prayer.
التأخير (al-ta'khir): Delaying the sujud al-sahw to after the salam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary rational proof (dalil ma'qul) given in al-Hidayah for performing sujud al-sahw after salam?
A) It is easier for the worshipper.
B) Sujud al-sahw is among things that are not repeated, so delaying avoids repetition.
C) It is based on the practice of the Prophet (PBUH).
D) It allows for more time to remember the forgotten parts.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi principle that sujud al-sahw is not repeated necessitates performing it after salam to avoid invalidity.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
The Principle of Non-Repetition of Sujūd al-Sahw
Ruling with rational proof on timing of sujūd al-sahw

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi principle that sujūd al-sahw cannot be repeated and state the muftā bihi position regarding its timing.

Core Idea
Sujūd al-Sahw cannot be repeated; therefore it is delayed after salām to avoid the impossibility of repetition.

In this passage, the author of Uṣūl al-Hidāyah establishes a foundational principle: sujūd al-sahw is not an act that can be performed multiple times in the same prayer. This seemingly simple rule has profound implications for the timing of the prostration. The Hanafī school argues that precisely because repetition is impossible, the prostration must be deferred until after the final salām, ensuring that any subsequent forgetfulness can be fully compensated without repeating the prostration.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Principle
The passage opens with the statement: 'Sujūd al-sahw is from things that are not repeated.' Understand that this means the prostration for forgetfulness cannot be performed twice in the same prayer, by consensus.
This is an axiomatic principle in Hanafi fiqh.
2
Trace the Rational Proof (Dalīl `Aqlī)
The author provides a rational proof: if sujūd al-sahw were performed before salām, and then another forgetfulness occurs (e.g., delay in salām due to doubt), one would either have to repeat the prostration (which is impermissible by consensus) or leave a deficiency unjabrated (uncompensated). Therefore, delay is necessary.
This is a qiyās-style argument from the impossibility of repetition.
3
Apply the Principle to Determine Timing
Since repetition is impossible, the only way to ensure that all forgetfulness is compensated is to perform sujūd al-sahw after the salām. In that position, if further forgetfulness occurs, it is already addressed in the same prostration.
The salām is also a wājib, and by analogy to other wājibāt, it is given precedence.
4
Compare with Other Schools
Note that Imām Mālik differentiates between increase and decrease, and Imām al-Shāfi`ī prefers before salām. The Hanafī response acknowledges the authenticity of hadith supporting both timings but prefers after salām due to the rational principle.
The ikhtilāf is legitimate, but the Hanafī position is muftā bihi.
5
State the Muftā Bihī Position
The relied-upon position in the Hanafī school is to perform sujūd al-sahw after salām in all cases, whether due to increase or decrease. This is the ẓāhir al-riwāyah and is preferred by the later authorities.
Performing it before salām is also valid but not the preferred practice.

[العناية: كتاب الصلاة، باب سجود السهو ، ج ۱ ص ۵۰۰، ط: دار الفکر] وَلَا خِلَافَ فِي الْجَوَازِ قَبْلَ السَّلَامِ وَبَعْدَهُ لِصِحَّةِ الْحَدِيثِ فِيهِمَا وَالتَّرْجِيحُ لِمَا قُلْنَا مِنْ جِهَةِ الْمَعْنَى أَنَّ السَّلَامَ مِنْ الْوَاجِبَاتِ فَيُقَدَّمُ عَلَى سُجُودِ السَّهْوِ قِيَاسًا عَلَى غَيْرِهِ مِنْ وَاجِبَاتِ الصَّلَاةِ، وَلِأَنَّ سُجُودَ السَّهُوِ مِمَّا لَا يَتَكَرَّرُ فَيُؤَخَّرُ عَنْ السَّلَامِ حَتَّى لَوْ سَهَا عَنْ السَّلَامِ يَنْجَبِرُ بِهِ. (115) Indeed, sujūd al-sahw is from things that are not repeated. Translation: Sujūd al-sahw is among things that are not repeated. Explanation: The meaning of the aforementioned principle is that some things are such that repetition does not occur in them, and sujūd al-sahw is also from these things, i.e., there is also no repetition in sujūd al-sahw. The author of Al-Hidayah, after mentioning this principle, is proving that according to the Hanafis, whether there is an increase or decrease in the prayer, one sujūd is obligatory after the salām, not before the salām. Actually, this is avoidance of the saying of Imām Mālik (ra). According to Imām Mālik (ra), in case of deficiency in prayer, one should prostrate before salām, and in case of increase, after salām. According to Imām al-Shāfi‘ī (ra), performing sujūd al-sahw before salām is more virtuous. However, according to the Hanafis, in both cases one will do sujūd al-sahw after salām, because if he prostrates before salām, repetition would occur in that case, whereas based on the mentioned principle there is no repetition in sujūd al-sahw. This is because there is a possibility of repetition in performing sujūd al-sahw before salām: if he prostrated before salām, then when the time for turning the salām came, he became doubtful whether three rak‘ahs had been performed or four, he remained in that thought until there was a delay in the salām, then he remembered that four rak‘ahs had been performed. Now due to the delay of salām, another sujūd al-sahw becomes obligatory upon him. Now should this person do another sujūd al-sahw or not? There are two possibilities: if he does not perform the second sujūd al-sahw, then a deficiency remains in the prayer that was not compensated; and if he does the second sujūd, then the sujūd al-sahw would be repeated, whereas this is unanimously unlegislated. Therefore it is appropriate that sujūd al-sahw be performed after salām so that compensation of all forgetfulness is possible. Al-Hidayah: Kitāb al-Ṣalāh, Bāb Sujūd al-Sahw, vol. 1, p. 164, R. And because sujūd al-sahw is from things that are not repeated) is a rational proof for the preferability of delay. Its explanation: sujūd al-sahw should not have been delayed from the time of the existence of the cause, which is forgetfulness, except that it was delayed due to the necessity of not being repeated, because... (then Arabic text from Al-`Ināyah) If he prostrates at the time of his forgetfulness and it is possible that he forgets after it, then if he forgets, either he prostrates a second time or not. If he does not prostrate, a necessary deficiency remains that cannot be compensated. If he prostrates, the prostration is repeated, and that is unlegislated by consensus, so delay becomes necessary. [Al-`Ināyah: Kitāb al-Ṣalāh, Bāb Sujūd al-Sahw, vol. 1, p. 500, Dār al-Fikr] And there is no disagreement about permissibility before salām and after it due to the authenticity of hadith about both, and the preference is for what we said from the standpoint of meaning: that salām is from the obligations (wājibāt), so it is given precedence over sujūd al-sahw by analogy to other obligations of the prayer, and because sujūd al-sahw is from things that are not repeated, so it is delayed after salām so that if one forgets the salām, it is compensated by it. [Tabyīn al-Ḥaqā’iq: Kitāb al-Ṣalāh, Bāb Sujūd al-Sahw, vol. 1, p. 192, Dār al-Kitāb al-Islāmī] Al-Hidayah: Kitāb al-Ṣalāh, Bāb Sujūd al-Sahw, vol. 1, p. 164, R.
Source pages p. 131

Commentary
This passage presents a Hanafi legal principle (uṣūl) from Uṣūl al-Hidāyah regarding sujūd al-sahw (prostration for forgetfulness). The passage is a ruling with proof, where the commentator (the author of Uṣūl al-Hidāyah) explains the principle that sujūd al-sahw is not subject to repetition. The ruling is that the Hanafī school holds that sujūd al-sahw is performed after the salām (final greeting) in all cases, whether the forgetfulness involves an increase or a decrease in the prayer. This is in contrast to Imām Mālik's view (before salām for decrease, after for increase) and Imām al-Shāfi‘ī's view (preferred before salām). The commentary provides a rational proof: if sujūd al-sahw is done before salām and then another forgetfulness occurs (like delay in salām due to confusion), one would either fail to compensate the deficiency or have to repeat the sujūd, which is unanimously unlegislated. Therefore, to avoid repetition, it is placed after salām. The passage also cites Al-`Ināyah and Tabyīn al-Ḥaqā’iq to support the Hanafī position, emphasizing that salām is a wājib and is given precedence by qiyās (analogy) to other wājibāt of prayer.

Key Terms
سجود السهو (sujūd al-sahw): Prostration for forgetfulness during prayer, performed to compensate for certain errors.
تكرر (takarrur): Repetition; the quality of being repeated. Here, the principle that sujūd al-sahw cannot be performed more than once in the same prayer.
السلام (al-salām): The final greeting of the prayer (said twice: to the right and left).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafī school, why is sujūd al-sahw performed after salām rather than before?
A) Because it is not permissible to prostrate before salām under any circumstances
B) Because salām is a wājib and takes precedence, and because the prostration cannot be repeated
C) Because the Prophet ﷺ always did it after salām
D) Because it is easier to remember the forgetfulness after salām

Key Takeaway
Sujūd al-sahw cannot be repeated; therefore, the Hanafī school delays it after salām to ensure all forgetfulness is covered in one prostration.
