Reciting Salawāt and Du‘ā in Qa‘dat al-Sahw
Applying the principle that du‘ā belongs at the end of prayer to qa‘dat al-sahw

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on reciting salawāt and du‘ā in qa‘dat al-sahw and explain the evidence based on the principle that du‘ā’s place is at the end of prayer.

Core Idea
Du‘ā and salawāt are recited in qa‘dat al-sahw because their place is the end of the prayer.

This passage from Uṣūl al-Hidāyah lays down a simple but powerful principle: supplication (du‘ā) belongs at the end of the prayer. The author then applies this principle to a specific case—the sitting after the prostrations of forgetfulness (qa‘dat al-sahw). By the end of this lesson, you will see how this principle determines the recommended actions in that sitting.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being discussed? It is the recitation of salawāt (blessings on the Prophet) and du‘ā (supplication) in the sitting after sujūd al-sahw. According to the Hanafi school, this is a sunnah mu’akkadah (emphasised sunnah).
The ruling is not fard or wajib; omission does not invalidate the prayer.
2
Locate the principle (dalil)
The evidence cited is the principle: 'Indeed, the place of supplication is the end of the prayer.' This principle is derived from the practice of the Prophet ﷺ and is established in the madhhab.
The principle itself functions as a dalīl; it is based on multiple aḥādīth about making du‘ā after tashahhud.
3
Apply the principle to the case
Since qa‘dat al-sahw is the final sitting of the prayer (occurring after the prostration and before salām), it is considered the end of the prayer. Therefore, the principle applies, and salawāt and du‘ā are to be recited there.
This is the wajh al-dalālah – the logical link between the principle and the ruling.
4
Note the authority
The passage mentions that this is the choice (ikhtiyār) of Imam al-Karkhī and is declared the ṣaḥīḥ (correct) view in Tabyīn al-Ḥaqā’iq. It is the muftā bihī position in the Hanafi school.
Al-Karkhī was a leading Hanafi jurist; his choice carries weight.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(١١٦) إِنَّ الدُّعَاءَ مَوْضِعُهُ آخِرُ الصَّلَاةِ.
ترجمہ: دعا کا مقام نماز کا آخری حصہ ہے۔
تشریح : مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ دعا کا حل نماز کا آخر ہے، یعنی نماز کے آخر میں دعا ہوتی ہے نہ کہ درمیان میں ۔ صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کرنے کے بعد اس بات کو ثابت کر رہے ہیں کہ سہو کے قعدے میں درود اور دعا پڑھی جائے گی ( قعدہ سہو سے مراد سجدہ کے بعد کا قعدہ ہے ) کیونکہ دعا کا محل آخر صلاۃ ہے، لہذا مذکورہ اصول کی بنیاد پر درود اور دعا بھی سہو کے قعدے کے بعد پڑھی جائے کیونکہ یہ نماز کا آخر ہے۔
(ثم النص العربي من البحر الرائق وتبيين الحقائق) أَنَّهُ يَأْتِي بِالصَّلَاةِ وَالدُّعَاءِ فِي قَعْدَةِ السَّهُو لِأَنَّ الدُّعَاءِ مَوْضِعُهُ آخِرُ الصَّلَاةِ. [البحر الرائق: كتاب الصلاة، باب سجود السهو، ص ۱۰۱، ط: دار الكتاب الإسلامي] وَيَأْتِي بِالصَّلَاةِ عَلَى النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ وَالدُّعَاءِ فِي قَعْدَةِ السُّهُو، وَهُوَ الصَّحِيحُ، لِأَنَّ مَوْضِعَهُمَا آخِرُ الصَّلَاةِ، وَهُوَ اخْتِيَارُ الْكَرْخِي. [تبيين الحقائق كتاب الصلاة، باب سجود السهو ج ۱ ص ۱۹۲، ط: دار الكتاب الإسلامي] الهداية كتاب الصلاة، باب سجود السهو ج ا ص ۱۶۵، ط: رحمانیه
(116) Indeed, the place of supplication is the end of the prayer. Translation: The place of supplication is the last part of the prayer. Explanation: The meaning of the aforementioned principle is that the place of supplication is the end of the prayer, i.e., supplication occurs at the end of the prayer, not in the middle. The author of Al-Hidayah, after mentioning this principle, is proving that in the sitting of forgetfulness (qa‘dat al-sahw, meaning the sitting after the prostration), one should recite salawāt (Durūd) and supplication (du‘ā), because the place of supplication is the end of the prayer. Therefore, based on the mentioned principle, salawāt and supplication are also recited after the sitting of forgetfulness, because it is the end of the prayer. (Then Arabic text from Al-Baḥr al-Rā’iq and Tabyīn al-Ḥaqā’iq) That he performs the salawāt and supplication in the sitting of forgetfulness because the place of supplication is the end of the prayer. [Al-Baḥr al-Rā’iq: Kitāb al-Ṣalāh, Bāb Sujūd al-Sahw, p. 101, Dār al-Kitāb al-Islāmī] And one recites the salawāt upon the Prophet ﷺ and the supplication in the sitting of forgetfulness, and that is the correct (view), because their place is the end of the prayer, and that is the choice of al-Karkhī. [Tabyīn al-Ḥaqā’iq: Kitāb al-Ṣalāh, Bāb Sujūd al-Sahw, vol. 1, p. 192, Dār al-Kitāb al-Islāmī] Al-Hidayah: Kitāb al-Ṣalāh, Bāb Sujūd al-Sahw, vol. 1, p. 165, R.
Source pages p. 132

Commentary
This passage presents a second principle from Uṣūl al-Hidāyah: the place of du‘ā (supplication) is at the end of the prayer. The commentator explains that this principle is used to determine that in the sitting after sujūd al-sahw (called qa‘dat al-sahw), one should recite both ṣalawāt (blessings on the Prophet) and du‘ā. This is because the sitting after sujūd al-sahw is considered the final part of the prayer, and it is established that du‘ā is made at the end. The passage cites Al-Baḥr al-Rā’iq and Tabyīn al-Ḥaqā’iq to confirm that this is the correct (ṣaḥīḥ) view, and it is the choice of Imam al-Karkhī. Thus, the practical ruling: in the final sitting after performing sujūd al-sahw, one should recite the tashahhud, then ṣalawāt upon the Prophet, and then make du‘ā (e.g., rabbanā ātinā) before saying the salām.

Key Terms
قعدة السهو (qa‘dat al-sahw): The sitting after performing sujūd al-sahw, before the final salām.
الدعاء (al-du‘ā): Supplication; personal prayer to Allah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the principle in this passage, why are salawāt and du‘ā recited in qa‘dat al-sahw?
A) Because qa‘dat al-sahw is the only sitting in the prayer.
B) Because the place of du‘ā is the end of the prayer, and qa‘dat al-sahw is the end.
C) Because the Prophet always made du‘ā after sujūd.
D) Because al-Karkhī mandated it.

Key Takeaway
The principle 'the place of du‘ā is the end of the prayer' establishes that in qa‘dat al-sahw, salawāt and du‘ā are sunnah mu’akkadah.

Salah — Prayer

6 min
The Three Causes of Sujūd al-Sahw
Principle defining triggers for sujūd al-sahw

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three causes that obligate sujūd al-sahw and distinguish between them.

Core Idea
Sujūd al-sahw is only required for three forgetful acts: omitting a wājib, delaying a wājib, or delaying a rukn.

In the Hanafi school, the prostration of forgetfulness (sujūd al-sahw) is not required for every mistake in prayer. The classical texts lay down a precise principle to determine when it becomes mandatory. This lesson unpacks that ruling statement from Al-Hidayah, clarifying the three specific situations that trigger the obligation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Sujūd al-sahw is a wajib act that compensates for certain forgetful omissions or delays in prayer. This principle tells us exactly when it becomes obligatory.
It is not fard; if omitted, the prayer is still valid but deficient.
2
List the three causes
From the text: (1) leaving (tark) a wājib, (2) delaying (ta’khīr) a wājib, (3) delaying a rukn. All must be done forgetfully (sāhiyan).
The word 'sāhiyan' at the end qualifies all three.
3
Distinguish between wājib and rukn
Omission of a wājib triggers sujūd al-sahw; omission of a rukn invalidates the prayer. Only delay of a rukn triggers sujūd. This is a key Hanafi distinction.
Knowing which acts are wājib and which are arkan is essential for correct application.
4
Apply to a scenario
For example, if a person forgetfully recites the Sūrah after rukū‘ instead of before, they have delayed a wājib and must perform sujūd al-sahw.
The same applies to forgetting to recite the Sūrah entirely (leaving a wājib).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(١١٧) إِنَّ سَجْدَةَ السَّهْوِ لَا تَجِبُ إِلَّا بِتَرْكِ وَاجِبٍ أَوْ تَأْخِيرِهِ أَوْ تَأْخِيرِ رُكُنٍ سَاهِيًا .
(117) Indeed, the prostration of forgetfulness is not obligatory except by leaving a wājib, or delaying it, or delaying a rukn forgetfully.
Source pages p. 132

Commentary
This passage states a principle that defines the causes for which sujūd al-sahw becomes obligatory according to the Hanafī school. It is a straightforward ruling statement. The prostration for forgetfulness is required only in three scenarios: (1) leaving out a wājib (obligatory component) of the prayer, e.g., forgetting to recite Sūrat al-Fātiḥa in the first two rak‘ahs; (2) delaying a wājib from its proper place, e.g., reciting the Sūrah after rukū‘ instead of before; (3) delaying a rukn (pillar) forgetfully, e.g., performing rukū‘ after the qirā’ah of the third rak‘ah due to forgetfulness. This principle helps the student identify when sujūd al-sahw is mandatory versus when it is just recommended or unnecessary. The Hanafī school distinguishes between wājib and fard in prayer; only omission or delay of a wājib or delay of a rukn triggers sujūd al-sahw. Omission of a fard (pillar) would invalidate the prayer and require repetition, not sujūd al-sahw.

Key Terms
واجب (wājib): An obligatory component of prayer that is not a rukn (pillar); its omission or delay requires sujūd al-sahw.
ركن (rukn): A pillar of prayer; its intentional omission invalidates prayer, but forgetful delay requires sujūd al-sahw.
ساهيا (sāhiyan): Forgetfully; unintentionally; the state of forgetfulness. The act must be done forgetfully for sujūd al-sahw to be due.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following requires sujūd al-sahw according to this principle?
A) Intentionally leaving a fard
B) Forgetfully delaying a rukn
C) Forgetting a sunnah
D) Deliberately omitting a wājib

Key Takeaway
Sujūd al-sahw is only obligatory in three specific forgetful incidents: omitting or delaying a wājib, or delaying a rukn.

The Principle: Dua is at the End of Salah
Principle stating the place of dua in salah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi principle that dua belongs at the end of salah and apply it to the sitting after sajdah al-sahw.

Core Idea
Dua belongs at the end of salah — including the final sitting after sajdah al-sahw.

This lesson presents a foundational Hanafi principle: the proper place for supplication (du'a) is at the end of the prayer (akhir al-salah). The passage from al-Hidayah applies this principle to the sitting of forgetfulness (qa'dat al-sahw), affirming that salat and dua are recited there. This reflects the Hanafi emphasis on precise placement within the prayer's structure.

Guided Path
1
Identify the principle
The text states: 'Indeed, the place of supplication is the end of prayer.' Recognize this as a foundational rule.
2
Apply the principle to the case
The text applies it to the sitting of forgetfulness (qa'dat al-sahw) — because it is the end of salah, salat and dua are recited there.
3
Note the tarjih
The text declares this the correct view (sahih) and the choice of al-Karkhi, indicating the preferred Hanafi position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إِنَّ الدُّعَاءَ مَوْضِعُهُ آخِرُ الصَّلَاةِ. أَنَّهُ يَأْتِي بِالصَّلَاةِ وَالدُّعَاءِ فِي قَعْدَةِ السَّهُو لِأَنَّ الدُّعَاءِ مَوْضِعُهُ آخِرُ الصَّلَاةِ. وَيَأْتِي بالصَّلَاةِ عَلَى النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ وَالدُّعَاء فِي قَعْدَةِ السُّهُو، وَهُوَ الصَّحِيحُ، لأنَّ مَوْضِعَهُمَا آخِرُ الصَّلاةِ، وَهُوَ اخْتِيَارُ الْكَرْخِي.
Indeed, the place of supplication is the end of prayer. That he performs the prayer (salat upon the Prophet) and supplication in the sitting of forgetfulness because the place of supplication is the end of prayer. And he performs prayer upon the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, and supplication in the sitting of forgetfulness, and that is the correct view, because their place is the end of prayer; and it is the choice of al-Karkhi.
Source pages p. 132

Commentary
This passage presents a foundational principle from the Hanafi school regarding the placement of dua (supplication) within the prayer (salah). The principle states that dua is to be made at the end of salah. The text then applies this principle to the case of sajdah al-sahw (prostration of forgetfulness): in the final sitting (qa'dah) after the sajdah al-sahw, the worshipper should recite the salat (blessings on the Prophet) and dua, because this qa'dah is the end of the prayer. This is affirmed as the correct view (sahih) and is the choice of Imam al-Karkhi, a prominent Hanafi scholar. The passage emphasizes that the end of salah, not the middle, is the proper time for these supplications.

Key Terms
الدعاء (al-du'a'): Supplication; personal plea to Allah.
آخر الصلاة (akhir al-salah): The end of the prayer, specifically the final sitting before or after salutations.
قعدة السهو (qa'dat al-sahw): The sitting performed after sajdah al-sahw (prostration of forgetfulness) to complete the prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the principle from al-Hidayah, where is the proper place for supplication (dua) in salah?
A) At the beginning of salah
B) In the middle of salah after recitation
C) At the end of salah
D) During sajdah

Key Takeaway
The place for supplication in salah is the end of the prayer, specifically the final sitting, and this applies also to the sitting after sajdah al-sahw.

Causes and Timing of Sajdah al-Sahw
Principle on causes and timing of sajdah al-sahw

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three causes of sajdah al-sahw and explain the preferred timing (after salam) with its proof.

Core Idea
Sajdah al-sahw is wajib only for omission/delay of a wajib or delay of a rukn, and is performed after salam.

Sajdah al-sahw (prostration of forgetfulness) is a compensatory act in prayer. This lesson clarifies exactly when it becomes obligatory and when it does not. It also resolves a common confusion: whether to prostrate before or after the salam (salutation). The Hanafi school has a precise, evidence-based position that safeguards the integrity of prayer without causing unnecessary invalidation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the principle
Read the opening sentence: sajdah al-sahw is obligatory only for three causes: omitting a wajib, delaying a wajib, or delaying a rukn forgetfully. Memorize this as the core rule.
Wajib is a component whose omission requires compensation but does not invalidate the prayer; rukn is an integral whose omission invalidates.
2
Understand the timing issue
The text confirms both before and after salam are permissible by hadith. But the Hanafi preference is after salam, based on authentic hadith and analogy: salam itself is a wajib, so it should come first. Also, sajdah does not repeat, so delaying it after salam allows it to compensate even if one forgets the salam.
This tarjih is a matter of preference, not a strict obligation.
3
Apply to a scenario: addition of a similar action
If a person adds an action that is from the same genre as prayer (e.g., an extra sajdah) but not part of its prescribed structure, sajdah al-sahw becomes wajib. The text explicitly states that this proves sajdah is wajib, like blood sacrifices (dimaa') in Hajj.
This reinforces that sajdah is legislated to compensate for deficiencies.
4
Distinguish from other mistakes
Sajdah al-sahw is NOT required for missing a sunnah or mustahab action, nor for intentional actions (which break the prayer entirely). Only forgetful omission or delay of wajib or delay of rukn trigger it.
This distinction prevents over-application and confusion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إِنَّ سَجْدَةَ السَّهْوِ لَا تَجِبُ إِلَّا بِتَرْكِ وَاجِبٍ أَوْ تَأْخِيرِهِ أَوْ تَأْخِيرِ رُكُنٍ سَاهِيًا . إِذَا سَجَدَ زَمَانَ سَهْوِهِ وَأَمْكَنَ أَنْ يَسْهُوَ بَعْدَهُ فَإِنْ سَهَا فَإِمَّا أَنْ يَسْجُدَ ثَانِيَا أَوْ لَا، فَإِنْ لَمْ يَسْجُدُ بَقِيَ نَقْصُ لَازِمٌ لَا جَبُرَ لَهُ، وَإِنْ سَجَدَ تَتَكَرَّرُ السَّجْدَةُ وَهُوَ غَيْرُ مَشْرُوعِ بِالْإِجْمَاعِ فَلَزِمَ التَّأْخِيرُ. وَلَا خِلَافَ فِي الْجَوَازِ قَبْلَ السَّلَامِ وَبَعْدَهُ لِصِحَةِ الْحَدِيثِ فِيهِمَا وَالتَّرْجِيحُ لِمَا قُلْنَا مِنْ جِهَةِ الْمَعْنَى أَنَّ السَّلَامَ مِنْ الْوَاجِبَاتِ فَيُقَدَّمُ عَلَى سُجُودِ السَّهْوِ قِيَاسًا عَلَى غَيْرِهِ مِنْ وَاجِبَاتِ الصَّلَاةِ، وَلِأَنَّ سُجُودَ السَّهُوِ مِمَّا لَا يَتَكَرَّرُ فَيُؤَخَّرُ عَنْ السَّلَامِ حَتَّى لَوْ سَهَا عَنْ السَّلَامِ يَنْجَبِرُ بِهِ. وَالسَّهُو يَلْزَمُهُ إِذَا زَادَ فِي صَلَاتِهِ فِعَلَا مِنْ جِنْسِهَا لَيْسَ مِنْهَا فِي قَوْلِهِ يَلْزَمُهُ تَصْرِيحٌ بِأَنَّهُ وَاجِبٌ وَهُوَ الصَّحِيحُ ، لأنَّهُ شُرِعَ لِجَبْرِ النُّقْصَانِ فَكَانَ وَاجِبًا كَالدِّمَاءِ فِي الْحَجِّ ...
Indeed, the prostration of forgetfulness is not obligatory except for the omission of an obligatory act, or its delay, or the delay of an integral (rukn) forgetfully. When he prostrates at the time of his forgetfulness and it is possible that he forgets after it, then if he forgets, he either prostrates a second time or not; if he does not prostrate, a necessary deficiency remains that cannot be compensated; if he prostrates, the prostration is repeated, and that is not prescribed by consensus, so delay becomes necessary. And there is no disagreement regarding the permissibility (of sajdah) before and after the salutation due to the authenticity of hadith on both; the preponderance is for what we said from a meaning perspective: that the salutation is among the obligatory acts, so it takes precedence over sajdah al-sahw by analogy to other obligatory acts of prayer; and because sajdah al-sahw is something that does not repeat, so it is delayed after the salutation, so that even if one forgets the salutation, it is compensated by it. And forgetfulness necessitates (sajdah) when he adds in his prayer an action from its type that is not part of it; in his statement 'it necessitates' is an explicit ruling that it is obligatory, and that is the correct view, because it is prescribed to compensate deficiency, so it is obligatory like the sacrificial offerings (dimaa') in Hajj...
Source pages p. 132

Commentary
This passage establishes the two main causes of sajdah al-sahw: (1) omitting or delaying a wajib (obligatory component, such as the first sitting or reciting a prayer in the first sitting), or (2) delaying a rukn (integral part, such as standing or bowing) due to forgetfulness. Intentionally omitting a rukn invalidates the prayer; sajdah al-sahw is not sufficient. Omitting sunnah or mustahab actions does not require sajdah. The text then addresses the timing of sajdah al-sahw: whether before or after the salam (salutation). It states that both are permissible based on authentic hadith, but the preferred view (tarjih) is to perform it after salam. The reasoning is that salam itself is a wajib, so it should come before sajdah, analogous to other obligatory acts. Moreover, sajdah al-sahw is not repeated; if performed after salam, it can compensate even if one forgets to say salam. Finally, the passage adds that if a person inadvertently adds an action of the same genre as prayer (e.g., extra prostrations) that is not an actual part of the prayer, sajdah al-sahw becomes obligatory. This is explicitly stated as obligatory (wajib) because sajdah is legislated to make up for deficiency, similar to how blood sacrifices (dimaa') are obligatory in Hajj to compensate for deficiencies.

Key Terms
سجدة السهو (sajdat al-sahw): Prostration of forgetfulness; two prostrations performed to compensate for omissions or delays due to forgetfulness in prayer.
واجب (wajib): A component of prayer that is obligatory but not integral; omission requires compensation via sajdah al-sahw.
ركن (rukn): An integral pillar of prayer; omission invalidates the prayer unless made up with sajdah al-sahw only if delayed, not omitted entirely.
سهو (sahw): Forgetfulness; the cause for sajdah al-sahw.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Hidayah, when does sajdah al-sahw become obligatory?
A) For any mistake in prayer
B) Only for omission of a fard (integral)
C) For omission or delay of a wajib, or delay of a rukn by forgetfulness
D) For adding extra rak'ahs intentionally

Key Takeaway
Sajdah al-sahw is a wajib compensatory act triggered only by forgetful omission/delay of a wajib, delay of a rukn, or addition of a similar action; the preferred timing is after salam.

The Three Causes of Sajdah al-Sahw and Its Proof
Explaining when Sajdah al-Sahw becomes obligatory

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three causes of Sajdah al-Sahw in the Hanafi school and explain why it is wajib through qiyas to dam in Hajj.

Core Idea
Sajdah al-Sahw is wajib only for leaving or delaying a wajib, or delaying a rukn — like dam in Hajj, it compensates deficiency.

This passage from Al-Hidayah sets forth the precise conditions under which Sajdah al-Sahw (prostration of forgetfulness) becomes obligatory. Many students mistakenly think it applies to any mistake, but the Hanafi school limits it to three specific scenarios. Furthermore, the author provides a proof via qiyas (analogy) to the blood offering (dam) in Hajj, establishing the wajib status of Sajdah al-Sahw.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its subject
Determine what is being ruled upon (Sajdah al-Sahw) and its legal classification (wajib). Note the three specific causes that trigger it.
2
Locate the dalil
The author uses qiyas: Sajdah al-Sahw is analogized to dam (blood offering) in Hajj. Identify the original case (asl) and the new case (far').
Asl: dam in Hajj; far': Sajdah al-Sahw in prayer.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Explain why the analogy holds: both are legislated to compensate for a deficiency in worship. This is the effective cause (illa).
Illah: legislated to compensate for deficiency.
4
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) do not differentiate between fard and wajib, and may consider Sajdah al-Sahw sunnah in some cases. Understand the basis of disagreement.
The difference stems from the classification of wajib vs. fard.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi within the school, supported by the consensus of the Sahibayn and the explicit reasoning of Al-Marghinani.
Zahir al-Riwayah supports this ruling.

Translation: Sajdah al-Sahw is not obligatory except upon leaving a wajib, or delaying a wajib, or delaying a rukn due to forgetfulness. Commentary: This principle mentions the matters due to which Sajdah al-Sahw becomes obligatory: leaving a wajib, delaying in performing a wajib, delaying in performing a rukn. Deliberately leaving a rukn invalidates the prayer and requires repetition; Sajdah al-Sahw is not sufficient. Similarly, leaving a sunnah or mustahabb does not require Sajdah al-Sahw. The author of Hidayah, after stating this principle, proves that if a person adds an act that is from the genus of prayer but not a part of it, e.g., three or four prostrations instead of two, then Sajdah al-Sahw is wajib because this addition is not free from delaying a rukn or delaying a wajib. Summary: Sajdah al-Sahw becomes obligatory due to forgetfully leaving a wajib (like first sitting), delaying a wajib (like standing after the final sitting in a two-rak'ah prayer), or delaying a rukn (like doing three sajdahs in one rak'ah, delaying the standing). (His statement: 'And forgetfulness becomes binding upon him when he adds to his prayer an act from its genus that is not from it' – in his statement 'binding upon him' is a clear indication that it is wajib, and that is sound, because it was legislated to compensate the deficiency, so it is wajib like the blood (offerings) in Hajj. And when ...
Source pages p. 133

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Hanafi school regarding the causes of Sajdah al-Sahw. The author first gives the translation of the principle from Hidayah, then elaborates. The core ruling is that Sajdah al-Sahw is only obligatory in three cases: (1) leaving a wajib of prayer, (2) delaying a wajib, or (3) delaying a rukn. Deliberate omission of a rukn nullifies the prayer. Adding an extraneous act that is similar to prayer parts (like extra sajdah) triggers Sajdah al-Sahw because it entails delay. The Arabic quote from the text confirms that such addition makes Sajdah al-Sahw wajib, analogized to the required blood offering in Hajj to compensate deficiency. The author emphasizes that deliberate or forgetful actions are distinguished: intentional omission of wajib or rukn has different consequences. The proof relies on the purpose of Sajdah al-Sahw: to repair defects.

Key Terms
سجدہ سہو (sajdah al-sahw): Prostration of forgetfulness performed to rectify omissions or delays in prayer
واجب (wajib): Obligatory element of prayer that is not as strongly proven as fard; omission requires compensation (sajdah al-sahw)
رکن (rukn): Essential pillar of prayer; deliberate omission invalidates prayer; forgetful delay requires sajdah al-sahw

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Delaying the final salam due to confusion about rak'ahs

Key Takeaway
Sajdah al-Sahw is wajib only for three specific forgetful acts: leaving a wajib, delaying a wajib, or delaying a rukn, and its obligation is proven by qiyas to dam in Hajj.

The Imam's Forgetfulness and Its Effect on Followers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that Sajdah al-Sahw is wajib on followers when the Imam forgets, and explain the causal link (talil) that establishes the obligation.

Core Idea
The Imam's deficiency transfers to followers because their prayer is linked for validity.

This passage from Al-Hidayah establishes a key principle in Hanafi fiqh regarding collective prayer: any deficiency in the Imam's prayer, such as forgetfulness, is attributed to the followers as well. Hence, if the Imam's forgetfulness necessitates Sajdah al-Sahw, the followers must also perform it. The ruling is based on the legal maxim that the cause established in the origin (Imam) is established in the follower (muqtadi).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act under discussion? The followers performing Sajdah al-Sahw. The ruling is that it is wajib (obligatory) when the Imam's forgetfulness triggers it.
The hukm level is wajib, not fard, because the evidence is from a general principle.
2
Locate the legal maxim
The passage states the maxim clearly: 'The deficiency established in the Imam's prayer becomes established in the followers' prayer.' Understand the wording.
The Arabic uses 'tamakkun' (establishment) to indicate that the deficiency applies fully.
3
Trace the causal link (talil)
Why does the deficiency transfer? Because the followers' prayer is connected to the Imam's prayer in validity and invalidity. If the Imam's prayer is deficient, the followers' prayer is likewise affected.
This is based on the principle that the follower (tabi') shares the ruling of the origin (asl).
4
Note the inter-madhhab dispute
The Shafi'i school holds that followers are not obliged to perform Sajdah al-Sahw for the Imam's forgetfulness. Understand the opposing view and the Hanafi response.
The practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf) is whether followers must follow the Imam in sujud al-sahw.

Source Text

تشریح : مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ اگر امام کی نماز میں کمی بیشی ہو جائے تو یہ کمی بیشی مقتدیوں کی نماز میں بھی ثابت ہوگی۔

(قَوْلُهُ: وَسَهْوُ الْإِمَامِ يُوجِبُ عَلَى الْمُؤْتَمِّ السُّجُودَ السُّجُودُ مَنْصُوبٌ لِأَنَّهُ مَفْعُولٌ يُوجِبُ التَّقَرُّرَ السَّبَبَ الْمُوجِبَ فِى حَقِّ الْأَصْلِ أَرَادَ بِالسَّبَبِيَّةِ السَّهْوَ، وَبِالْأَصْلِ الْإِمَامَ، فَلَمَّا وَجَبَ عَلَيْهِ وَجَبَ عَلَى مَنْ خَلْفَهُ، لِأَنَّ النُّقْصَانَ الْمُتَمَكِّنَ فِي صَلَاتِهِ مُتَمَكِّنٌ فِي صَلَاةِ الْقَوْمِ، لِأَنَّ صَلَاتَهُمْ مُتَعَلِّقَةٌ بِصَلَاتِهِ صِحَّةً وَفَسَادًا، فَوَجَبَ عَلَيْهِمُ السُّجُودُ.

Translation: The deficiency that becomes established in the Imam's prayer becomes established in the followers' prayer. Commentary: This principle means that if there is an excess or deficiency in the Imam's prayer, that excess or deficiency becomes established in the followers' prayer. The author of Hidayah, after mentioning this principle, wants to prove that the Imam's mistake also makes Sajdah al-Sahw obligatory upon the followers, i.e., if such forgetfulness occurs from the Imam that necessitates Sajdah al-Sahw, then Sajdah al-Sahw becomes wajib upon the followers due to following the Imam. (119) Surely, the establishment of the causing cause in respect of the origin is establishment in respect of its follower. Translation: The establishment of the causing cause in respect of the origin is its establishment in respect of its follower. Commentary: This principle means that the cause that is established in respect of the origin also becomes established in respect of its follower, because the follower is the deputy of the origin. The author of Hidayah, after mentioning this principle, is branching out from it: e.g., the Imam's intention... Indeed, the deficiency that becomes established in the prayer of the Imam becomes established in the prayer of the people. (His statement: And the Imam's forgetfulness obligates upon the follower the prostration; 'the prostration' is accusative because it is the object of 'obligates'; the establishment of the causing cause in respect of the origin; he meant by 'causing cause' the forgetfulness, and by 'origin' the Imam. So when it became obligatory upon him, it became obligatory upon those behind him, because the deficiency established in his prayer is established in the prayer of the people, since their prayer is connected to his prayer in validity and invalidity, so the prostration became obligatory upon them. (Al-Binayah, Kitab al-Salah, Bab Sujud al-Sahw, vol. 2 p. 616, Dar al-Kitab al-Ilmiyyah) (Al-Hidayah, Kitab al-Salah, Bab Sujud al-Sahw, vol. 1 p. 165, Rahmaniyyah)

Commentary
This passage presents a principle of Hanafi fiqh regarding collective prayer. It states that any deficiency (such as forgetfulness) occurring in the Imam's prayer is considered to have occurred in the followers' prayer as well. Hence, if the Imam's forgetfulness necessitates Sajdah al-Sahw, the followers must also perform it. This is based on the legal maxim that the cause (forgetfulness) established in the origin (Imam) is established in the follower (muqtadi) because the follower's prayer is dependent on the Imam's prayer for validity. The text quotes from Al-Hidayah and Al-Binayah to support this. The ruling is that Sajdah al-Sahw becomes wajib on both Imam and followers when the Imam forgets, due to the connection between their prayers.

Key Terms
سجدہ سہو (sajdah al-sahw): Prostration for forgetfulness, obligatory on both Imam and followers when the Imam forgets
سبب موجب (sabab mujib): The effective cause (forgetfulness) that necessitates the ruling
اصل (asl): The origin (Imam) whose ruling is transferred to the follower (tabi')

Deficiency Transfer in Congregational Prayer: Sajdah al-Sahw for the Follower
States a legal maxim and applies it to sajdah al-sahw

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi maxim about the transfer of deficiency in congregational prayer and apply it to determine when sajdah al-sahw is wajib on the followers.

Core Idea
A substantive deficiency in the imam's prayer is attributed to the congregation, making sajdah al-sahw wajib on all followers.

This lesson unpacks a foundational legal maxim from al-Hidayah that connects the imam's prayer errors to the congregation. Understanding this principle explains why followers must perform sajdah al-sahw even when they themselves did not commit the error. The maxim relies on the concept of legal connection (ta'alliq) between the imam's prayer and that of the followers.

Guided Path
1
State the maxim
Read the Arabic maxim and its translation. Grasp the key term 'al-taqsān al-mutamakkin' (established deficiency).
The maxim is: 'Indeed, the deficiency that becomes established in the prayer of the imam becomes established in the prayer of the congregation.'
2
Identify the legal connection
Recognise that the follower's prayer is legally tied to the imam's – validity, invalidity, and deficiencies transfer.
This connection (ta'alliq) is the basis for the maxim.
3
Apply to sajdah al-sahw
If the imam commits an error that requires sajdah al-sahw, that deficiency is attributed to the followers, making sajdah al-sahw wajib on them as well.
The error might be omitting a wajib (e.g., first tashahhud) or delaying it.
4
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Some schools hold that sajdah al-sahw is not obligatory on the follower unless the follower also commits the same error.
The Hanafi position relies on the connection maxim.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إِنَّ التَّقْصَانَ الْمُتَمَكِّنَ فِى صَلَاةِ الْإِمَامِ مُتَمَكِّنْ فِى صَلَاةِ الْقَوْمِ. ترجمہ: وہ نقصان جو امام کی نماز میں ثابت ہو جائے تو وہ مقتدیوں کی نماز میں بھی ثابت ہوگا۔ تشریح : مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ اگر امام کی نماز میں کمی بیشی ہو جائے تو یہ کمی بیشی مقتدیوں کی نماز میں بھی ثابت ہوگی۔ ماحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول کو ذکر کرنے کے بعد اس بات کو ثابت کرنا چاہتے ہیں کہ امام کی غلطی مقتدیوں پر بھی سجدہ سہو واجب کرتی ہے، یعنی اگر امام سے نماز میں ایسا سہو ہو جائے جس سے سجدہ سہو واجب ہوتا ہے تو اس صورت میں مقتدیوں پر بھی سجدہ سہو واجب ہوگا امام کی اقتداء کی وجہ سے.
Indeed, the deficiency that becomes established in the prayer of the imam becomes established in the prayer of the congregation. Translation: The deficiency that becomes established in the imam's prayer also becomes established in the followers' prayer. Explanation: The meaning of the mentioned principle is that if there is any excess or deficiency in the imam's prayer, this excess or deficiency will also be established in the followers' prayer. The author of al-Hidayah, after mentioning this principle, intends to prove that the imam's error obligates sajdah al-sahw upon the followers as well. That is, if an oversight occurs in the imam's prayer that would necessitate sajdah al-sahw, then sajdah al-sahw becomes obligatory upon the followers too due to following the imam.
Source pages p. 134

Commentary
This passage presents a foundational legal maxim (qawida) concerning congregational prayer. The passage type is a ruling with explanation. The maxim states that any deficiency (naqs) that takes hold in the imam's prayer is also considered to be present in the followers' prayer. The author then uses this maxim to establish a specific ruling: the imam's forgetfulness (sahw) obligates sajdah al-sahw upon the followers as well. This is because the deficiency is transferred to the followers' prayer through connection (ta'alliq) — the followers' prayer is linked to the imam's prayer both in validity and invalidity. Thus, if the imam commits an act that requires sajdah al-sahw, the followers must also perform it. The commentary explains this clearly, emphasizing that the obligation on the followers is due to their following (iqtida).

Key Terms
التَّقْصَانَ الْمُتَمَكِّنَ (al-taqsān al-mutamakkin): A deficiency that is firmly established or takes hold in the prayer, meaning a substantive error or omission that affects the prayer's validity.
سجدہ سہو (sajdah al-sahw): Two prostrations performed to compensate for forgetfulness (sahw) during prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the maxim 'al-taqsān al-mutamakkin...', what is the consequence if the imam forgetfully omits a wajib in prayer?
A) The follower must perform sajdah al-sahw as well.
B) The follower's prayer becomes invalid.
C) The follower does nothing; only the imam performs sajdah.
D) The follower must repeat the prayer.

Key Takeaway
The maxim 'a deficiency in the imam's prayer is also in the congregation's prayer' makes sajdah al-sahw wajib on the followers when the imam commits an error requiring it.

The Maxim: Cause Established for the Principal Applies to the Follower
States a legal maxim and applies it to iqamah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi maxim regarding principal and follower, and apply it to determine that the imam's intention of iqamah obligates the followers to complete four rak'ahs without their own intention.

Core Idea
The imam's intention of iqamah makes the follower's prayer four rak'ahs—the follower's status changes with the leader.

This lesson introduces a key legal maxim used in Hanafi fiqh to extend obligations from a principal to its follower. The context is prayer: when a traveling imam intends to settle during the prayer, the followers automatically become residents and must complete the full prayer, even without their own intention. This principle illustrates the representative relationship between imam and follower.

Guided Path
1
Identify the maxim and its components
The maxim states: 'The establishment of a causative factor (sabab mujib) for the principal is establishment for the follower.' Identify 'asl' (the imam) and 'tabi'' (the follower). The cause here is the imam's intention of iqamah.
The maxim is a general principle applicable in various fiqh chapters.
2
Understand the basis: the follower as deputy
The follower is considered a deputy (na'ib) of the imam. Therefore, the imam's causative condition transfers to the follower, binding them in the same ruling.
This is based on the analogy that the imam represents the congregation.
3
Apply the maxim to the case of iqamah
When the imam intends iqamah (becoming a resident) during prayer, a cause is established for him that changes the prayer from qasr (2 rak'ahs) to full (4). By the maxim, this cause applies to the followers, making their prayer also full.
The imam's intention alone suffices; the followers need not have their own intention.
4
Derive the ruling for the followers
The followers must complete 4 rak'ahs even if they did not intend iqamah. Their prayer becomes tamam (complete) due to the imam's intention.
If a follower leaves after 2 rak'ahs, his prayer is invalid because he missed required rak'ahs.
5
Note the ikhtilaf
Some schools require the follower's own intention of iqamah. The Hanafi school relies on this maxim to dispense with that requirement, citing the principal-follower relationship.
This ikhtilaf has practical consequences in congregational travel prayers.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إِنَّ تَقَرُّرَ السَّبَبِ الْمُوْجَبِ فِي حَقِّ الْأَصْلِ تَقَرُّرٌ فِي حَقِّ تَابِعِهِ. ترجمہ: اصل کے حق میں سبب موجب کا ثابت ہونا یہ اس کے تابع کے حق میں ثابت ہونا ہے۔ تشریح : مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ جو سبب موجب اصل کے حق میں ثابت ہوتا ہے تو وہ سبب اصل کے تابع کے حق میں بھی ثابت ہوگا کیونکہ تابع اصل کا نائب ہے، جیسے مذکورہ بالا اصول میں امام کی غلطی سے مقتدی پر بھی سجدہ سہو واجب ہوتا ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کرنے کے بعد اس پر تفریح کر رہے ہیں کہ امام کی نیت اقامت سے مقتدی پر بھی اقامت کا حکم لازم ہوتا ہے، یعنی اگر مسافر امام نے دورانِ نماز اقامت کی نیت کر لی اب امام پر دو کے بجائے چار رکعت لازم ہوئی ، تو اس امام کی نیت اقامت سے مقتدی بھی مقیم شمار ہوگا اور مقتدی کی بھی شائی نماز رباعی ہو جائے گی ،اگر چہ مقتدی نے اقامت کی نیت نہ کی ہو، کیونکہ مذکورہ اصول کی بنیاد پر مقتدی کے حق میں بھی سبب موجب ثابت ہوگا. 
وَلِأَجْلِ تَقَرُّرِ السَّبَبِ الْمُوجِبِ فِي حَقِّ الْأَصْلِ يَلْزَمُ الْمُؤْتَمَّ حُكْمُ الْإِقَامَةِ بِنِيَّةِ الْإِمَامِ يَعْنِي إِذَا نَوَى الْإِمَامُ فِي وَسَطِ صَلَاتِهِ الْإِقَامَةَ يَصِيرُ فَرْضُهُمْ أَرْبَعًا، وَإِنْ لَمْ يُوجَدْ مِنَ الْقَوْمِ النِّيَّةُ.
Indeed, the establishment of the causative factor in the right of the principal is establishment in the right of its follower. Translation: The existence of a cause that obligates something for the principal means it also exists for the follower. Explanation: The meaning of the mentioned principle is that when a causative factor is established for the principal, that same factor is also established for the follower, because the follower is a deputy of the principal. For example, in the previous principle, the imam's error obligates sajdah al-sahw upon the follower as well. The author of al-Hidayah, after mentioning this principle, elaborates that the imam's intention of iqamah (completing the prayer as a resident) imposes the ruling of iqamah upon the follower. That is, if a traveling imam intends iqamah during his prayer, then four rak'ahs become obligatory upon him instead of two. Consequently, the follower also becomes considered a resident and his prayer becomes four rak'ahs, even if the follower did not intend iqamah, because based on the mentioned principle, the causative factor is also established for the follower. And because of the establishment of the causative factor in the right of the principal, the ruling of iqamah becomes binding upon the follower by the imam's intention; meaning if the imam intends iqamah in the middle of his prayer, their obligatory prayer becomes four rak'ahs, even if the congregation did not have the intention.
Source pages p. 134

Commentary
This passage presents a second legal maxim concerning the relationship between a principal (asl) and its follower (tabi'). The passage type is a ruling with explanation and proof. The maxim states that if a cause (sabab) that produces an obligation is established for the principal, it is also established for the follower. The follower stands in the position of the principal's deputy (na'ib). The author then applies this maxim to a specific case: the imam's intention of iqamah (to become a resident) during prayer. If the imam, originally a traveler, intends to settle (iqamah) mid-prayer, his own prayer changes from two to four rak'ahs. According to this maxim, the same cause (the intention) applies to the followers, so they also become residents and must complete four rak'ahs, even without their own intention. The supporting Arabic text from al-Binayah clarifies: because the cause is established for the imam (the principal), the ruling of iqamah becomes binding on the followers. This shows the principle's practical effect in Hanafi fiqh.

Key Terms
السبب الموجب (al-sabab al-mujib): The causative factor that necessitates a ruling; in this context, it refers to the imam's intention of iqamah that triggers an obligation.
الإقامة (al-iqamah): The intention to settle (become a resident) in a place, changing the traveler's prayer from qasr to full.
تابع (tabi'): Follower, specifically the person who prays behind an imam (mu'tamm).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a traveling imam intends iqamah during Zuhr prayer (which would normally be 2 rak'ahs qasr), what happens to the followers' prayer?
A) The followers' prayer remains 2 rak'ahs.
B) The followers must also intend iqamah individually for their prayer to become 4 rak'ahs.
C) The followers' prayer becomes 4 rak'ahs because the imam's intention establishes the cause for them.
D) The followers must leave the congregation and complete their own prayer as travelers.

Key Takeaway
The imam's intention of iqamah during prayer makes the followers' prayer full (4 rak'ahs) because the causative factor established for the imam applies to the followers.

Proximity to Sitting: When Forgetting the First Sitting Does Not Require Sajdah al-Sahw
States a maxim and applies it to the case of forgetting the first sitting

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi maxim 'what is close to a thing takes its ruling' to determine the ruling when a person forgetfully stands from the first sitting in prayer.

Core Idea
If you are closer to sitting than standing, you are legally still sitting — no extra prostration needed.

Have you ever forgotten to recite the tashahhud in the first sitting of a prayer and started to stand up? This lesson explores a powerful Hanafi maxim that resolves the confusion: whether you should sit back down and whether you need to perform the extra prostration of forgetfulness (sajdah al-sahw). By understanding the principle of proximity, you will be able to handle this common scenario with confidence.

Guided Path
1
State the maxim
Read the Arabic and English of the maxim: 'What is close to a thing takes its ruling.' Understand that this is a general legal principle applicable in various fields of fiqh.
2
Identify the scenario
Recognize the specific case: a person forgetfully stands up from the first sitting (qaidah ula) of a prayer with three or four rak'ahs.
The first sitting is a wajib in the Hanafi school; omitting it intentionally invalidates the prayer.
3
Determine proximity
At the moment of remembering, assess the person's posture: has he fully risen to a standing position, or is he still closer to sitting? The key term is 'aqrab ila al-qu'ud' (closer to sitting).
This is a physical assessment: hands still on the ground, knees bent, back not fully erect.
4
Apply the maxim
If the person is closer to sitting, then by the maxim, he is legally considered still sitting. Therefore, he should sit back down, recite tashahhud, and complete the prayer without any extra prostration.
The ruling of sitting applies to the state that is close to sitting.
5
Conclude the ruling
No sajdah al-sahw is required because in the ruling of the law, he never actually stood up. If he were closer to standing, he would be considered standing and would not return, and sajdah al-sahw would be necessary.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إِنَّ مَا يَقْرُبُ مِنَ الشَّيْءِ يَأْخُذُ حُكْمَهُ. ترجمہ: جو کسی شئی سے قریب ہوتا ہے تو وہ بھی اسی کا حکم لے لیتا ہے۔ تشریح: مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ شی اور قرب ھی کا حکم ایک ہوتا ہے ، یعنی جو چیز کسی چیز کے قریب ہو تو اس بھی مقرب کا وہی حکم ہوتا ہے جو مقرب منہ کا ہوتا ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول کو ذکر کرنے کے بعد اس بات کو ثابت کر رہے ہیں کہ اگر مصلی بھولے سے قعدہ اولی سے کھڑا ہو گیا اب اگر وہ اقرب الی القعود ہو یعنی بیٹھنے کے زیادہ قریب ہوتو دوبارہ بیٹھ جائے اور قعدہ کرے اور تشہد پڑھے اور سلام پھیر دے، کیونکہ جب مصلی ایسی حالت پر تھا جو اقرب الی القعود تھی تو مذکورہ اصول کی بنیاد پر یہ قعود کے حکم میں ہو گا گویا کہ وہ کھڑا ہی نہیں ہوا، اس لئے اس پر سجدہ سہولا زم نہیں ہوگا۔
Indeed, what is close to a thing takes its ruling. Translation: Whatever is near to something also takes the same ruling. Explanation: The meaning of the mentioned principle is that a thing and its nearness share the same ruling. That is, whatever is close to something has the same ruling as that which it is close to. The author of al-Hidayah, after mentioning this principle, is proving that if a person forgetfully stands up from the first sitting, and if he is closer to sitting (i.e., his body is still near the sitting position), then he should sit back down, recite the tashahhud, and conclude the prayer. Because when the person was in a state closer to sitting, based on the mentioned principle, it is considered as if he never stood up, and therefore sajdah al-sahw is not obligatory upon him.
Source pages p. 135

Commentary
This passage introduces a third maxim dealing with proximity and its legal effect. The passage type is a ruling with explanation and application. The maxim states that something close to a thing takes the same ruling as that thing. The author applies it to a common scenario in prayer: someone forgetfully stands up from the first sitting (qaidah ula) but then remembers. If at the moment of remembering, the person is physically closer to sitting than to standing—meaning he has not fully risen—he is still considered in the ruling of sitting. Therefore, he should sit back, recite tashahhud, and complete the prayer without the need for sajdah al-sahw, because he is legally treated as if he never stood up. This application shows how the maxim resolves a practical issue: the threshold of proximity determines the ruling.

Key Terms
اقرب الی القعود (aqrab ila al-qu'ud): The state of being closer to the sitting position than to standing; a physical state that determines the ruling of whether the person is considered sitting or standing.
قعدہ اولی (qaidah ula): The first sitting in a prayer of three or four rak'ahs, after the second rak'ah, during which tashahhud is recited.
سجدہ سہو (sajdah al-sahw): The prostration of forgetfulness performed to compensate for unintentional omissions or additions in prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person forgetfully begins to stand from the first sitting but remembers while his knees are still bent and his hands are on the ground (closer to sitting), what is the ruling?
A) He must continue standing and perform sajdah al-sahw later.
B) He should sit back immediately but must perform sajdah al-sahw.
C) He should sit back immediately, recite tashahhud, and no sajdah al-sahw is required.
D) His prayer is invalid and he must start over.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi maxim of proximity allows a forgetful worshipper who is closer to sitting to return to the first sitting without needing sajdah al-sahw, showing the school's consideration of physical reality in legal rulings.

Imam Muhammad on Forgetful Salam
States a ruling by Imam Muhammad about the effect of salam from forgetfulness

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state Imam Muhammad's ruling on the effect of a forgetful salam and distinguish it from the majority Hanafi position.

Core Idea
A forgetful salam does not exit the prayer according to Imam Muhammad.

This lesson examines a unique ruling by Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani regarding the effect of a forgetful salam (taslim) in prayer. While the majority of the Hanafi school, including Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, hold that any salam—even if done forgetfully—concludes the prayer, Imam Muhammad takes a different position. Understanding this intra-madhhab difference sharpens your appreciation of how the Hanafi school accommodates minority views.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the forgetful salam (taslim) performed by someone in prayer. According to Imam Muhammad, this salam does not remove the person from the prayer. Confirm the ruling: the person remains in prayer.
The ruling is specific to forgetful salam, not intentional salam.
2
Note the scholar attributing the view
This ruling is attributed to Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani (student of Abu Hanifa). Recognize that it is a minority view within the Hanafi school, not the relied-upon position.
Imam Muhammad's view is recorded in the Nawadir (rare transmissions).
3
Distinguish from the majority position
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (the Sahibayn) hold that salam, even if forgetful, exits the prayer. Compare: Imam Muhammad says no exit; the Sahibayn say exit occurs. The practical consequence differs for continuing the prayer.
The majority position is mufta bihi (relied upon for fatwa).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إِنَّ سَلَامَ مَنْ عَلَيْهِ السَّهُوَ لَا يُخْرِجُهُ عَنِ الصَّلَاةِ أَصْلًا عِنْدَ مُحَمَّدٍ.
Indeed, the salam of one upon whom there is forgetfulness does not remove him from the prayer at all according to Muhammad.
Source pages p. 135

Commentary
This is a brief ruling statement attributed to Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani (رحمه الله). The passage type is a ruling statement without proof. It addresses a specific issue: if a person forgetfully gives salam (taslim) at the end of prayer before completing it properly—such as after the first two rak'ahs mistakenly—according to Imam Muhammad, this salam does not take him out of the prayer at all. That is, the prayer is not considered concluded, and he remains in the state of prayer. This is a minority view within the Hanafi school; the other two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) hold that salam does exit the prayer if it is deliberate, but if forgetful, it may depend. However, the text here presents Muhammad's position as a distinct ruling. The practical effect: if one forgetfully says salam before completing the prayer, according to Muhammad, he is still in prayer, so he can continue without needing to repeat, but the details are not expanded here.

Key Terms
سلام (salam): The concluding salutation of prayer (taslim) that exits one from the prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The prayer is invalid and must be repeated.
B) The person exits the prayer and must perform sajdah al-sahw.
C) The person remains in the prayer and has not exited.
D) The prayer is valid and no further action is needed.

Key Takeaway
Imam Muhammad holds that a forgetful salam does not exit the prayer, contrary to the majority Hanafi position.

The Principle of Proximity: That Which is Close Takes its Ruling
States a legal maxim and applies it to forgetting the first sitting.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi legal maxim 'ma yaqrubu min al-shay'i yakhudh hukmahu' to the case of forgetting the first sitting and explain why no sujud as-sahw is required.

Core Idea
What is close shares the same ruling – a person closer to sitting is still considered sitting, so no prostration of forgetfulness is needed.

This lesson introduces a key legal maxim in Hanafi fiqh: that which is close to a thing takes its ruling. The passage from Al-Hidayah applies this principle to a specific scenario in prayer: forgetting the first sitting. Understanding this maxim allows you to derive rulings in similar cases involving proximity, whether in prayer or other acts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The person forgets the first sitting and stands up. At the moment he remembers, he is neither fully sitting nor fully standing.
The judgement depends on which state he is closer to.
2
Determine the proximity state
Assess whether he is closer to sitting (aqrab ila al-qu'ud) or closer to standing at the time of remembering.
This is a physical assessment based on posture.
3
Apply the maxim
If closer to sitting, the maxim 'ma yaqrubu...' deems him as still sitting, as if he never stood. If closer to standing, he is considered standing.
The maxim transfers the ruling of the nearer state.
4
Derive the ruling
If deemed sitting, he must return to the full sitting position, recite tashahhud, and conclude the prayer. If deemed standing, he continues and must perform sujud as-sahw.
No sujud is needed when returning from near-sitting.
5
Note the tarjih
Al-Hidayah declares the no-sujud ruling as sahih (correct), establishing it as the relied-upon position in the Hanafi school.
This is from a Zahir al-Riwayah text, giving it strong authority.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اقامت سے مقتدی پر بھی اقامت کا حکم لازم ہوتا ہے، یعنی اگر مسافر امام نے دورانِ نماز اقامت کی نیت کر لی اب امام پر دو کے بجائے چار رکعت لازم ہوئی ، تو اس امام کی نیت اقامت سے مقتدی بھی مقیم شمار ہوگا اور مقتدی کی بھی شائی نماز رباعی ہو جائے گی ،اگر چہ مقتدی نے اقامت کی نیت نہ کی ہو، کیونکہ مذکورہ اصول کی بنیاد پر مقتدی کے حق میں بھی سبب موجب ثابت ہوگا۔ (۱۲۰) إِنَّ مَا يَقْرُبُ مِنَ الشَّيْءِ يَأْخُذُ حُكْمَهُ. ترجمہ: جو کسی شئی سے قریب ہوتا ہے تو وہ بھی اسی کا حکم لے لیتا ہے۔ تشریح: مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ شی اور قرب ھی کا حکم ایک ہوتا ہے ، یعنی جو چیز کسی چیز کے قریب ہو تو اس بھی مقرب کا وہی حکم ہوتا ہے جو مقرب منہ کا ہوتا ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول کو ذکر کرنے کے بعد اس بات کو ثابت کر رہے ہیں کہ اگر مصلی بھولے سے قعدہ اولی سے کھڑا ہو گیا اب اگر وہ اقرب الی القعود ہو یعنی بیٹھنے کے زیادہ قریب ہوتو دوبارہ بیٹھ جائے اور قعدہ کرے اور تشہد پڑھے اور سلام پھیر دے، کیونکہ جب مصلی ایسی حالت پر تھا جو اقرب الی القعود تھی تو مذکورہ اصول کی بنیاد پر یہ قعود کے حکم میں ہو گا گویا کہ وہ کھڑا ہی نہیں ہوا، اس لئے اس پر سجدہ سہولا زم نہیں ہوگا۔ البناية كتاب الصلاة، باب سجود السهو ، ج ٢ ص ٦١٦ ، ط: دار الكتب العلمية الهداية: كتاب الصلاة، باب سجود السهو ، ج ا ص ٦٦ ا ، ۱۶۶، ط: رحمانیه (وَمَنْ سَهَا عَنِ الْقَعْدَةِ الْأُولَى ثُمَّ تَذَكَّرَ وَهُوَ إِلَى الْقُعُودِ أَقْرَبُ عَادَ وَتَشَهَّدَ لِأَنَّ مَا يَقْرُبُ مِنَ الشَّيْءِ يَأْخُذُ حُكْمَهُ وَلَا يَسْجُدُ لِلسَّهْوِ هُوَ الصَّحِيحُ كَأَنَّهُ لَمْ يَقُمُ.
From the iqamah, the ruling of iqamah also becomes binding on the follower. That is, if the traveling imam intends iqamah during the prayer, four rak'ahs become obligatory upon him instead of two, and due to the imam's intention of iqamah, the follower also becomes a resident and his prayer becomes four rak'ahs, even if the follower did not intend iqamah, because based on the aforementioned principle, the cause is established for the follower as well. (120) Indeed, that which is close to a thing takes its ruling. Translation: Something that is close to a thing takes its ruling. Explanation: The meaning of the aforementioned principle is that the thing and the close one share the same ruling, meaning when something is close to something else, it has the same ruling as that to which it is close. The author of Hidayah, after mentioning the aforementioned principle, is proving that if a person erroneously stands up from the first sitting, and if he is closer to sitting, then he should sit back down, perform the sitting, recite the tashahhud, and say the salam, because when he was in a state closer to sitting, based on the aforementioned principle, he is considered as if he is sitting, so he did not stand. Therefore, he does not have to perform the prostration of forgetfulness. Al-Binayah: Book of Prayer, Chapter of Sajdah Sahw, vol. 2, p. 616, Dar al-Kutub al-Ilmiyya. Al-Hidayah: Book of Prayer, Chapter of Sajdah Sahw, vol. 1, p. 66a, 166, Rahmaniyya: (And whoever forgets the first sitting, then remembers while he is closer to sitting returns and recites tashahhud because that which is close to a thing takes its ruling, and he does not prostrate for forgetfulness. That is the correct view, as if he did not stand.)
Source pages p. 135

Commentary
This lesson presents a foundational legal principle (qa'idah) in Hanafi fiqh: 'That which is close to a thing takes its ruling.' The passage first applies this to a scenario of an imam who intends to settle (iqamah) during travel prayer—his intention makes his prayer full (4 rak'ahs), and the followers, even without intention, must follow because they are close to the imam. Then the author applies the principle to a case of forgetfulness: if a person stands up from the first sitting (qad'ah ula) and then remembers while he is still closer to sitting than to standing (i.e., he hasn't fully straightened up), the principle deems him as still sitting. Therefore, he sits back, recites tashahhud, and concludes the prayer without performing sujud as-sahw, since he never truly left the sitting state. The Hidayah quote confirms that this is the correct (sahih) position in the Hanafi school, contrasting with any view that would require prostration. This principle is a key tool for analogical reasoning (qiyas) in similar situations.

Key Terms
مَا يَقْرُبُ مِنَ الشَّيْءِ يَأْخُذُ حُكْمَهُ (ma yaqrubu min al-shay'i yakhudh hukmahu): A legal maxim: something close to another thing takes the same ruling as that thing.
اقرب الی القعود (aqrab ila al-qu'ud): State of being closer to sitting than standing, specifically while standing up from the first sitting.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the principle 'ما يقرب من الشيء يأخذ حكمه', what should a person do if he forgets the first sitting and remembers while he is closer to sitting?
A) He should continue standing and perform sujud as-sahw at the end.
B) He should sit back, recite tashahhud, and perform sujud as-sahw.
C) He should sit back, recite tashahhud, and give salam without sujud as-sahw.
D) He should ignore the forgetfulness and complete the prayer normally.

Key Takeaway
The proximity maxim ('ma yaqrubu...') allows a person who forgets the first sitting and is still closer to sitting to return without performing sujud as-sahw.

Salah — Prayer

The Suspended Salam: Imam Muhammad vs. Shaykhayn on Sajdah Sahw
Presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on the effect of salam when sajdah sahw is owed.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on the effect of salam when sajdah sahw is owed and apply the thamarah al-khilaf to the issues of iqtida' and nullification of wudu.

Core Idea
When sajdah sahw is owed, salam does not exit prayer at all (Muhammad) or exits in suspension (Shaykhayn).

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute with significant practical consequences. The central question: if a person says the final salam before performing sajdah sahw, are they still in prayer? Imam Muhammad holds that the salam does not exit the prayer at all, while the Shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) maintain that the salam exits the prayer in a suspended manner (tawaqquf), contingent on performing the sajdah. This difference affects the validity of following an imam after his salam and the nullification of wudu by laughter during this interval.

Guided Path
1
State the two Hanafi positions
Identify what each party (Imam Muhammad and the Shaykhayn) says about the effect of salam when sajdah sahw is owed.
Imam Muhammad: salam does not exit at all. Shaykhayn: salam exits in a suspended manner.
2
Identify the dalil for each position
Examine the reasoning behind each view. Muhammad: sajdah sahw is wajib to compensate for a deficiency, so it must be performed within the state of ihram of prayer; therefore, the salam cannot terminate the prayer. Shaykhayn: salam is a permissible act in itself, but its effect is suspended because of the need to perform the sajdah; once performed, the salam retroactively takes effect.
Both arguments are based on the nature of sajdah sahw as a compensatory act.
3
Understand the concept of tawaqquf
The Shaykhayn's view introduces a 'suspended' state: the salam takes the person out of prayer conditionally, pending the performance of sajdah sahw. If sajdah is performed, the person is deemed to have been out of prayer from the moment of salam; if not, he is considered to have remained in prayer.
This is a middle position between full exit and no exit.
4
Apply the thamarah al-khilaf
Identify the practical consequences: (1) validity of a follower joining the imam after the imam's salam but before sajdah sahw; (2) nullification of wudu by laughter during this interval; (3) change of obligation by intention of iqamah.
These applications show that the dispute is not merely theoretical.

مصلی پر سہو کے دو سجدے باقی تھے دوسرا شخص اس کے ساتھ نماز میں داخل ہو گیا تو اب اس شخص کی اقتداء درست ہوگی یا نہیں؟ تو شیخین کے نزدیک اگر امام نے سہو کا سجدہ کرلیا تو اقتداء درست ہوگی ورنہ نہیں ، جبکہ امام محمد رحمہ اللہ کے نزدیک مطلقاً اقتداء درست ہوگی چاہے امام سجدہ کرے یا نہ کرے، اور اس اختلاف کی بنیاد مذکورہ مختلف فیہ اصل ہے۔ الهداية: كتاب الصلاة، باب سجود السهو ، ج ۱ ص۱۶۷، ط: رحمانیہ (قَوْلُهُ وَفِى انْتِقَاضِ الطَّهَارَةِ بِالْقَهْقَهَةِ وَتَغْ الْفَرْضِ بَنِيَّةِ الْإِقَامَةِ فِي هَذِهِ الْحَالَةِ.
(121) Indeed, the salam of one upon whom is the prostration of forgetfulness does not exit him from the prayer at all according to Muhammad, and for the sake of establishing the cause that necessitates in the case of the original (it binds him, meaning it binds the follower) the ruling of iqamah by the imam's intention, meaning if the imam intends iqamah in the middle of his prayer, their obligatory prayer becomes four, even if there is no intention from the people. And according to the two shaykh (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), it exits him in a suspended manner. Translation: The salam of the person on whom sajdah sahw is obligatory: according to Imam Muhammad, this salam does not take him out of the prayer at all; according to the Shaykhayn, it takes him out in a suspended manner. Explanation: The meaning of the aforementioned principle is: if a person still owes sajdah sahw and he says salam before performing it, does this salam take him out of the prayer or not? According to Imam Muhammad, this salam does not take the person out of the prayer at all, meaning he is still in prayer. According to the Shaykhayn, this salam takes him out of prayer in a suspended manner, i.e., if he performs sajdah sahw, he will be considered to have re-entered prayer; otherwise, he is out of prayer. The author of Hidayah, after mentioning the aforementioned principle, is proving that if a person says salam while he still owes two prostrations for forgetfulness, and another person joins him in prayer, then is this following valid or not? According to the Shaykhayn, if the imam performs sajdah sahw, the following is valid; otherwise not. According to Imam Muhammad, however, the following is absolutely valid whether the imam performs the prostration or not. And this difference is based on the aforementioned disputed principle. Al-Hidayah: Book of Prayer, Chapter of Sajdah Sahw, vol. 1, p. 167, Rahmaniyya: (His saying: And if the forgetful person says salam and someone else follows him, then if he prostrates it is valid, otherwise not. Muhammad says it is valid whether the imam prostrates or not, because in his view, the salam of one upon whom is forgetfulness does not take him out of the prayer at all, because it (the prostration) was required as a compensatory act for deficiency, so he must be in the state of ihram of prayer. According to them (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), it takes him out in a suspended manner because the salam is a permissible act in itself; it only does not take effect due to his need to perform the prostration, so it does not appear without it. And there is no need to consider the return to prayer. And the difference appears in the validity of following, and in the nullification of purity by laughter, and in the change of the obligation by intention of iqamah in this state.)
Source pages p. 135

Commentary
This lesson addresses an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the effect of salam (the final greeting of prayer) when the person still owes sajdah as-sahw (prostration for forgetfulness). The dispute is between Imam Muhammad and the Shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf). According to Imam Muhammad, if one says salam before performing the obligatory sajdah sahw, the salam does NOT exit him from the prayer at all; he remains in the state of prayer. The reason is that sajdah sahw is a compensatory obligation that must be performed within the prayer, so the prayer state continues. According to the Shaykhayn, the salam does exit him from the prayer, but in a suspended manner (tawaqquf): if he later performs the sajdah, it is considered that he re-entered prayer, and his previous actions are valid; if he does not perform it, he is considered out of prayer and his prayer is incomplete. The practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) appears in two issues: (1) the validity of a follower joining the imam's prayer after the imam has said salam but before performing sajdah sahw – according to Muhammad, it is valid; according to the Shaykhayn, it is valid only if the imam subsequently performs the sajdah; (2) the nullification of ablution by loud laughter during prayer – if one laughs before performing sajdah sahw, the dispute affects whether the laughter occurred inside or outside prayer, thus impacting wudu. The text also mentions that this difference extends to the change of the obligatory prayer by the intention of iqamah. This passage highlights the sophistication of Hanafi legal reasoning, where a single principle generates multiple applied rulings.

Key Terms
سلام من عليه السهو (salamu man 'alayhi al-sahw): The salaam (final greeting of prayer) uttered by a person who still owes the obligatory prostration of forgetfulness.
التوقف (al-tawaqquf): A suspended state: the salam takes the person out of prayer conditionally, pending the performance of sajdah sahw.
الشيخين (ash-shaykhayn): The two senior Hanafi imams: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (in this context, sometimes also includes Muhammad? But here 'Shaykhayn' refers to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, as Muhammad is mentioned separately).
الثمرة الخلاف (al-thamarah al-khilaf): The practical consequence of a legal difference; the real-world ruling that changes based on which view is adopted.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Shaykhayn, what is the status of a follower who joins an imam after the imam's salam but before the imam performs sajdah sahw?
A) The follower's prayer is always valid.
B) The follower's prayer is never valid.
C) The follower's prayer is valid only if the imam later performs sajdah sahw.
D) The follower's prayer is valid only if the follower also intends to perform sajdah.

Key Takeaway
When sajdah sahw is owed, the salam's effect is disputed: Imam Muhammad says it does not exit prayer; the Shaykhayn say it exits in suspension, and this difference affects multiple practical rulings.

Intention Changing the Act's Nature Invalidates It
States a rule about intention (niyyah) invalidating an act if it changes its nature.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi maxim on intention that changes the prescribed nature, and apply it to determine the validity of acts of worship.

Core Idea
An intention altering the essential form of an act voids it.

Intention (niyyah) is the cornerstone of every act of worship in Hanafi fiqh. But what happens when your intention fundamentally changes what you are supposed to be doing? This lesson unpacks a crisp maxim that draws a clear line: if your intention transforms the prescribed act, the act becomes invalid. We'll explore what 'changing the nature' means and why it matters for your prayer, fasting, and other devotions.

Guided Path
1
Memorize the maxim
Commit the Arabic text to memory: إِنَّ النِّيَّةَ إِنْ كَانَتْ مُغَيِّرَةً لِلْمَشْرُوع تَلْغُو. This is your anchor for the lesson.
2
Define the key terms
Break down the maxim: niyyah (intention), mugheyyira (changing), lil-mashru' (the prescribed act), telgheu (invalid). Understand that 'changing' means altering the essential legal character of the act.
E.g., changing a fard prayer into a nafl is a change; mere distraction is not.
3
Apply the maxim to a scenario
Consider a person who starts the zuhr prayer (fard) but mid-prayer decides to make it a voluntary prayer. Apply the maxim: the intention changes the prescribed nature, so the prayer becomes invalid.
4
Distinguish from harmless thoughts
The maxim does not cover momentary thoughts that do not alter the act's nature. For example, thinking about daily matters during salah does not constitute a 'changing intention'.
Only deliberate resolve to alter the act's legal identity triggers invalidity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۱۲۲) إِنَّ النِّيَّةَ إِنْ كَانَتْ مُغَيِّرَةً لِلْمَشْرُوع تَلْغُو.
(122) Indeed, the intention (niyyah) if it changes the prescribed (act) is invalid.
Source pages p. 136

Commentary
This is a concise legal maxim in Hanafi fiqh regarding the role of intention (niyyah) in acts of worship. It states that if a person's intention changes the fundamental nature of a prescribed act, that intention renders the act invalid (laghw). For example, if during prayer one intends to break the prayer or to change it to a different type, the prayer becomes invalid. Similarly, if one intends something contrary to the prescribed form, such as intending to make a voluntary prayer obligatory, the intention nullifies the act. The maxim is derived from the principle that acts of worship are tied to specific intentions, and altering that intention disrupts the act's legal validity. This principle is used in various chapters of fiqh, especially in salah and fasting.

Key Terms
نية (niyyah): Intention, the mental resolve to perform a specific act of worship for the sake of Allah.
مغيرة للمشروع (mugheyyiratun lil-mashru'): An intention that changes the prescribed form or nature of the act of worship, such as intending to cut short an obligatory prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the principle 'إن النية إن كانت مغيرة للمشروع تلغو', what happens if during an obligatory prayer, one intends to make it a voluntary prayer?
A) The prayer automatically becomes voluntary.
B) The prayer becomes invalid and must be restarted.
C) The prayer continues as obligatory despite the intention.
D) The intention has no effect on the prayer.

Key Takeaway
An intention that fundamentally alters the prescribed nature of an act of worship renders that act invalid.

The Suspended Exit: Salam When Sahw Sajdah Is Due
Intra-Hanafi dispute on salam and sahw sajdah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on whether salam exits prayer when sahw sajdah is due, and apply the dispute to the case of a follower joining the imam.

Core Idea
When sahw sajdah is due, salam exits prayer only suspended — effect depends on performing the sajdah.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute about the effect of the final salam when the worshipper still owes the sahw sajdah. Imam Muhammad holds that salam does not exit the prayer at all; the Shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) hold that it exits in a suspended manner. This seemingly theoretical difference has real consequences for the validity of following an imam, nullification of wudu by laughter, and changing the fard by intention. We will work through the reasoning of each view and trace its practical impact.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed issue
The core question: When a worshipper gives salam but has not yet performed the obligatory sahw sajdah, does the salam end the prayer or not? Determine the two positions within the Hanafi school.
The dispute is between Imam Muhammad and the Shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf).
2
Analyze Imam Muhammad's position
Imam Muhammad argues that the salam does not exit the worshipper at all. His reasoning: the prayer remains incomplete because the sahw sajdah is wajib as a compensation for deficiency, so the state of ihram must continue until the sajdah is performed.
Thus, according to Muhammad, the worshipper is still in prayer even after salam.
3
Analyze the Shaykhayn's position
The Shaykhayn hold that the salam exits the prayer in a suspended manner (tawaqquf). The salam is a permissible act in itself, but its effect is conditional on the subsequent performance of sajdah. If sajdah is done, the exit is voided as if the worship continued; if not, the exit stands.
Key concept: tawaqquf (suspension) — the ruling is provisional.
4
Apply to the case of following the imam
The Hidayah text presents a practical application: A person gives salam while sahw sajdah is due, and another person intends to follow him as imam. According to the Shaykhayn, the following is valid only if the imam subsequently performs sajdah; according to Muhammad, it is valid regardless.
The difference in principle directly affects whether the follower's prayer is valid.
5
Identify other affected rulings
The passage notes that the same dispute extends to two other cases: nullification of wudu by laughter during this state, and changing the fard by intention of iqamah. Reflect on how each position would rule in those scenarios.
This shows the systematic nature of Hanafi fiqh — a single principle governs multiple branches.
