وعند الشيخين يخرجه على سبيل التوقف . ترجمہ: اس آدمی کا سلام پھیرنا جس پر سجدہ سہو واجب ہو تو امام محمد کے نزدیک یہ سلام اس کو نماز سے بالکل نہیں نکالتا اور شیخین کے نزدیک توقف کے طور پر نکالتا ہے۔ تشریح : مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ اگر ایک آدمی پر سجدہ سہو باقی تھا ابھی تک اس نے سجدہ سہو نہیں کیا تھا کہ سلام پھیر دیا، اب یہ سلام پھیرنا اس آدمی کو نماز سے نکال دیتا ہے یا نہیں؟ تو امام محمد رحمہ اللہ کے نزدیک یہ سلام بالکل مصلی کو نماز سے نہیں نکالتا، گویا کہ وہ اب بھی نماز میں ہے، جبکہ شیخین کے نزدیک یہ سلام موقوفا اس کو نکالتا ہے، یعنی اگر سجدہ سہو کرے تو یہ داخل فی الصلاۃ شمار ہو گا ورنہ خارج عن الصلاۃ ہوگا۔ صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول کو ذکر کرنے کے بعد اس بات کو ثابت کر رہے ہیں کہ ایک آدمی نے سلام پھیر دیا جبکہ اس مصلی پر سہو کے دو سجدے باقی تھے دوسرا شخص اس کے ساتھ نماز میں داخل ہو گیا تو اب اس شخص کی اقتداء درست ہوگی یا نہیں؟ تو شیخین کے نزدیک اگر امام نے سہو کا سجدہ کرلیا تو اقتداء درست ہوگی ورنہ نہیں ، جبکہ امام محمد رحمہ اللہ کے نزدیک مطلقاً اقتداء درست ہوگی چاہے امام سجدہ کرے یا نہ کرے، اور اس اختلاف کی بنیاد مذکورہ مختلف فیہ اصل ہے۔ 
الهداية: كتاب الصلاة، باب سجود السهو ، ج ۱ ص۱۶۷، ط: رحمانیہ (قَوْلُهُ وَلَوْ سَلَّمَ السَّاهِي فَاقْتَدَى بِهِ غَيْرُهُ فَإِنْ سَجَدَ صَحْ وَإِلَّا لَا قَالَ مُحَمَّدٌ هُوَ صَحِيحٌ سَجَدَ الْإِمَامُ أَو لَمْ يَسْجُدُ لِأَنَّ عِنْدَهُ سَلَامَ مَنْ عَلَيْهِ السَّهُوَ لَا يُخْرِجُهُ عَنْ الصَّلَاةِ أَصْلًا لِأَنَّهَا وَجَبَتْ جَبْرًا لِلتَّقْصَانِ فَلَا بُدَّ أَنْ يَكُونَ فِي إِحْرَامِ الصَّلَاةِ وَعِنْدَهُمَا يُخْرِجُهُ عَلَى سَبِيلِ التَّوَقُفِ لِأَنَّهُ مُحَلَّلٌ فِي نَفْسِهِ وَإِنَّمَا لَا يَعْمَلُ لِحَاجَتِهِ إِلَى أَذَاءِ السَّجُدَةِ فَلَا تَظْهَرُ دُونَهَا وَلَا حَاجَةَ عَلَى اعْتِبَارِ عَندَمِ الْعَوْدِ وَيَظْهَرُ الاخْتِلَافُ فِي صِحَّةِ الاقْتِدَاءِ وَفِى انْتِقَاضِ الطَّهَارَةِ بِالْقَهْقَهَةِ وَتَغْ الْفَرْضِ بَنِيَّةِ الْإِقَامَةِ فِي هَذِهِ الْحَالَةِ.
البحر الرائق: كتاب الصلاة، باب سجود السهو ج ۲ ص ۱۱۵، ط: دار الكتاب الإسلامي
And according to the two shaykhs, he exits it in the manner of suspension. Translation: The salam of the person upon whom sahw sajdah is obligatory: according to Imam Muhammad, this salam does not take him out of prayer at all, and according to the two shaykhs, it takes him out with suspension. Explanation: The meaning of the mentioned principle is that if a person still had sahw sajdah remaining and he had not yet performed it when he gave salam, does this salam take him out of prayer or not? According to Imam Muhammad, this salam does not take the worshipper out of prayer at all, as if he is still in prayer, while according to the two shaykhs, this salam takes him out in a suspended manner, meaning if he performs sahw sajdah, then it will be considered entering into prayer, otherwise it will be exiting prayer. The author of Hidayah, after mentioning the above principle, is proving that if a person gave salam while two sajdahs of sahw remained upon him, and another person entered the prayer with him, then according to the two shaykhs, if the imam performed the sahw sajdah, the following is valid, otherwise not, while according to Imam Muhammad, the following is valid absolutely whether the imam performs sajdah or not, and the basis of this difference is the aforementioned disputed principle. Al-Hidayah: Kitab al-Salah, Bab Sujud al-Sahw, vol.1 p.167, Rahmaniyyah ed. (His saying: And if the forgetful one gives salam and someone else follows him, then if he performed sajdah it is valid, otherwise no. Muhammad said it is valid whether the imam performed sajdah or not, because according to him, the salam of the one upon whom sahw is due does not take him out of prayer at all, because it (the prayer) is obligatory as a compensation for deficiency, so it must be in the state of ihram of prayer. According to them, it takes him out in the manner of suspension because it (the salam) is a permissible act in itself, but it does not take effect due to his need to perform sajdah, so it does not appear without it, and there is no need to consider the return. And the difference appears in the validity of following, and in the nullification of wudu by laughter, and in changing the fard by the intention of iqamah in this situation.) Al-Bahr al-Raiq: Kitab al-Salah, Bab Sujud al-Sahw, vol.2 p.115, Dar al-Kitab al-Islami.
Source pages p. 136

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the effect of salam (salutation) when sahw sajdah (prostration of forgetfulness) is due but not yet performed. Imam Muhammad holds that the salam does not exit the worshipper from prayer at all; the prayer remains validly in progress. Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (the Shaykhayn) hold that the salam exits the prayer in a suspended manner (tawaqquf): if sajdah is performed, the exit is voided and the worshipper is considered to have re-entered prayer; if not, he is considered to have exited. This difference is then applied to the case of a follower joining the imam who has given salam but not yet performed sahw sajdah. According to the Shaykhayn, the following is valid only if the imam subsequently performs sajdah; according to Muhammad, it is valid in any case. The passage also notes that this dispute extends to other rulings, such as nullification of wudu by laughter during this state and changing the fard by intention of iqamah. The textual support from Al-Hidayah and Al-Bahr al-Raiq is cited.

Key Terms
سجدہ سہو (sujūd al-sahw): Prostration of forgetfulness, two sajdahs performed to compensate for errors during prayer.
سلام (salām): The final salutation (assalamu alaykum) that traditionally ends the prayer.
توقف (tawaqquf): Suspension; the effect of salam is conditional on subsequent performance of sajdah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Shaykhayn, what is the status of a worshipper who gave salam while sahw sajdah was due but then never performs the sajdah?
A) He is still in prayer.
B) He exited prayer with a suspended exit; since sajdah is not performed, the exit becomes final.
C) His prayer is invalid and must be repeated.
D) He is out of prayer but must perform sajdah later.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, when sahw sajdah is due, the effect of salam is disputed: Imam Muhammad says it does not exit, while the Shaykhayn say it exits in a suspended manner, affecting many related rulings.

Intention to Change the Legislated Act is Void
Principle with application to sahw sajdah case.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi principle that an intention to alter a legislated act is void and apply it to cases involving required external actions (arkan) versus inner convictions.

Core Idea
Mere intention cannot override a required external act when the act's pillar is physical.

This lesson examines a foundational Hanafi principle: if a worshipper intends to change a legally prescribed act (mashru'), that intention is legally ineffective. The author of Hidayah applies this to a scenario where a person gives salam while sahw sajdah is due and intends to exit prayer. Despite his intention, the prayer continues until the sajdah is performed. This illustrates that intention alone cannot alter a ruling that depends on external actions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the principle and its statement
Locate the phrase 'إن النية إن كانت مغيرة للمشروع تلغو' and note that it is a general rule. Understand that 'مغير' means changing or altering.
2
Examine the application to salah
Read the passage describing the worshipper who has sahw sajdah due, gives salam, and intends to end the prayer. See that the author argues the salam does not terminate the prayer because the sajdah is still obligatory.
This builds on the previous lesson's ruling that salam before sahw sajdah is not a valid exit.
3
Understand the reasoning based on pillar (rukn)
The author explains that intention alone (niyyah mujarradah) cannot nullify a required action when the pillar of that action is external (amal al-jawarih). Here, sajdah is an action of the limbs, so intention cannot override it.
4
Analyze the counterexample: intention of disbelief
The passage contrasts with niyyat al-kufr, which does nullify iman because the pillar of iman is inner belief (amal al-batin). This distinction shows the principle's limits.
The counterexample strengthens the rule by clarifying where intention alone is effective.
5
Apply the principle to other scenarios
Generalize: whenever a legal act requires a physical pillar (e.g., salah, fasting, hajj), an intention to change or cancel it without performing the required action is void.
This principle applies broadly in Hanafi fiqh, especially in ibadat.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۱۲۲) إِنَّ النِّيَّةَ إِنْ كَانَتْ مُغَيِّرَةً لِلْمَشْرُوع تَلْغُو. ترجمہ: اگر نیت مشروع کو تبدیل کرنے والی ہو تو وہ نیت لغو ہو جائے گی ۔ تشریح : مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ ایسی نیت کرنا جو مشروع کو تبدیل کرنے والی ہو تو وہ نیت خود لغو ہو جائے گی اور مشروع تبدیل نہیں ہو گا بلکہ مشروع ہی رہے گا۔ صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے اس بات کو ثابت کر رہے ہیں کہ اگر مصلی پر سجدہ سہو باقی تھا کہ اس نے سلام پھیر دیا اور اس سلام سے نماز کے ختم کا ارادہ بھی کیا تو ابھی اس مصلی پر سجدہ سہو کرنا ضروری ہے اگر چہ سلام پھیر لیا ہو، اس لئے کہ یہ سلام نماز کوختم کرنے والا نہیں ہے اور اس نے مشروع کو تبدیل کرنے کی جو نیت کی تھی وہ نیت بھی لغو ہو جائے گی اور اس نیت سے مشروع تبدیل نہیں ہوگا، کیونکہ امر مشروع کی تغییر بندے کے اختیار میں نہیں ہے۔ قَوْلُهُ لِأَنَّ هَذَا السَّلَامَ غَيْرُ فَاطِعِ) لِأَنَّهُ فِي مَحَلِّهِ بَعْدَ الْقَعْدَةِ فَهُوَ مُحَلَّلٌ مِنْهُ، وَنِيَّتُهُ تَغْيِيرُ الْمَشْرُوعِ وَهُوَ الْقَطْعُ لِيُرَتِّبَ عَلَيْهِ تَرُكَ السُّجُودِ، وَالنّيَّةُ الْمُجَرَّدَةُ عَنْ الْعَمَلِ غَيْرِ الْمُسْتَحَقِّ عَلَيْهِ لَا يُؤَكِّرُ إِبْطَالُ مَا رُكْتُهُ أَعْمَالُ الْجَوَارِحِ وَهُوَ السُّجُودُ فَلَغَتْ بِخِلَافِ نِيَّةِ الْكُفْرِ فَإِنَّهَا تُؤْثِرُ إِبْطَالَ الْإِيمَانِ وَالْعِيَادُ بِاللَّهِ تَعَالَى لِأَنَّ رُكْنَهُ عَمَلُ الْبَاطِنِ فَقَطْ عِنْدَ الْمُحَقِّقِينَ، وَالْإِقْرَارُ إِنَّمَا هُوَ شَرْطُ إِجْرَاءِ الْأَحْكَامِ وَهُوَ فَرْضٌ فِيهِ. فتح القدير: كتاب الصلاة، باب سجود السهو ، ج ا ص ۵۱۶، ط: دار الفکر
(122) Indeed, the intention, if it is changing of the legislated [act], is void. Translation: If the intention is one that changes the legislated act, then that intention becomes void. Explanation: The meaning of the mentioned principle is that making an intention that changes the legislated act, that intention itself becomes void, and the legislated act will not change but will remain as legislated. The author of Hidayah, after mentioning this principle, is proving that if a worshipper still had sahw sajdah remaining and he gave salam and also intended to end the prayer with this salam, then performing sahw sajdah is still obligatory upon him, even if he has given salam, because this salam is not one that ends the prayer, and the intention he made to change the legislated act will also become void, and the legislated act will not change by this intention, because changing a prescribed matter is not within the servant's control. His saying: Because this salam is not cutting, because it is in its place after the sitting, so it is permissible from him, and his intention is to change the legislated act, which is cutting, to base upon it abandoning the sajdah, and the mere intention without the action not incumbent upon him does not effect the nullification of what his pillar is actions of the limbs, which is the sajdah, so it became void, contrary to the intention of disbelief, for it nullifies iman – and refuge is sought with Allah Almighty – because its pillar is only the inner action according to the verifiers, and the confession is only a condition for the implementation of rulings and it is a fard within it. Fath al-Qadir: Kitab al-Salah, Bab Sujud al-Sahw, vol.1 p.516, Dar al-Fikr.
Source pages p. 137

Commentary
This passage presents a fundamental principle in Hanafi fiqh: an intention that seeks to alter a legislated act (mashru) is void and does not change the act. The author uses the example of a worshipper who gives salam while sahw sajdah is due and intends to exit the prayer. Despite his intention, the salam does not actually end the prayer (as per the previous dispute), and his intention to change the legislated ruling is ineffective. The reason given is that the salam is not a true terminator (qati) in this context; it is only a permissible act (muhallal) that cannot override the obligation of sajdah. An intention alone, without the corresponding action (which is the sajdah, an action of the limbs), cannot nullify what is required. This is contrasted with the intention of disbelief (niyyat al-kufr), which does nullify iman because the pillar of iman is inner belief, not external action. Thus, the principle is applied: mere intention cannot change a ruling that depends on external actions. The source is Fath al-Qadir.

Key Terms
نیة (niyyah): Intention; here, the mental resolve to change a legally prescribed act.
مشروع (mashrū‘): The legislated act; what is prescribed by Shariah.
لغو (laghw): Void, ineffective; the intention has no legal effect.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is an intention to exit prayer by salam ineffective when sahw sajdah is due?
A) Because such an intention is sinful.
B) Because the salam itself is not a valid exit.
C) Because the intention is not accompanied by the required action (sajdah), and the pillar of salah is external action.
D) Because the worshipper must repeat the prayer.

Key Takeaway
An intention to change a legally prescribed act is void if the act's pillar is external (actions of limbs); intention alone suffices only when the pillar is internal (belief).

Intention to Change a Prescribed Act is Void Without Action
Explaining that a mere intention to alter a shariah ruling is ineffective

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi principle that a mere intention without corresponding action cannot change a prescribed act, and apply it to the case of sajda sahw.

Core Idea
Mere intention cannot override a prescribed shariah ruling.

This passage from al-Hidayah presents a fundamental Hanafi principle: a mere intention to alter a prescribed act (mashru') does not effect any legal change; the intention is void (laghw). The ruling is applied to sajda sahw: if a worshipper still owes sajda sahw but says salam intending to end the prayer, the salam does not terminate the prayer and sajda sahw remains wajib. The text contrasts this with the intention of kufr, which does invalidate iman because iman's pillar is internal (tasdiq bil qalb), not dependent on physical action.

Guided Path
1
State the Principle
Identify the general rule: 'النية المجردة عن العمل لا تؤثر' – a mere intention without the corresponding physical action does not affect the prescribed act.
The prescribed act (mashru') remains unchanged.
2
Apply to Sajda Sahw
Consider the scenario: a worshipper has sajda sahw due but says salam, intending to cut the prayer. Recognize that the salam is not effective because sajda sahw is still wajib. The intention to change the prescribed act (cutting the prayer) is void (laghw).
The act of prostration is a physical action that is still required.
3
Contrast with Intention of Kufr
Note that the text contrasts this with the intention of disbelief, which does invalidate iman. Understand why: the pillar of iman is internal (tasdiq bil qalb), so intention alone suffices to nullify it.
The declaration of faith is only a condition for legal rulings, not the essence of iman.
4
Extract the Rational Basis
The underlying 'illa (reason) is that external acts require physical action; intention alone cannot override them. Internal acts like iman are purely inward, so intention is effective.
This is a rational proof (dalil aqli) distinguishing between internal and external acts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمہ: اگر نیت مشروع کو تبدیل کرنے والی ہو تو وہ نیت لغو ہو جائے گی ۔

تشریح : مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ ایسی نیت کرنا جو مشروع کو تبدیل کرنے والی ہو تو وہ نیت خود لغو ہو جائے گی اور مشروع تبدیل نہیں ہو گا بلکہ مشروع ہی رہے گا۔ صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے اس بات کو ثابت کر رہے ہیں کہ اگر مصلی پر سجدہ سہو باقی تھا کہ اس نے سلام پھیر دیا اور اس سلام سے نماز کے ختم کا ارادہ بھی کیا تو ابھی اس مصلی پر سجدہ سہو کرنا ضروری ہے اگر چہ سلام پھیر لیا ہو، اس لئے کہ یہ سلام نماز کوختم کرنے والا نہیں ہے اور اس نے مشروع کو تبدیل کرنے کی جو نیت کی تھی وہ نیت بھی لغو ہو جائے گی اور اس نیت سے مشروع تبدیل نہیں ہوگا، کیونکہ امر مشروع کی تغییر بندے کے اختیار میں نہیں ہے۔

قَوْلُهُ لِأَنَّ هَذَا السَّلَامَ غَيْرُ فَاطِعٍ) لِأَنَّهُ فِي مَحَلِّهِ بَعْدَ الْقَعْدَةِ فَهُوَ مُحَلَّلٌ مِنْهُ، وَنِيَّتُهُ تَغْيِيرُ الْمَشْرُوعِ وَهُوَ الْقَطْعُ لِيُرَتِّبَ عَلَيْهِ تَرُكَ السُّجُودِ، وَالنّيَّةُ الْمُجَرَّدَةُ عَنْ الْعَمَلِ غَيْرِ الْمُسْتَحَقِّ عَلَيْهِ لَا يُؤَكِّرُ إِبْطَالُ مَا رُكْتُهُ أَعْمَالُ الْجَوَارِحِ وَهُوَ السُّجُودُ فَلَغَتْ بِخِلَافِ نِيَّةِ الْكُفْرِ فَإِنَّهَا تُؤْثِرُ إِبْطَالَ الْإِيمَانِ وَالْعِيَادُ بِاللَّهِ تَعَالَى لِأَنَّ رُكْنَهُ عَمَلُ الْبَاطِنِ فَقَطْ عِنْدَ الْمُحَقِّقِينَ، وَالْإِقْرَارُ إِنَّمَا هُوَ شَرْطُ إِجْرَاءِ الْأَحْكَامِ وَهُوَ فَرْضٌ فِيهِ.

فتح القدير: كتاب الصلاة، باب سجود السهو ، ج ا ص ۵۱۶، ط: دار الفکر
Translation: If the intention is such that it would change the prescribed act, then that intention becomes void. Explanation: The meaning of the aforementioned principle is that intending something that would change the prescribed act renders the intention itself void, and the prescribed act does not change but remains as prescribed. The author of al-Hidayah mentions this principle to prove that if the worshipper still owed sajda sahw and he said salam, intending thereby to end the prayer, then sajda sahw is still obligatory upon him even if he has said salam. This is because this salam is not effective to end the prayer, and his intention to change the prescribed act (the termination of prayer) is also void, and the prescribed act does not change because changing what is prescribed is not within the servant's control. His saying: 'Because this salam is not a cutter' because it is in its place after the sitting, so it is a permissible act from him, and his intention to change the prescribed (which is cutting) in order to base upon it the abandonment of the prostration, and the mere intention without the action that is not due upon him does not effect the invalidation of what he has performed of the actions of the limbs, which is the prostration, so it becomes void. Contrary to the intention of disbelief, for it does effect the invalidation of faith, and refuge is sought with Allah the Exalted, because its pillar is only internal action according to the investigators, and the declaration is only a condition for the application of rulings, and it is an obligation in it.
Source pages p. 137

Commentary
This passage presents a Hanafi ruling regarding the effect of intention on a prescribed act (mashru'). The principle is that a mere intention to change a prescribed act does not actually change it; the intention is rendered void (laghw). The application is to a case of sajda al-sahw: if a worshipper has sajda sahw remaining but says salam, intending thereby to end the prayer, the salam does not actually terminate the prayer because the sajda is still due. Consequently, the worshipper must still perform the sajda sahw. The intention to change the prescribed act (cutting the prayer) is ineffective because it is not accompanied by the corresponding physical action. The text contrasts this with the intention of kufr, which does invalidate iman, because the pillar of iman is internal (tasdiq bil qalb), and the verbal declaration is only a condition for legal rulings. Thus, intention alone can affect internal matters but not external acts where physical actions are required.

Key Terms
نیت (niyyah): Intention; here specifically the intention to change a prescribed act.
مشروع (mashru'): That which is prescribed by shariah; the legally required act.
لغو (laghw): Void, ineffective; the intention has no legal effect.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the effect of a worshipper's intention to end the prayer by saying salam while sajda sahw is still due?
A) The prayer ends and sajda sahw is waived.
B) The prayer does not end and sajda sahw must still be performed.
C) The intention itself is sinful but the prayer is valid.
D) The prayer ends but sajda sahw must be made up later.

Key Takeaway
A mere intention without corresponding action cannot alter a prescribed shariah ruling; the intention is legally void.

Obedience According to Capacity: The Sick Person's Prayer
Principle and its application to sick prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the principle 'al-ta'atu bihasab al-taqah' and apply it to determine the manner of prayer (standing, sitting, or gesturing) for a sick person based on their ability.

Core Idea
Obedience is according to capacity: the obligation of prayer remains, but the manner is eased to match the worshipper's ability.

This lesson introduces a fundamental Hanafi principle: al-ta'atu bihasab al-taqah (obedience according to capacity). Rooted in the Quranic verse 'Allah does not charge a soul except [with that within] its capacity' (2:286), this principle governs how obligations are fulfilled when one faces genuine inability. The classical Hanafi text al-Hidayah applies this to the prayer of the sick, showing that while the obligation of prayer remains, its postural requirements (standing, bowing, prostrating) are relaxed according to what the person can manage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the principle and its textual basis
Locate the principle 'al-ta'atu bihasab al-taqah' in the passage and note its proof from Quran 2:286, which is cited in the Hanafi position.
This is a foundational maxim (qa'ida fiqhiyya) that appears across fiqh.
2
Understand the meaning of 'taklif ma la yutaq'
Understand why imposing an obligation beyond capacity is invalid. The passage explicitly states that 'taklif ma la yutaq' is not permissible.
This is a key Hanafi usul principle: obligations are limited to what is possible.
3
Apply to the sick person's prayer
Work through the three scenarios: if able to stand, standing is required; if unable, sit and perform ruku/sujud normally; if unable to do even that, gesture with head.
The progression follows from most to least able.
4
Confirm the ruling remains fard
Note that the obligation (fard) of prayer does not drop; only the manner of performance is adjusted. This is consistent with the principle.
The ruling_anatomy block below shows the hukm level is fard 'ayn.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب صلاة المريض

(۱۲۳) إِنَّ الطَّاعَةَ بِحَسَب الطَّاقَةِ.

ترجمہ: اطاعت کرنا طاقت کے مطابق ہے۔

تشریح : مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ انسان پر اطاعت کرنا اور شریعت کے احکام کی بجا آوری کرنا یہ انسان کی طاقت کے بقدر ہے، جو طاقت سے ماوراء ہے اس کا انسان مکلف نہیں ہے، کیونکہ تکلیف مالا يطاق جائز نہیں ہے۔
صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول کو ذکر کر کے اس بات کو بتلا رہے ہیں کہ اگر مریض نماز میں قیام سے عاجز ہو جائے ، کھڑے ہونے پر قادر نہ ہو تو بیٹھ کر نماز پڑھے اور رکوع اور سجدہ کرے، اور اگر رکوع اور سجدہ کرنے کی بھی قدرت نہیں رکھتا تو پھر رکوع اور سجدہ اشارے سے کرے۔ وجہ یہ ہے کہ جب آدمی کھڑے ہونے پر قادر نہیں ہے اور اگر اس کے لئے قیام کو ضروری قرار دیں تو یہ تکلیف مالا يطاق ہے اور یہ جائز نہیں ، کیونکہ اطاعت بقدر طاقت ہے، لہذا مذکورہ اصول کی بنیاد پر اس شخص کو بیٹھ کر نماز ادا کرنے کی اجازت ہے۔

الهداية كتاب الصلاة، باب صلاة المريض، ج ۱ ص ۱۶۸، ط: رحمانیہ (قَوْلُهُ وَمُومِيًا إِنْ تَعَذَّرَ) أَى يُصَلَّى مُومِيًا وَهُوَ قَاعِدٌ إِنْ تَعَدَّرَ الرُّكُوعُ وَالسُّجُودُ لِمَا قَدَّمُنَاهُ وَلانَّ الطَّاعَةَ بِحَسَب الطَّاقَةِ.
Chapter: Prayer of the Sick. (123) Indeed obedience is according to capacity. Translation: Obedience is according to strength. Explanation: The meaning of the aforementioned principle is that obedience and fulfilling the commands of shariah are according to one's capacity; what is beyond capacity is not obligated, because imposing an impossible obligation (taklif ma la yutaq) is not permissible. The author of al-Hidayah mentions this principle to explain that if a sick person is unable to stand in prayer, not able to stand, then he should pray sitting and perform ruku and sujud. If he has no ability to perform ruku and sujud, then he should gesture with his head for ruku and sujud. The reason is that when a person is not able to stand, if standing were made obligatory for him, it would be an impossible obligation, which is not permissible, because obedience is according to capacity. Therefore, based on this principle, such a person is permitted to pray sitting. al-Hidayah, Book of Prayer, Chapter on the Prayer of the Sick, vol. 1 p. 168, Rahmaniyyah edition: His saying: 'and gesturing if it is not possible' i.e., he should pray gesturing while sitting if ruku and sujud are not possible, due to what we have presented and because obedience is according to capacity.
Source pages p. 138

Commentary
This passage presents a key Hanafi principle: 'Obedience is according to capacity.' It is from the chapter on the prayer of the sick. The principle is used to justify the relaxation of postural requirements in prayer when one is genuinely unable. If a sick person cannot stand, he sits; if he cannot perform ruku and sujud normally, he gestures. The underlying reasoning is that imposing obligations beyond one's ability (taklif ma la yutaq) is not valid in Islam. The text cites the Hidayah to show that the Prophet's instruction to pray sitting if unable to stand is based on this principle.

Key Terms
طاعة (ta'ah): Obedience to Allah's commands.
طاقة (taqah): Capacity, ability.
تکلیف مالا يطاق (taklif ma la yutaq): Imposing an obligation beyond one's capacity, which is not permissible.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the principle 'obedience is according to capacity', what should a sick person do if he cannot stand for prayer?
A) He is exempt from the prayer altogether.
B) He should pray sitting and perform ruku and sujud as usual.
C) He should pray sitting and gesture for ruku and sujud if unable.
D) He should pray lying down only.

Key Takeaway
The obligation of prayer remains binding even when one is sick; only the manner of performance is relaxed according to the worshipper's capacity.

No Substitution of Ritual Acts by Personal Opinion
Stating that setting alternatives for worship by personal opinion is prohibited

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the principle that setting substitutes in worship by personal opinion is prohibited and apply it to the prayer of the sick and similar scenarios.

Core Idea
In worship, substitutes are fixed by shariah, not by human reasoning.

This lesson introduces a fundamental Hanafi maxim: you cannot invent your own alternatives for Islamic acts of worship. If you cannot perform an act, you must use the specific substitute that shariah itself provided, such as sitting and gesturing in prayer when ill. This principle preserves the integrity of divine commands.

Guided Path
1
Identify the principle
Read the Arabic maxim: إِنَّ نَصْبَ الْأبْدَالِ بِالرَّأي مُمْتَنِعٌ. Understand that it prohibits setting substitutes (abdal) for acts of worship based on personal opinion (ra'y).
2
Understand the scope
This applies to all acts of worship (ibadat). The substitute must be the one designated by shariah, such as gestures for bowing and prostrating in the prayer of the sick.
Example from al-Hidayah and al-Bahr al-Raiq, see source references.
3
Recognize the epistemological basis
Worship (ibadat) is tawqifi (revealed) and not subject to human modification. Raising personal opinion to the level of shariah in setting substitutes is prohibited (haram).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۱۲۴) إِنَّ نَصْبَ الْأبْدَالِ بِالرَّأي مُمْتَنِعٌ .

ترجمہ: رائے سے بدل مقرر کرناممنوع ہے۔

تشریح : مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ اپنی رائے سے کسی عبادت یا کسی رکن کا بدل مقرر کرنا جائز نہیں ہے، شریعت نے جس عبادت کا بدل یا جس رکن کا بدل مقرر کیا ہے وہی بدل رہے گا، اگر شریعت نے بدل مقرر نہیں کیا تو از خود اپنی رائے سے بدل مقرر کرنا ممنوع ہے۔

البحر الرائق: كتاب الصلاة، باب صلاة المريض، ج ۲ ص ۱۲۱، ط: دار الكتاب الإسلامي
الهداية كتاب الصلاة، باب صلاة المريض، ج ۱ ص ۱۶۹، ط: رحمانیہ
(124) Indeed setting alternatives by opinion is prohibited. Translation: Setting a substitute by opinion is prohibited. Explanation: The meaning of the aforementioned principle is that it is not permissible to set a substitute for any worship or pillar by one's own opinion. The substitute that shariah has prescribed for a worship or pillar will remain that substitute; if shariah has not prescribed a substitute, then setting a substitute by one's own opinion is prohibited.
Source pages p. 138

Commentary
This is a standalone legal maxim in the Hanafi school. It addresses the issue of substitutes (abdal) in worship. For example, in the prayer of the sick, when one cannot perform the normal postures, the shariah itself has prescribed the substitute: sitting and gesturing. One cannot invent a different substitute based on personal reasoning. This principle reinforces that the rules of worship are tawqifi (revealed and fixed) and not subject to human modification.

Key Terms
نصب الأبدال (nasb al-abdal): Setting substitutes (for acts of worship).
الرأي (al-ra'y): Personal opinion or reasoning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the principle 'setting substitutes by opinion is prohibited', what should a person do if he cannot perform a required act in prayer?
A) He can invent any alternative that makes sense to him.
B) He must follow the specific substitute prescribed by shariah.
C) He should not pray at all.
D) He should ask a scholar for a new ruling.

Key Takeaway
Substitutes in worship are divinely fixed; personal opinion cannot create new alternatives.
